ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 5-1. - Fire limits-Designated. 
    The fire limits in the city shall embrace and include the following territory in the city: 
(1)	Blocks numbered 30, 31, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10 and 11, all as shown by the map or plat of the city, as the plat is of record in the office of judge of probate of the county; also block 6 of the Gowan Addition to the city as the map or plat of the Gowan Addition is recorded in the office of the judge of probate in the county; also that area in the city which is bounded on the north by First Avenue South, on the east by Sixth Street, on the south by Second Avenue South if Second Avenue South was extended to the right-of-way of the Louisville and Nashville Railroad, and on the west by the Louisville and Nashville Railroad; also all of that area in the city which is bounded on the south by Fourth Avenue North, on the east by Seventh Street, and on the north by Chilton Avenue, as such avenue is shown by the W.M. Adams lots as the lots appear of record on page 6 of the map book 1 in the office of judge of probate of the county, and on the west by the Louisville and Nashville Railroad; also the south half of block A and block 29 which is an area bounded on the north by Oakdale Avenue as shown on the map or plat of the W.M. Adams lots in the probate office of the county, and bounded on the east by Sixth Street, on the south by Fourth Avenue, and on the west by Seventh Street, all of the area described in this subsection being east of the Louisville and Nashville Railroad as the railroad is now located through the city. 
(2)	All of the following area in the city, which is located west of the Louisville and Nashville Railroad as the railroad is now located in the city: lots numbered 1 and 4 in block 1; all of block 2 except lots numbered 1 and 4; also all that area in the city which is bounded on the north by Second Avenue, on the east by the Louisville and Nashville Railroad and on the south by First Avenue South, if First Avenue South was extended in a westerly direction across the Louisville and Nashville Railroad so as to intersect Ninth Street, if Ninth Street was extended in a southerly direction, and on the west by Ninth Street if Ninth Street was extended in a southerly direction so as to intersect First Avenue, if First Avenue South was extended in a westerly direction. 
(Code 1979, § 6-1) 
Sec. 5-2. - Same-Building regulations. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to erect or construct any building or structure within the fire limits designated in section 5-1 unless the building or structure is erected or constructed of brick, stone or concrete, or to cover any such building or structure, or to recover any building or structure, with any material other than slate or metal; provided that the city council may permit a structure of wood to be erected within the fire limits, such permission to be shown in the minutes of proceedings, provided that the structure of wood does not exceed six (6) feet in height from the ground and is covered with metal. 
(Code 1979, § 6-2) 
Secs. 5-3-5-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - BUILDING CODES 

Sec. 5-26. - Adoption; amendments. 
(a)	Adoption. The following codes are hereby adopted by reference as though they were copied fully in this section: 
2009 International Building Code (IBC). 
2009 International Residential Code (IRC). 
2009 International Mechanical Code (IMC). 
2008 National Electrical Code (NEC). 
2009 International Plumbing Code (IPC). 
2009 International Fuel Gas Code (IFGC). 
2009 International Fire Code (IFC). 
2009 International Property Maintenance Code (IPMC). 
2009 International Existing Building Code (IEBC). 
(b)	Amendments. The codes adopted in subsection 5-26(a) are amended as follows: 
AMENDMENT 1. General inserts and modifications. 
The following sections are hereby revised and/or modified: 
Section 101.1 in the following: 2009 International Fire Code, 2009 International Building Code (IBC), 2009 International Residential Code (IRC) (with respect to Section R101.1), 2009 International Mechanical Code (IMC), 2009 International Plumbing Code (IPC), 2009 International Fuel Gas Code (IFGC), 2009 International Property Maintenance Code (IPMC), and 2009 The International Existing Building Code (IEBC). 
Insert: CITY OF CLANTON. 
Section 103.1 in the following: 2009 International Building Code (IBC), 2009 International Residential Code (IRC) (with respect to Section 103.1), 2009 International Mechanical Code (IMC), 2009 International Plumbing Code (IPC), 2009 International Fuel Gas Code (IFGC), 2009 International Property Maintenance Code (IPMC), 2009 The International Existing Building Code (IEBC), will be changed from: the department of building safety, the department of plumbing inspection, the department of property maintenance inspection, the department of inspection, and the department of mechanical inspection, to: "The Building Department." 
Article 100 of the 2008 National Electrical Code (NEC) refers to an "Authority Having Jurisdiction." The Building Official or any of his/her designees, shall be included within the definition of an "Authority Having Jurisdiction." 
AMENDMENT 2. 
The 2009 International Building Code (including Section 113); the 2009 International Property Maintenance Code (including Section 111); the 2009 International Fire Code (including Section 108); the 2009 International Existing Building Code (including Section 112); the 2009 International Mechanical Code (including Section 109); the 2009 International Fuel Gas Code (including Section 109); the 2009 International Residential Code (including Section R112); and the 2009 International Plumbing Code (including Section 109) refer to a "board of appeals." All such references shall relate to the City of Clanton Code Enforcement Board of Appeals. The provisions in this Amendment 2 shall supersede any contradictory and irreconcilable provisions in the above-referenced codes, as the same relate to a board of appeals and the operation or decisions thereof. 
(a)	Establishment. There is hereby established the "City of Clanton Code Enforcement Board of Appeals" (referred to herein as the "Board"). The Board shall exercise the powers as set forth herein and in the respective codes adopted by the City and referenced in this Amendment 2. 
(b)	Membership of Board. The Board shall consist of five persons appointed by the City Council to serve for a term of three years, except that the City Council shall upon first appointing members to the Board modify the length of the initial terms so as to ensure the members serve staggered terms. Each new member shall serve for three years or until a successor has been appointed. No member of the Board may be an employee of the City. The Building Official, or his designee, shall be an ex officio member of said board but shall have no vote on any matter before the Board. The City Council shall appoint two alternate members who shall be called by the Board chairperson to hear appeals during the absence or disqualification of a member. Alternate members shall be appointed for three years, or until a successor has been appointed. The City Council may remove any member of the Board at any time in its sole discretion, and appoint another person to serve during his/her remaining term. Members of the Board shall not be compensated for their services as members of the Board. 
(c)	Rules and Procedures. The Board is authorized to establish policies and procedures necessary to carry out its purpose as set forth in the respective codes adopted by the City and referenced in this Amendment 2. The Board may adopt and make available to the public through the secretary procedures under which a hearing shall be conducted. The procedures will not require compliance with strict rules of evidence, but shall mandate that only relevant information be received. 
(d)	Chairperson. The Board shall annually select one of its members to serve as chairperson.
(e)	Disqualification. A member of the Board shall not hear an appeal in which that member has a personal, professional, or financial interest. 
(f)	Secretary. The chairperson shall designate a qualified clerk to serve as secretary to the Board. The secretary shall file a detailed record of all proceedings in the office of the Building Official. 
(g)	Meetings. The Board shall meet upon notice from the chairperson, within thirty (30) days of the filing of an appeal or at regular, periodic meetings as may be established by the Board. 
(h)	Postponement. Five members must be present to hear an appeal. When five members are not present to hear an appeal, the hearing shall be postponed. 
(i)	Appeal. An application for appeal of a notice of violation shall be filed on a form obtained from the building inspector within twenty (20) days after the notice of violation was served. 
(j)	Board decision. The Board shall modify or reverse the decision of the Building Official by a concurring vote of a majority of its members. The Building Official shall take immediate action in accordance with the decision of the Board. 
AMENDMENT 3. 
The International Residential Building Code, 2009 edition, Code Section R313, concerning Automatic Fire Sprinkler Systems, shall be deleted in its entirety. The deletion of this Section R313 shall supersede any contradictory and irreconcilable provisions in any code adopted as stated in Section 5-26 of the Code of Ordinances. 
AMENDMENT 4. 
Permit Fees. All references to fees shall mean the "City of Clanton - Schedule of Permit Fees". On new buildings, structures, alterations, additions, or modifications to existing buildings or structures, a permit fee shall be paid as required, in accordance with the schedule established in Section 5-26 of the Code of Clanton, Alabama. 
TOTAL VALUATION 
1.	Determining the Valuation of a Detached Single-Family Dwelling.
a.	The actual contract price or sum of contracts shall be used in determining the valuation of the detached single-family dwelling. 
b.	Exceptions. Provided that the minimum price of $65.00 per square foot of heated area plus $30.00 for all unheated areas, porches, balcony, garages, etc be used in determining the valuation of a single-family detached building. 
c.	All Buildings Excluding Single-Family Dwelling. All buildings, other than single-family detached, shall have their values taken from the actual contract price, Or the sum of contracts. 
d.	All valuations of $2000.00 (two thousand dollars) or less shall have a minimum fee of $20.00 (twenty dollars). 
2.	Penalties. Where work for which a permit is required by the 2009 International Building Code is started or proceeded prior to obtaining said permit, the fees herein specified shall be doubled, but the payment of such doubled fee shall not relieve any persons from fully complying with the requirements of the code in the execution of the work nor from any other penalties prescribed herein. 
(Code 1979, § 4-1; Ord. No. 1-83, § 1, 3-28-83; Ord. No. 12-91, § 1, 5-13-91; Ord. No. 14-97, § 1, 8-27-97; Ord. No. 2-02, 3-25-02; Ord. No. 5-03, § 1, 9-22-03; Ord. No. 6-03, § 1, 9-22-03; Ord. No. 8-10, § 1, 8-9-2010) 
Editor's note- 
Ord. No. 8-10, § 4, adopted Aug. 9, 2010, provides that nothing in this ordinance or in the residential code hereby adopted shall be construed to affect any suit or proceeding impending in any court, or any rights acquired, or liability incurred, or any cause or causes of action acquired or existing, under any act or ordinance hereby repealed as cited in section 2 of this ordinance; nor shall any just or legal right or remedy of any character to be lost, impaired or affected by this ordinance. 
Sec. 5-27. - Compliance. 
    No person shall construct, alter, change or amend any structure or building or any plumbing, gas or electrical lines, fixtures or appliances contrary to the codes enumerated and adopted in this article. 
(Code 1979, § 4-2) 
Sec. 5-28. - Enforcement. 
    Within the codes adopted in this article, when reference is made to the duties of certain officials named therein, that designated official in the city who has duties corresponding to those of the named official in the code shall be deemed to be the responsible official insofar as enforcing the provisions of the code is concerned. 
(Ord. No. 1-83, § 3, 3-28-83; Ord. No. 12-91, § 3, 5-13-91) 
Secs. 5-29-5-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - ELECTRICAL REGULATIONS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 5-51. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Electrician means any person having a regular place of business in his name who performs the work of installing, maintaining, altering or repairing, for hire, wires, electric signs, devices, conduits, apparatus, fixtures or other appliances for carrying or using electricity for light, heat or power purposes. 
    Person means any individual, firm, corporation, partnership, company, trustee, agency or association, and any agent, servant, employee or officer thereof, singular or plural. 
    Within the city refers to both the corporate limits and the police jurisdiction of the city. 
(Code 1979, § 4-6) 
Sec. 5-52. - Interpretation of article. 
    The provisions of this article shall not be construed to relieve any person from or to lessen the responsibility of any person owning, operating, controlling, installing or repairing any electrical wiring, apparatus, devices or equipment for damage or an injury to any person or property, nor shall it be construed to impose on the city any liability whatever by reason of the examinations provided for in this article or by reason of any certificate issued under this article. 
(Code 1979, § 4-7) 
Sec. 5-53. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person violating any provision of this article or doing or failing to do any act or thing prohibited by this article or declared by this article to be unlawful shall be guilty of an offense against the city and shall, upon conviction in any case, be punished as provided in section 1-9, and revocation of license may be imposed. 
(Code 1979, § 4-18) 
Sec. 5-54. - Electrical official-Authority generally. 
    The electrical official is hereby authorized, empowered and directed to regulate and determine the placing of electrical wires or other appliances for electric light, heat, or power in the city, and to cause such wires or appliances to be placed, constructed, guarded and maintained so as not to cause fires or accidents endangering life or property. 
(Code 1979, § 4-4) 
Cross reference- Administration, Ch. 2. 
Sec. 5-55. - Same-Powers and duties. 
(a)	The electrical official shall enforce the provisions of this article and he or his duly authorized representative may enter any structure or premises to perform any duty imposed upon him by this Code. 
(b)	The electrical official shall have the right, in the discharge of his duties, to enter, during reasonable hours, any building, manhole or subway, or to climb any pole, for the purpose of examining and testing the electrical appliances therein or thereon contained. For that purpose, he shall be given prompt access to all buildings, public and private, and to all manholes, subways or poles. Whenever an electric wire or appliance shall be defective through improper or insufficient insulation, or for any other reason, he shall at once cause the removal of such defect at the expense of the owner of such wires or appliances. 
(Code 1979, §§ 4-5, 4-9) 
Sec. 5-56. - Permit. 
(a)	Application for a permit to install, add to or repair electrical systems shall be made to the electrical official. The applicant shall furnish such information as may be required to complete the application form furnished by the electrical official. Any permit issued shall become invalid unless the work authorized by it shall have been commenced within six (6) months after its issuance, or if the work authorized by such permit is suspended or abandoned for a period of one (1) year after the work is commenced. 
(b)	No permit shall be valid until the fees prescribed shall have been paid. If any person commences any work on electrical installation before obtaining the necessary permit from the city, he shall be subject to the penalty prescribed in this article. 
(Code 1979, § 4-14) 
Sec. 5-57. - Fees. 
    The following are the fees to be charged in connection with electrical permits and inspections: 
For issuing permit$ 1.00For inspecting:Fixtures (lights, switches and outlets): 1 to 10  1.0011 to 20  2.0021 to 30   3.0031 to 40  4.0041 to 59  5.00All over 50 to be figured in proportionMotors:Up to 3 hp  2.00 4 hp to 10 hp  3.0011 hp to 20 hp  4.0020 hp and over   6.00Power box, each  1.00Loop, each  1.00Panel box, each  1.00Circuits, each  1.00Heat pump and unit1-story building  5.0011/2-story building  7.502-story building 10.00 
(Code 1979, § 4-15) 
Sec. 5-58. - Inspection. 
    Work regulated under this article must be inspected when roughed in. When this inspection has been completed, notification will be issued by the inspector to the supplier of current. If, for any reason, an installation does not pass these inspections, an additional inspection shall be made after the installation has been changed so as to conform to specifications. An inspection fee of two dollars ($2.00) will be charged for each additional inspection made, and a certificate of inspection will be issued for each approved installation. 
(Code 1979, § 4-16) 
Secs. 5-59-5-70. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Electrical contractors, Code of Ala. 1975, § 34-36-1 et seq. (Back)
Sec. 5-71. - Required. 
    No person shall, within the city or the police jurisdiction, work at or engage in the business of installing, maintaining, altering or repairing electric wires, conduits, apparatus, fixtures, electric or neon signs, or other appliances for carrying or using electricity for light, heat or power purposes unless such person has a license as provided by this division. 
(Code 1979, § 4-8) 
Sec. 5-72. - Exemption. 
    The provisions of this division requiring a license for working at or engaging in the business of installing, maintaining, altering or repairing electric wires, conduits, apparatus, fixtures or other appliances shall not apply to homeowners. Any individual may do such work upon his own premises, provided the work is done by himself and is used exclusively by him or his family, and when he demonstrates to the electrical inspector that he is qualified and receives from the electrical inspector a special permit to do such work and pays the fees provided for in section 5-57. 
(Code 1979, § 4-12) 
Sec. 5-73. - Application. 
    All applications for licenses under this division shall be made in writing to the electrical inspector. The applicant shall state in this application the name and age of the applicant and the experience of the applicant in performing electrical work. 
(Code 1979, § 4-10) 
Sec. 5-74. - Fee. 
    Each application for a license under this division shall be accompanied by a fee of five dollars ($5.00). An applicant who fails in his examination shall not have his fee returned to him, but shall be entitled to one (1) reexamination without payment of any additional fee. For each subsequent examination, he shall pay the regular fee of five dollars ($5.00). The five-dollar fee shall also accompany each application for a renewal certificate. All fees required to be paid under the provisions of this section shall be paid to the city clerk. 
(Code 1979, § 4-11) 
Sec. 5-75. - Bond. 
    No business license shall be issued to any person to engage in the business or trade of electrical construction and installation, or electrical contractor, unless such person shall have filed with the city clerk a bond approved by the city clerk, in the amount of five hundred dollars ($500.00), payable to the city. The bond shall be made by some suitable surety company duly authorized to do business in the state and the city, and shall be conditioned that such person will faithfully perform all work and will comply with and observe all ordinances, rules and regulations of the city regulating electrical work, will pay all license, permit and inspection fees accruing thereto, will save the city harmless from all loss, damage or injury resulting from any work done or any neglect or omission incident thereto by such person or his agents, servants or employees, or from improper material used therein, and will restore to like condition to that found any street, alley, sidewalk or other property and keep the property in good repair for one (1) year. 
(Code 1979, § 4-13) 
Sec. 5-76. - Correction of work; revocation. 
(a)	Any person engaged in the electrical business whose work does not conform to the applicable rules and regulations set out in this chapter or whose workmanship or materials are of inferior quality, shall, on notice from the electrical inspector, make necessary changes or corrections at once so as to conform to this Code. If the work has not been so changed after ten (10) days' notice from the electrical inspector, the electrical inspector shall then refuse to issue any more permits until such work has fully complied with the rules and regulations of this Code. The electrical inspector may appear before the governing authority and request that all licenses be revoked because of continuous violations. When the revocation of any such license is to be considered at any meeting, the person to whom the license has been issued shall have at least three (3) days' notice in writing of the time and place of such meeting, together with a statement of the grounds upon which it is proposed to revoke such license. 
(b)	All work must meet specifications and requirements of the electrical code adopted by the city. 
(Code 1979, § 4-17) 
Chapter 6 - ELECTIONS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, Ch. 2. (Back)
State Law reference- Municipal elections, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-46-1 et seq.; elections generally, Code of Ala. 1975, § 17-1-1 et seq. (Back)
Sec. 6-1. - Conduct. 
    General municipal elections held in the city shall be conducted pursuant to the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-46-2 and 11-46-20 et seq. 
(Code 1979, § 5-1) 
Sec. 6-2. - Election of mayor and council-Generally. 
    Pursuant to the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-2, the city council shall consist of a mayor and five (5) aldermen, who shall be elected from the city, by the qualified electors of the city, at general municipal elections to be held on the fourth Tuesday in August, and quadrennially thereafter. Such officers elected at such general municipal elections shall commence their term of office on the first Monday in October following their election and serve for four-year terms, or until their successors are lawfully chosen and installed in office. 
(Code 1979, § 5-2) 
Sec. 6-3. - Same-Establishment of wards. 
    The method of election of the members of the city council and the mayor shall be as follows: 
(1)	The city shall be divided into five (5) wards having as nearly as may be the same number of inhabitants. The wards shall be designated as ward number 1, ward number 2, ward number 3, ward number 4 and ward number 5. One (1) councilmember shall be elected from each ward and the mayor shall be elected from the city at large. 
(2)	The plan shall meet the constitutional requirement of one (1) man, one (1) vote.
(3)	The geographical boundaries of the wards shall be established so as to embrace one (1) minority ward which shall have a population of not less than sixty (60) percent of the minority race, and the minority community shall have an opportunity to be heard in the development of the plan. 
(Ord. No. 6-84, § I, 5-14-84) 
Sec. 6-4. - Same-Polling places. 
    The city establishes and adopts the following locations as the polling places for the election of the member of the city council for the ward or district where the polling place is located. The location of the polling places shall be by ward number and shall be as follows: 
(1)	Ward number 1: Clanton Airport, Clanton Avionics office, Airport Road.
(2)	Ward number 2: Clanton city park, facility building, Lay Dam Road.
(3)	Ward number 3: Old Clanton Elementary School, Fifth Avenue North.
(4)	Ward number 4: Veteran's club, Enterprise Road.
(5)	Ward number 5: Martin Funeral Home, back door, Fourth Avenue North at Thirteenth Street.
(Ord. No. 6-88, § I, 6-27-88) 
Sec. 6-5. - Qualification fees. 
(a)	A qualification fee in the amount of fifty dollars ($50.00) is hereby fixed and imposed upon all candidates seeking election as mayor of the city, except as hereinafter provided for. 
(b)	A qualification fee in the amount of fifty dollars ($50.00) is hereby fixed and imposed upon all candidates seeking election as councilmember of the city, except as hereinafter provided for. 
(c)	Such qualification fee shall be paid to the city clerk and deposited to the general fund of the city at or prior to the time of taking out qualification papers by any such candidates. 
(d)	Any person desiring to qualify who is not financially able to pay the required fee may qualify provided such prospective candidate furnishes the clerk with an affidavit stating that he is financially unable to pay the required fee fixed by this section. 
(e)	This section is adopted pursuant to Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-46-2 and shall be effective in all elections, both general and special, for aforesaid offices from and after the date of adoption. 
(Ord. No. 9-96, §§ 1-5, 6-10-96) 
Chapter 7 - FIRE PREVENTION AND PROTECTION 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, Ch. 2; buildings, Ch. 5; flood damage prevention, Ch. 8; housing, Ch. 9; licenses and business regulations, Ch. 10; motor vehicles and traffic, Ch. 11; offenses and miscellaneous provisions, Ch. 13; police, Ch. 16; solid waste, Ch. 17; utilities, Ch. 20; subdivisions, App. B; fire services in police jurisdiction, § 2-5; levy of tax for sale and storage of gasoline, § 10-110; fireworks, § 13-10 et seq.; public nuisances enumerated, § 13-63; abatement of fire and explosion hazards, App. A, § 9(12); general improvements in subdivisions, App. B, art. VI, § 1. (Back)
State Law reference- Firemen, rescue squad members, etc., rendering first aid or emergency care at scene of accident, etc., Code of Ala. 1975, § 6-5-332; volunteer firemen or rescue squad members entering burning buildings, etc., to preserve property, etc., Code of Ala. 1975, § 6-5-335; municipal fire regulations, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-59; fire department, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-140 et seq.; adoption of fire prevention code, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-8; water, sewer and fire protection authorities, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-88-1 et seq.; chief of fire department and chief of police as assistants to state fire marshal, Code of Ala. 1975, § 36-19-3; fire fighters' personnel standards and education commission, Code of Ala. 1975, § 36-32-1 et seq.; fireworks, Code of Ala. 1975, § 8-17-210 et seq.; license tax paid by dealers in fireworks, Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-12-102. (Back)
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 7-1. - Penalty for violation of chapter. 
    Any person who shall violate any provision of this chapter or any rule established by the chief of the fire department shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-9. 
(Code 1979, § 9-9) 
Sec. 7-2. - Fire department created; composition. 
    There is hereby created for the city a fire department to be composed of one (1) fire chief and as many firefighters as the mayor, chief of the fire department and members of the city council may deem necessary for the efficient handling of the department. 
(Code 1979, § 2-9) 
Cross reference- Administration, Ch. 2. 
Sec. 7-3. - Appointment and compensation of fire chief, firefighters. 
    The chief of the fire department and the members of the fire department shall be appointed by the mayor and members of the waterworks committee, and shall hold their office at the will of the city council. The compensation to be paid the chief of the fire department and members of the fire department shall be fixed by the city council from time to time as the needs of the city may require. 
(Code 1979, § 2-10) 
Cross reference- Administration, Ch. 2. 
Sec. 7-4. - Authority to make arrests. 
    The chief of the fire department and each member of the fire department shall have authority to make arrests for a violation, within his presence, of any of the rules or regulations set out in this chapter or any rules or regulations which may be promulgated and adopted by the chief of the fire department, and it shall be the duty of the chief of the fire department and each member of the fire department to arrest any person who violates any of such rules and regulations within his presence. 
(Code 1979, § 9-8) 
Cross reference- Police, Ch. 16. 
Sec. 7-5. - Unauthorized use of fire equipment. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person other than the chief of the fire department and the members of the fire department to use, remove or assist in using or removing any fire hose, ladder, reel or any part of the fire equipment of the city, unless directed to do so by the chief of the fire department or some member of the fire department. It shall be unlawful to use the fire equipment of the city for any purpose other than for fire drills and the extinguishing of fires. 
(Code 1979, § 9-3) 
Cross reference- Offenses and miscellaneous provisions, Ch. 13. 
Sec. 7-6. - Injuring fireplug, standpipe or manhole. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to drive any motor vehicle or other conveyance upon or against any fireplug, standpipe or manhole or to injure any fireplug, standpipe or manhole with any other instrument. 
(Code 1979, § 9-5) 
Sec. 7-7. - Interfering with fire-extinguishing activities. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to remove, handle or use any fire hose, reel, ladder or other parts of the fire equipment while being used in extinguishing a fire, or for any person to interfere with or fail to obey reasonable instructions or orders given by the chief of the fire department or any member of the fire department toward the efficient extinguishing of the fire or for the preserving of property or the preventing of injury to persons or property. 
(Code 1979, § 9-6) 
Sec. 7-8. - Danger zones at fires. 
    The chief of the fire department or other member of the fire department who may be acting as such shall have authority to establish a danger zone at each fire and it shall be unlawful for any person to go within the zone as established until the fire is fully extinguished and all objects of danger are removed and the premises within the zone are approved as safe for persons to go upon by the chief of the fire department or member acting as such. 
(Code 1979, § 9-7) 
Secs. 7-9-7-35. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - FIRE PREVENTION 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 7-36. - Fire prevention code adopted. 
    There is hereby adopted the Standard Fire Prevention Code, edition of 1991, recommended by the American Insurance Association, a copy of which is on file in the office of the city clerk, city hall building. 
(Code 1979, §§ 4-1, 6-7; Ord. No. 12-91, § 1, 5-13-91) 
Secs. 7-37-7-50. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - BURNING OF GARBAGE
