Every person hauling, transporting or conveying gasoline over any of the public streets or highways within the city or its police jurisdiction must, during the entire time he is so engaged, have in his possession an invoice or bill of sale or other recorded evidence showing the true name and address of the person from whom he has received the gasoline, the number of gallons so originally received by him from such person, the true name and address of every person to whom he has made deliveries of the gasoline or any part thereof, and the number of gallons so delivered to each of the persons. The person hauling, transporting or conveying such gasoline shall, at the request of any person authorized or required by law to inquire into or investigate such matters, produce and offer for inspection the invoice, bill of sale, or other recorded evidence. If the person fails or refuses to produce the invoice or bill of sale or other recorded evidence or if, when produced, it fails to clearly disclose the information, this shall be prima facie evidence of a violation of this subsection. 
(c)	Marking of vehicles. No person shall haul, transport or convey gasoline over any of the public streets or highways within the city or its police jurisdiction except in vehicles plainly and visibly marked on each side and on the rear thereof with the word "gasoline" or other name of the motor fuel being transported, in letters at least four (4) inches high and of corresponding appropriate width, together with the name and address of the owner of the vehicle in which such gasoline is contained. 
(d)	Exceptions. The provisions of this section do not apply to gasoline contained in the fuel tank of any vehicle provided by the manufacturer of such vehicle for the carrying of gasoline for propelling the vehicle, which gasoline is to be used solely for the motive power of such vehicle, nor to a vehicle transporting gasoline in quantities of not more than five (5) gallons for emergency purposes, nor to gasoline being transported by common carriers in railroad cars, nor to vehicles owned and being operated by any government agency. 
(Code 1979, § 8-49) 
Secs. 10-95-10-105. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE 

Sec. 10-106. - Rights of council. 
    The adoption of this division shall not abridge the right of the city council to change, alter, increase or decrease the license tax provided for in this division, or to revoke for cause the license provided for in this division, at any time, and when any increase is made, unless the increase is paid in thirty (30) days, the license shall be revoked and no further business carried on thereunder. 
(Code 1979, § 8-52) 
Sec. 10-107. - License required. 
    Each person engaging in the business for which a license tax is provided and required under this division without first obtaining and having a license therefor as required under this division shall be guilty of an offense against the city and shall be punished as set forth in this article. 
(Code 1979, § 8-42) 
Sec. 10-108. - Permit for persons without place of business within city. 
    It shall be unlawful for any seller, distributor or storer, or any other person, having no place of business within the corporate limits of the city or within the police jurisdiction thereof, to make any sale, distribution or delivery of gasoline therein, without first having obtained a permit so to do from the city clerk. Such person, seller, distributor or storer shall be liable for and pay the same license tax as that fixed and specified in section 10-110. 
(Code 1979, § 8-41) 
Sec. 10-109. - Issuance fee. 
    A fee of fifty cents ($0.50) shall be collected for issuing each license under this division. 
(Code 1979, § 8-50) 
Sec. 10-110. - Levy of tax. 
    Every distributor, seller or storer shall pay a license tax to the city, and a license tax is hereby fixed and created, which license tax shall be equal to one cent ($0.01) on each and every gallon of gasoline sold, distributed, delivered, stored or withdrawn from storage within the corporate limits of the city, and an amount equal to one-half of one cent ($0.005) on each and every gallon of gasoline sold, distributed, delivered, stored or withdrawn from storage outside the corporate limits of the city but within the police jurisdiction thereof, such license tax to be due and payable as set forth in this division. Any distributor, seller or storer may obtain the exemption provided for in section 10-111 by filing the statement provided for in section 10-111. The license tax fixed in this section on the business of selling, distributing, delivering, storing or withdrawing from storage of gasoline outside of the corporate limits of the city but within the police jurisdiction thereof is for administrative purposes and not for revenue. 
(Code 1979, § 8-37) 
Cross reference- Fire prevention and protection, Ch. 7; police, Ch. 16. 
Sec. 10-111. - Exemption from tax. 
    Any seller, distributor or storer selling, distributing, delivering, storing or withdrawing from storage gasoline purchased in whole from any other seller, distributor or storer who has paid the license tax imposed in this division with respect to such gasoline shall not be required to pay any license tax under this division based on the sale, distribution, delivery, storage or withdrawal from storage of such gasoline so purchased; provided, however, that in order to obtain such exemption such seller, distributor or storer must, on or before February 20, and on or before the twentieth day of each and every month thereafter, file with the city clerk a written statement, sworn to and subscribed by such seller, distributor or storer, showing each and every purchase or procurement of gasoline made by such seller, distributor or storer during the calendar month next preceding, together with the name of the person from whom purchased or procured, and the disposition thereof by such seller, distributor or storer claiming the exemption, such statement to be made in the form prescribed by the city clerk. 
(Code 1979, § 8-38) 
Sec. 10-112. - Filing of monthly statement. 
    Each and every distributor, seller and storer, except such as claim and obtain exemption under the provisions of the section 10-111, shall, on or before February 20, and on or before the twentieth day of each and every month thereafter, file with the city clerk, on forms prescribed by the city clerk, a sworn statement of the amount and quantity of all gasoline sold, distributed, delivered, stored or withdrawn from storage by such distributor, seller or storer within the corporate limits of the city, and within its police jurisdiction, during the calendar month next preceding, and which also shall contain a detailed, itemized statement of the amount and quantity of all gasoline sold, distributed or delivered to any other distributor, seller or storer. Any distributor, seller or storer failing, refusing or omitting to file such statement within the time prescribed in this section shall be guilty of an offense against the city, which shall be a continuing offense, and each day that such default continues shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Code 1979, § 8-39) 
Sec. 10-113. - Payment of tax; penalties for delinquency. 
    The license tax fixed and prescribed in this division shall be paid by each person against whom the tax is levied under this division, or who is liable or subject to such license under the provisions of this division, on or before the twentieth day of each calendar month, at the time of filing the statement required by section 10-112. The license tax shall be based on the sale, delivery, distribution, storage and withdrawal from storage of gasoline made during the calendar month next preceding. Any person failing, refusing or omitting to pay such license tax within the time prescribed in this division shall be guilty of an offense against the city, which shall be a continuing offense, and each day that such default continues shall constitute a separate offense. In addition to the other penalties provided for in this article, there shall be added to such license tax a penalty of twenty (20) percent of the amount thereof for such delinquency. 
(Code 1979, § 8-40) 
Sec. 10-114. - Right of collection of tax. 
    The acceptance of any money paid for the license tax provided for in this division shall in no way preclude the collection of the amount actually due; provided, however, that any payment made shall be credited against the amount actually due. 
(Code 1979, § 8-44) 
Sec. 10-115. - Acting as agent for delinquent dealer. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, after the license tax provided for in this division becomes delinquent, to act as agent, servant or employee for any person liable for such delinquent license tax, in engaging in or assisting in carrying on the business for which his principal or employer is required to pay such license, and each day such agent, servant or employee shall engage in or assist in carrying on such business shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Code 1979, § 8-46) 
Sec. 10-116. - Audits. 
    Upon demand by the city clerk or his authorized deputy, auditor or representative, it shall be the duty of any person subject to the license tax imposed by this division to furnish to such city clerk or his authorized deputy, auditor or representative, without delay, all such information as may be required for determination of the correct amount of license tax to which such person is subject, and to that end it shall be the duty of such person to submit to the city clerk or his authorized deputy, auditor or representative, for inspection and examination, during reasonable business hours, at such person's place of business, all books of account, invoices, papers, reports and memoranda containing entries showing the amount of purchases, sales, receipts, inventories, and any other information from which the correct amount of license tax to which such person is subject may be determined, including exhibition of bank deposit books and bank statements. Any person failing or refusing to submit such records for such examination and inspection upon such demand shall be guilty of an offense against the city. 
(Code 1979, § 8-47) 
Sec. 10-117. - Assessment of tax when information not available. 
(a)	If any person subject to the provisions of this division does not have in his possession or under his control true and intelligible books of account, invoices, papers, reports or memoranda correctly showing the data and information necessary for determination of the correct amount of the license tax due, or if, having in his possession or under his control such books, invoices, papers, reports or memoranda, he fails or refuses to submit and exhibit the books, invoices, papers, reports or memoranda for inspection and examination as required by this division, then, in either event, it shall be the duty of the city clerk to ascertain, from such information and data as he may reasonably obtain, the correct amount of license tax due from such person, to assess the tax against such person, to give such person notice of the assessment, and to demand of such person immediate payment of the amount of such license tax ascertained to be due, less any amount such person may have theretofore paid upon the license tax. 
(b)	If the amount of the license tax so ascertained and demanded is not paid within ten (10) days after receipt of notice of the assessment and demand for payment thereof, the city clerk shall notify such person by registered mail that, at a time and place specified in the notice, which time shall be not less than five (5) days after the mailing of such notice, and which place shall be the usual meeting place of the city council, he will apply to the council for revocation of such person's license. At the time and place so specified, such person may appear before the council in person or by counsel, or both, and show cause, if there be any, why the license should not be revoked. 
(c)	At any such hearing, and for all other purposes, the decision and determination of the city clerk as to the amount of the license tax due shall be deemed correct and final, unless and until it is satisfactorily shown that such decision and determination is incorrect. 
(Code 1979, § 8-48) 
Secs. 10-118-10-140. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - TOBACCO PRODUCTS 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (5) --- 
State Law reference- State tobacco taxes, Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-25-1 et seq.; basis of municipal tax levy on cigarettes, Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-25-29; state license taxes on tobacco dealers, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 40-12-72, 40-12-73. (Back)
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 10-141-10-150. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - CIGARETTES 

Sec. 10-151. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. The masculine gender shall include the feminine and neuter genders. Whenever the context requires, the plural shall include the singular, and singular the plural. Any words or phrases used in this division and not defined in this division which are defined in the General Revenue Act of General Acts of Alabama of 1935, pages 530 to 584 inclusive, shall have the meaning ascribed to them by that act. 
    Corporate limits means the corporate limits of the city. 
    Dealer means any wholesale or retail dealer subject to this division. 
    Package means the individual box or other container from which or in which retail sales of the tobacco products mentioned in this division are normally made or intended to be made. 
    Person means a natural person, firm, corporation, club, association, joint stock company, receiver, estate, trustee or any other person acting in a fiduciary capacity. 
    Police jurisdiction means the territory outside, but within one and one-half (11/2) miles of the corporate limits of the city. 
    Retail price means the usual retail selling price of the article before adding the amount of the tax assessed in this division or the tobacco tax assessed by the state. 
    Sale means any transfer of title or possession, or both, exchange or barter, conditional or otherwise, in any manner or by any means whatsoever, for a consideration or any agreement therefor, including rewards, prizes or premiums or the giving of tobacco products as a result of operations on punchboards, shooting galleries or other activities. 
    Stamps means the stamps by the use of which the tax levied under this division is paid. 
    Storer means any person who ships or causes to be shipped or receives tobacco products into the city or its police jurisdiction and stores the products in any manner or withdraws or uses the products for any purpose other than for resale or reshipment outside the city and police jurisdiction. 
    Tobacco products includes cigarettes and any substitution therefor. 
    Wholesale dealer and jobber means a person who sells or delivers, within the city or its police jurisdiction, any tobacco products, and all persons operating under a retail dealer's license. 
(Code 1979, § 8-53) 
Sec. 10-152. - Division cumulative. 
    This division shall not repeal any of the provisions of Article II, but shall be held to be cumulative. 
(Code 1979, § 8-60(c)) 
Sec. 10-153. - Exceptions to division. 
(a)	This division shall not be applied so as to impose any unlawful tax or unlawful burden on interstate commerce or any business of the United States government or any branch or agency thereof. 
(b)	This division shall not apply to tobacco products stored by a wholesale dealer for the purpose of resale or reshipment outside the city and its police jurisdiction and which are actually so resold or shipped. 
(Code 1979, § 8-60(a), (b)) 
Sec. 10-154. - Levy of tax. 
(a)	Within corporate limits. In addition to all other taxes imposed by law, every person who sells, stores or delivers any tobacco products shall pay a license tax to the city, and a license tax is hereby levied, which license tax shall be in the amounts fixed from time to time by the council, for the sale, storage or delivery of tobacco products in the corporate limits of the city. 
(b)	Police jurisdiction. Every person selling, delivering or storing any tobacco products in the police jurisdiction of the city shall pay to the city one-half the license tax levied under subsection (a) of this section. 
(Code 1979, §§ 8-54, 8-55) 
Sec. 10-155. - Form of stamps; purchase of stamps. 
    The city clerk shall keep on hand for sale an adequate quantity of stamps to be affixed to each package of tobacco products in denominations as required under this division. Each such stamp shall have inscribed thereon the words "City of Clanton, Alabama-Tobacco Tax," but the words need not be arranged in this order and may be abbreviated. The stamps may be sold to the wholesale dealer only by the city clerk at a price equal to ninety (90) percent of the full amount thereof, the remaining ten (10) percent of such full amount representing compensation to the wholesale dealer for the labor of affixing them to the tobacco products. All other persons, except such wholesale dealer, must pay the full face amount of the stamps, but no person or dealer shall be entitled to purchase any such number of the stamps as would cause the purchase price to include the fraction of a cent. 
(Code 1979, § 8-56) 
Sec. 10-156. - Affixing and cancellation of stamps. 
(a)	Before any tobacco products shall be sold or delivered within the corporate limits of the city or police jurisdiction by any dealer, such dealer shall affix to each package of tobacco products the stamps obtained from the city clerk, in the amounts provided for in this division, in payment of the license taxes imposed by this division. Every dealer shall, within one (1) hour after the receipt of any such tobacco products within the city or its police jurisdiction, unless sooner offered for sale, cause stamps to the requisite amount of the tax to be affixed as provided in this section and cause the stamps to be canceled by writing or stamping with waterproof ink across the face of each stamp the registered number furnished such dealer by the state department of revenue. 
(b)	After such stamping has been begun it shall be continued with reasonable diligence by such dealer until all the unstamped tobacco products have been stamped and the stamps canceled as provided in this section. No stamp required to be affixed to any package of tobacco products shall be used again in payment of any part of the tax levied under this division after the stamps have been affixed as provided in this section. Such stamps shall be affixed in such a manner that their removal will require continued application of water or steam. In the case of cigarettes sold by retail in package, the stamps shall be affixed to each individual package in such a way that such stamps shall be torn in two (2) or mutilated when such package is opened. 
(Code 1979, § 8-57) 
Sec. 10-157. - Subsequent sales or delivery after stamps have been affixed. 
    Whenever the requisite amount of stamps has been affixed to tobacco products as required under this division, this division shall not require additional stamps to be affixed thereto in case of subsequent sales, deliveries or storages; except, where such products have been properly stamped for sale, delivery or storage within the police jurisdiction, there must be properly affixed to such products and properly canceled an equal amount of stamps to those already affixed in case such products are sold, delivered or stored within the corporate limits of the city. 
(Code 1979, § 8-60(e)) 
Sec. 10-158. - Records; report of receipt of unstamped articles. 
(a)	Every wholesale dealer shall, at the time of selling or delivering any tobacco products into the city or its police jurisdiction, make a true duplicate invoice of the sale or delivery which shall show full and complete details of the sale or delivery of such tobacco products, and shall retain the invoice subject to the use and inspection of the city clerk or his duly authorized deputy for a period of three (3) years. 
(b)	Wholesale and retail dealers shall also keep a record of the purchase, sale, exchange or receipt of all tobacco products and hold all books, records, canceled checks and all other memoranda pertaining to such purchase, sale, exchange or receipt for the period mentioned in this section, subject to the inspection of the city clerk or his duly authorized deputy, who shall have the power and authority to enter upon the premises of any dealer and to examine such books, records and memoranda at all reasonable times. 
(c)	Any person who purchases or receives in any manner whatsoever any tobacco product which does not have affixed the stamps required by this division shall, within three (3) days after receipt of such articles of tobacco, report the receipt and purchase of the tobacco products to the city clerk, giving the date of purchase or receipt, the name and address of the person from whom purchased or received, and a list describing the articles of tobacco purchased or received. Such report must be made by registered mail or in person. 
(d)	It shall be unlawful for any person to interfere with or obstruct the city clerk or his deputy in the exercise of the power and authority conferred by this division. 
(Code 1979, § 8-58) 
Sec. 10-159. - Unlawful acts. 
    Among others, the following acts and omissions shall be unlawful: 
(1)	It shall be unlawful for any person required by this division to affix stamps to tobacco products to fail to affix such stamps or to cancel such stamps in the manner or within the time required by this division. 
(2)	It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, offer for sale or deliver within the city or its police jurisdiction any tobacco products to which stamps have not been affixed and canceled as provided by this division. 
(3)	It shall be unlawful for any dealer to have in his possession or under his control any tobacco products not properly stamped as required by this division for more than six (6) hours after receipt of such products on the premises of such person, provided that this subsection shall not apply to tobacco products in the possession of wholesale dealers or jobbers kept for the purpose of resale or reshipment outside the city and its police jurisdiction, which products are actually so resold or reshipped. The possession of each article or commodity not having the proper stamps affixed thereto as required by this division shall be deemed a separate offense. 
(4)	It shall be unlawful to manufacture, buy, sell, offer for sale or possess any reproduction or counterfeit of the stamps provided for in this division, or attempt to do so, or to possess tools, implements, instruments or materials of any kind necessary or appropriate to reproduce or counterfeit such stamps or to alter or cause to be altered any stamp provided for in this division. 
(5)	It shall be unlawful to remove from a package or otherwise prepare any stamp with intent to use or cause the stamp to be used, or to buy, sell, offer for sale or give away, any washed, removed, altered or restored stamp to any person or to have in possession any such washed or removed or restored or altered stamp, or, for the purpose of indicating the payment of any tax under this division, to reuse any stamp which has theretofore been used for the payment of any tax provided in this division, or, except as to the city clerk, to sell any stamp provided for in this division. 
(6)	It shall be unlawful to reuse or refill with any tobacco products any package from which such tobacco products have been removed and on which the tax has theretofore been paid. 
(Code 1979, § 8-59) 
Secs. 10-160-10-170. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - PRODUCTS OTHER THAN CIGARETTES 

Sec. 10-171. - Exceptions to division. 
(a)	This division shall not be applied so as to impose any unlawful tax or unlawful burden on interstate commerce or any business of the United States government or any branch or agency thereof. 
(b)	This division shall not apply to the tobacco products mentioned in this division stored by a wholesale dealer for purpose of resale or reshipment outside the city when such tobacco products are actually so resold or reshipped. 
(Ord. No. 11-89, § 5, 12-20-89) 
Sec. 10-172. - Levy of tax. 
    In addition to all other taxes of every kind imposed by law, every person within the city who sells or stores or receives for the purpose of distribution to any person within the city cigars, cheroots, stogies, smoking tobacco, chewing tobacco, smokeless tobacco, snuff or any substitute therefor shall pay to the city, for municipal purposes only, a license, excise or privilege tax, which shall be measured by and graduated in accordance with the volume of sales of each person in the city. There is hereby levied a license, excise or privilege tax on articles containing tobacco, other than cigarettes, as enumerated in this section, in the following amounts: 
(1)	Cigarettes. Upon cigarettes of all descriptions made of tobacco, or any substitute therefor, packaged in twenty (20) items or less per package, five cents ($0.05) for each package. 
(2)	Little cigars, small cigars, cigarillos. Upon cigars of all descriptions made of tobacco, or any substitute therefor, packaged in twenty (20) items or less per package, five cents ($0.05) for each package. 
(3)	All other cigars, cheroots, stogies, etc. Upon cigars of all descriptions, other than those described in subsection (1) of this section, made of tobacco, or any substitute therefor, five cents ($0.05) per cigar. 
(4)	Smoking tobacco, chewing tobacco, smokeless tobacco, snuff, etc. Upon all smoking tobacco, including granulated, plug cut, crimp cut, ready rubbed and other kinds and forms of tobacco prepared in such manner as to be suitable for smoking in a pipe or cigarette, upon all chewing tobacco or smokeless tobacco prepared in such manners to be suitable for chewing only, and not suitable for smoking; and upon snuff, five cents ($0.05) per container. 
(Ord. No. 11-89, § 1, 12-20-89; Ord. No. 4-03, § 1, 8-25-03) 
Sec. 10-173. - Payment of tax; monthly statement of sales. 
(a)	The tax levied in this division shall be paid to the city by every person who is liable therefor, and against whom such tax is levied and fixed under the provisions of this division, on or before the twentieth day of each calendar month, based upon applicable sales during the preceding month. 
(b)	Every person liable for the payment of the tax levied in this division shall accompany the payment thereof, as required in subsection (a) of this section, with a sworn, written statement accurately reflecting sales by quantity and by gross receipts for each category of product described in this division. The city clerk shall make available to each taxpayer forms suitable to reflect the information required under this subsection. 
(Ord. No. 11-89, § 2, 12-20-89) 
Sec. 10-174. - Records. 
    Every wholesale dealer shall, at the time of selling and delivering any tobacco products subject to the tax imposed by this division into the city, make a true duplicate invoice of the sale and delivery, which shall show full and complete details of the sale and delivery of such tobacco products, and shall retain the invoice subject to the use and inspection of the city clerk or his duly authorized deputy for a period of three (3) years. Wholesale and retail dealers shall also keep a record of the purchase, sale, exchange and receipt of all tobacco products and shall hold all books, records, canceled checks and other memoranda pertaining to such purchase, sale, exchange and receipt for the period mentioned in this section, subject to the inspection of the city clerk or his duly authorized deputy, who shall have the power and authority to enter upon the premises of any dealer and to examine such books, records and memoranda at all reasonable times. 
(Ord. No. 11-89, § 3, 12-20-89) 
Sec. 10-175. - Addition of tax to sales price. 
    The tax levied in this division shall be paid to the city, accompanied by a monthly sworn written statement, as provided in this division. However, every wholesaler, distributor, jobber or retail dealer shall add the amount of the tax levied in this division to the price of the tobacco or tobacco products sold, it being the purpose and intent of this division that the tax levied is, in fact, a levy on the ultimate consumer or user, with the wholesaler, distributor, jobber or retail dealer acting merely as an agent of the state for collection and payment of the tax to the city. It shall be unlawful for any person to fail or refuse to add to the sale price, and collect from the purchaser, the amount of the tax to be added to the sale price and collected from the purchaser under this division. 
(Ord. No. 11-89, § 4, 12-20-89) 
Secs. 10-176-10-180. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - TOBACCO SMOKE IN FOOD AND BEVERAGE ESTABLISHMENTS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (6) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2-05, §§ I-VIII, adopted Feb. 28, 2005, was not specifically amendatory of the Code and has been included as art. V, div. 4, §§ 10-181-10-188 at the discretion of the editor. 
Sec. 10-181. - Definitions and guidelines. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Business agent. An individual who has been designated by the owner or operator of any establishment to be the manager or otherwise in charge of said establishment. 
    Employee. Any individual who performs services for an employer in return for wages or profit. 
    Enclosed. A space, structure, facility or any portion thereof, bounded by walls (with or without windows) continuous from floor to ceiling or deck above and served by heating, ventilating and air conditioning (HVAC) system(s), and through which air can circulate from one (1) portion to another, including, but not limited to offices, rooms, hallways, customer service areas, foyers, common areas, waiting areas, restrooms, lounges, and eating areas. 
    Food and/or beverage establishment. Any establishment which is required to have a business license from the City of Clanton and which provides food and/or beverage under a permit from the health department and/or an "on premises" liquor license from the alcohol and beverage control (ABC) board. 
    Smoking. Inhaling, exhaling, burning or carrying any lighted cigar, cigarette, pipe, or other lighted tobacco product in any manner or form. 
(Ord. No. 2-05, § I, 2-28-05) 
Sec. 10-182. - Designating food and beverage establishments as smoke-free or smoking. 
(a)	It shall be the responsibility of the owner of the food and beverage establishment to designate his/her establishment as one (1) of the following: 
(1)	Smoke-free or
(2)	Smoking.
(b)	For establishments designated as SMOKE-FREE, no smoking by any persons (employees or patrons) at anytime will be allowed in any part of the enclosed areas of the establishment, except as noted in section 10-182, subsections (h) and (i) below. 
(c)	For establishments designated as SMOKE-FREE, signage shall be posted conspicuously on or adjacent to each and every door to the establishment that is generally accessed by patrons or employees, plainly visible from the exterior of the building to persons entering through the door. Signage shall be no smaller than eight and one-half (8.5) inches by eleven (11) inches, with white lettering on a red or black background, and include the following statements; 
"This establishment is a SMOKE-FREE facility" with letters no smaller than 5 / 8 inch tall (approximately 66 pts.); "Smoking is prohibited throughout this facility at all times" with letters no smaller than 1/4 inch tall (approximately 36 pts.); and "City of Clanton Ordinance Book ____________, Page ____________" with letters no smaller than 1/8 inch tall (approximately 20 pts.). 
(d)	For establishments designated as SMOKING, smoking by patrons shall be allowed throughout all enclosed areas generally occupied by patrons. 
(1)	If an owner, operator, business agent, or other person who controls a food and/or beverage establishment that is designated as SMOKING wishes to have a non-smoking area within the premises, it shall be at the discretion of said owner, operator, business agent or other person who controls said establishment whether to declare and enforce a non-smoking policy within the premises. 
(e)	For establishments designated as SMOKING, signage shall be posted conspicuously on or adjacent to each and every door to the establishment that is generally accessed by patrons or employees, plainly visible from the exterior of the building to persons entering through the door. Signage shall be no smaller than eight and one-half (8.5) inches by eleven (11) inches, with white lettering on a red or black background, and include the following statements: "This establishment is a SMOKING facility" with letters no smaller than five-eighths (5/8) inch tall (approximately sixty-six (66) pts.); "Smoking is allowed throughout this facility at all times" with letters no smaller than one-quarter (1/4) inch tall (approximately thirty-six (36) pts.); "There is no nonsmoking section" with letters no smaller than one-quarter (1/4) inch tall (approximately thirty-six (36) pts.); and "City of Clanton Ordinance Book ____________, Page ____________" with letters no smaller than one-eighth (1/8) inch tall (approximately twenty (20) pts.). 
(f)	Two (2) or more food and beverage establishments operating under separate permits and/or licenses shall not be directly connected by any interior means of access including but not limited to doorways, windows, service bars or service windows, unless each has the same designation (SMOKE-FREE or SMOKING). If SMOKING is chosen for any but not all of the establishments, each one for which SMOKING is chosen must have HVAC system(s) which serve only that area, and the HVAC system shall be balanced so as to keep a zero percentage pressure environment in all doorways and windows, and be physically separated by barriers which are constructed in a manner so as to shield non-smoking patrons in their entirely from smoking patrons. 
(g)	A facility which is SMOKE-FREE but which has a SMOKING establishment within it may add additional language to the required signage (see section 10-182(c)), after "Smoking is prohibited throughout this facility at all times" stating "except in designated areas" in matching letters and signage is required for exterior doors only. If all areas/establishments within a facility are SMOKE-FREE, then signage shall be required for exterior doors only. 
(h)	Food and beverage establishments may offer a separate smoking lounge if it is physically separated by barriers which are constructed in a manner so as to shield non-smoking patrons in their entirety from smoking patrons, is served by HVAC system(s) which serve only that area, and the HVAC system shall be balanced so as to keep a zero percentage pressure environment in all doorways and windows. 
(i)	Smoking may be permitted in hotel, motel, inn, bed and breakfast and lodging rooms that are rented to guests designated as "smoking rooms". A facility which offers such rooms for rent to guests may add additional language to the required signage (see section 10-182(c)), after "Smoking is prohibited throughout this facility at all times" stating "Lodging rooms are available for guests who smoke" in matching letters and signage. 
(j)	Food and beverage establishments will be listed in a listing by status (SMOKE-FREE or SMOKING) to be published annually by the city clerk's office no later than March 1; the first listing will be done by July 1, 200____________; the listing will be available to the public from the city clerk's office and will also be posted on the city's website. 
(Ord. No. 2-05, § II, 2-28-05) 
Sec. 10-183. - Violations. 
(a)	It shall be the responsibility of the owner, business agent, manager or other person having control of such food and beverage establishment to ensure compliance with all sections of this division pertaining to his/her place of business. A violator of this division may receive: 
(1)	In the case of a first violation, a fine of one hundred dollars ($100.00);
(2)	In the case of a second violation, within twenty-four (24) months of the first violation, a fine of five hundred dollars ($500.00); and, 
(3)	In the case of three (3) or more violations within twenty-four (24) months of the second or current violation, a fine of five hundred dollars ($500.00) for each violation. 
(b)	No provision, clause or sentence of this section of this division shall be interpreted as prohibiting the City of Clanton from suspending or revoking any license or permit issued by and within the jurisdiction of the City of Clanton for repeated violations of this division. 
(c)	If the owner, business agent, manager or other person having control of such food and beverage establishment attempts to enforce this division and a patron violates it (smoke in a SMOKE-FREE establishment), then the owner, business agent, manager or other person having control shall not be deemed to be in violation of this division and the patron shall be subject to a fine as follows: 
(1)	In the case of a first violation, a fine of one hundred dollars ($100.00);
(2)	In the case of a second violation, within twenty-four (24) months of the first violation, a fine of five hundred dollars ($500.00); and, 
(3)	In the case of three (3) or more violations within twenty-four (24) months of the second or current violation, a fine of five hundred dollars ($500.00) for each violation. 
(d)	Each calendar day an owner, business agent, manager or other person having control of a food and beverage establishment operates in violation of any provision of this division shall be deemed a separate violation; each calendar day a patron violates this division (i.e., smokes in a SMOKE-FREE establishment) shall be deemed a separate violation. 
(Ord. No. 2-05, § III, 2-28-05) 
Sec. 10-184. - Enforcement. 
(a)	Authority to enforce this division shall be held by the City of Clanton, its subsidiary programs or designees. 
(b)	An owner, manager, operator, or employee of an establishment regulated by this division shall inform persons violating this division of the appropriate provisions thereof. 
(c)	The City of Clanton's Fire Department, or its designee, the Chilton County Health Department, or its designee, shall, while in an establishment that is undergoing otherwise mandated inspection, or at any other time deemed necessary by these entities, inspect for compliance with this division. 
(d)	Any citizen who desires to register a complaint under this division may initiate enforcement with the Magistrate of the City of Clanton. 
(e)	Any fines or fees collected under this division shall be used for the enforcement of these regulations. 
(Ord. No. 2-05, § IV, 2-28-05) 
Sec. 10-185. - Non-retaliation. 
    No owner, business agent, manager or other person having control of a food and beverage establishment shall discharge, refuse to hire, refuse to serve or in any manner retaliate or take any adverse personnel action or other adverse action against any employee, applicant, customer or person because such employee, applicant, customer or person takes any action in furtherance of the enforcement of this division or exercises any right conferred by this division. 
(Ord. No. 2-05, § V, 2-28-05) 
Sec. 10-186. - Conflict with other laws, ordinances or regulations. 
(a)	Nothing in this division shall be deemed to amend or repeal any applicable fire, health or other law, ordinance or regulation so as to permit smoking in areas where it is prohibited by such fire, health or other law, ordinance or regulation. 
(b)	Nothing in this division shall be deemed to preempt the further limitation of smoking in the City of Clanton by any local regulatory body within the limits of its authority and jurisdiction. 
(Ord. No. 2-05, § VI, 2-28-05) 
Sec. 10-187. - Severability. 
    If any provision, clause, sentence, paragraph or word of this division or the application thereof to any person, entity or circumstances shall be held invalid, such invalidity shall not affect the other provisions of this division which can be given effect without the invalid provisions or application and to this end the provisions of this division are declared severable. 
(Ord. No. 2-05, § VII, 2-28-05) 
Sec. 10-188. - Effective date. 
    Food and beverage establishments legally permitted an/or licensed shall designate their status by notifying the city clerk's office in writing by May 01, 2005, and annually, thereafter, at the time of renewing their regular, annual business license. Food and beverage establishments shall implement the provisions of this division by June 01, 2005. Should an establishment opt to change its status prior to the regular annual renewal date for its business license, it will be required to purchase another business license at the same cost as the most recent regular annual one, in addition to any and all regular annual purchases. 
(Ord. No. 2-05, § VIII, 2-28-05) 
Secs. 10-189-10-195. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - PEDDLERS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (7) --- 
Cross reference- Licenses schedule, § 10-45. (Back)
State Law reference- State and county licenses for certain peddlers, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 40-12-139, 40-12-174; itinerant vendor's bond under sales tax law, Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-23-24. (Back)
Sec. 10-196. - Peddling of goods not produced by seller-Prohibited in certain areas. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to peddle, sell or offer for sale any goods, wares, merchandise, vegetables, fruits or produce not manufactured, raised or produced by the seller, on public streets, avenues, alleys or sidewalks and from any automobile, truck or motor vehicle parked upon the public streets, avenues alleys or sidewalks, in the area designated as follows: 
First Avenue, between the Louisville and Nashville Railroad and First Street. 
First Street, between Third Avenue North and Second Avenue South. 
Second Avenue North, between Eighth Street and First Street. 
Second Avenue South, between Sixth Street and First Street. 
Second Street, between Third Avenue North and Second Avenue South. 
Third Avenue North, between the Louisville and Nashville Railroad and First Street. 
Third Street, between Third Avenue North and Second Avenue South. 
Fourth Avenue North, between the Louisville and Nashville Railroad and Fourth Street. 
Fourth Street, between Fourth Avenue North and Second Avenue South. 
Fifth Avenue North, between Fifth Street and Seventh Street. 
Fifth Street, between Fifth Avenue North and Second Avenue South. 
Sixth Street, between Fifth Avenue North and Second Avenue South. 
Seventh Street, between Fifth Avenue North and Jackson Avenue. 
(Code 1979, § 9-21; Ord. No. 4-84, § 1, 4-9-84) 
Sec. 10-197. - Same-Areas where permitted. 
    It shall be lawful for any person to sell, peddle or offer for sale any goods, wares, merchandise, vegetables, fruits or produce not manufactured, raised or produced by the seller upon streets and alleys within the corporate limits of the city and outside and beyond the area prohibited in section 10-196. 
(Code 1979, § 9-22) 
Sec. 10-198. - Peddling of goods produced by seller. 
    It shall be lawful for any person who has raised, manufactured or produced any goods, wares, merchandise, vegetables, fruits or produce to sell, peddle or offer for sale such goods upon the streets, avenues, sidewalks or alleys of the city, after first obtaining the necessary producer's or grower's permit, and without the necessity of the purchase of a peddler's license. 
(Code 1979, § 9-23) 
Secs. 10-199-10-220. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - CARNIVALS AND STREET FAIRS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (8) --- 
State Law reference- State license for street fairs and carnivals, Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-12-163. (Back)
Sec. 10-221. - Definition. 
    For purposes of this article, the term "carnival" or "street fair" means an amusement enterprise consisting of sideshows, animal acts, vaudeville, games of chance and exhibitions, road shows, circuses, carnivals, exhibitions or amusements of every kind, character, Ferris wheels, merry-go-rounds, shooting galleries, games of skill, amusement rides, and rides of every character open to the public where an admission charge is charged, where a charge is made to enter onto the premises thereof, where a charge is made to enter into the various shows or exhibits thereof, or where a charge is made to participate in the games. 
(Code 1979, § 9-37) 
Sec. 10-222. - Application for license. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to hold, present, sponsor or conduct, within the city limits or the police jurisdiction, any carnival or street fair, without the person sponsoring, presenting or conducting the carnival or street fair making an application for a license to the city clerk. The application must state the owner of the carnival or street fair, the sponsoring organization, the proposed location thereof, the length of time for the running or conducting thereof, and the number and type of restrooms and other sanitary facilities available on the premises for the use of the public thereon and the employees of the carnival or street fair. 
(Code 1979, § 9-38) 
Sec. 10-223. - License tax. 
    There is hereby levied a privilege license for each carnival or street fair as follows: 
(1)	In the city limits of the city where the carnival or street fair is sponsored by an organized local civic, fraternal or religious organization, one hundred dollars ($100.00) per day. 
(2)	In the police jurisdiction of the city where the carnival or street fair is sponsored by an organized local civic, fraternal or religious organization, fifty dollars ($50.00) per day. 
(3)	In the city limits of the city where the carnival or street fair is not sponsored by an organized local civic, fraternal or religious organization, five hundred dollars ($500.00) per day. 
(4)	In the police jurisdiction of the city where the carnival or street fair is not sponsored by an organized local civic, fraternal or religious organization, two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) per day. 
(Code 1979, § 9-40) 
Sec. 10-224. - Cleanup deposit. 
    Prior to the issuance of a privilege license under this article, the carnival, street fair, or sponsoring organization must post with the city clerk a deposit in cash sufficient for the clearing and removal of all trash, paper or debris left upon the location of the carnival site, and conditioned upon the removal of all trash, paper or debris within three (3) days after the end of the carnival or street fair. If the trash, paper or debris is not so removed, then the cash amount may be forfeited to the city at the discretion of the mayor. 
(Code 1979, § 9-41) 
Sec. 10-225. - Sanitary facilities. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to promote, hold or conduct any carnival or street fair in the city limits or the police jurisdiction of the city unless proper and adequate restrooms or other sanitary facilities are provided on the premises for the use of the public and the use of the employees thereof. 
(Code 1979, § 9-39) 
Sec. 10-226. - Closing of unsuitable shows. 
    If the city council deems or determines that any show, sideshow, act or device is unsuitable for the public welfare, obscene or lewd, or not in the best public interest of the general public, then any or all of the carnival or street fair, upon the order of the city council, will be closed immediately. 
(Code 1979, § 9-42) 
Secs. 10-227-10-250. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VIII. - BILLIARD ROOMS AND POOLROOMS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (9) --- 
State Law reference- Billiard rooms, Code of Ala. 1975, § 34-6-1 et seq.; general municipal powers as to billiard and pool tables, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-51-102. (Back)
Sec. 10-251. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Billiard room, poolroom or pool hall means any public place where the game of billiards or pool is permitted to be played, and for which a charge is made. 
    Billiards means any of the several games played on a table surrounded by an elastic ledge of cushions, with balls which are impelled by a cue, and shall include all forms of the game known as carom billiards, pocket billiards, pool, and English billiards. 
(Code 1979, § 9-43) 
Sec. 10-252. - Authority of council. 
    The city council may fix a license fee for the operation of billiard rooms and may make such additional regulations governing the operation of billiard rooms as it may deem proper. 
(Code 1979, § 9-47) 
Sec. 10-253. - Persons ineligible for license. 
    No license shall be issued to any person to operate any billiard room or poolroom to which the public has access for amusement and recreation who is not twenty-one (21) years of age and a citizen of the United States, or who has been convicted of a felony. 
(Code 1979, § 9-44) 
Sec. 10-254. - Application for license; bond. 
    Application for a license to operate a billiard room shall be made to the city clerk and shall be accompanied by an affidavit of the applicant, sworn to before an officer authorized by law to administer oaths, that the applicant is a citizen of the United States, that he is of good moral character, that he has not been convicted of a felony, that he will not permit any person under the influence of intoxicating liquors to frequent or play in his place of business, that the applicant will have sole personal charge and management of the business, and that he will not permit public gambling in such place of business or permit the billiard tables to be used in any manner other than as provided by law. There shall also be filed with such application a bond in the penal sum of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00), payable to the state, and conditioned upon the faithful performance of all provisions of this article, signed by the applicant as principal and either a surety company or two (2) individuals as sureties. The bond shall be approved by the probate judge and filed in his office. 
(Code 1979, § 9-45) 
Sec. 10-255. - County license required. 
    Before any person shall be authorized to conduct a billiard room in the city, in addition to complying with the provisions of this article requiring the person to make application to the city clerk for a license, the applicant shall certify that application has been made to and a license granted to such applicant by the probate judge of the county. 
(Code 1979, § 9-46) 
Sec. 10-256. - Location of business. 
    No license shall be issued by the city council or by the city clerk to any person for the operation of a poolhall or billiard hall except where the poolhall or billiard hall is located adjacent to and fronting on a street or avenue in the city and on the street level of the city. 
(Code 1979, § 9-56) 
Sec. 10-257. - Penalty for operation without license. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or permit to be kept or used any billiard table within the city without having applied for a license as provided by this article. 
(Code 1979, § 9-54) 
State law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, § 34-6-30. 
Sec. 10-258. - Closing hours. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a billiard room between the hours of 11:30 p.m. and 6:00 a.m., or to harbor or permit any person to be or remain in such billiard room between such hours, except regular employees performing necessary labor within the premises. 
(Code 1979, § 9-48) 
Sec. 10-259. - Permitting minors on premises; misrepresentation of age. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to play billiards, or to be permitted to remain in a billiard room for any purpose, who has not reached the age of nineteen (19) years, unless accompanied by a parent or guardian. If the keeper of a billiard room is of the opinion that any person desiring admission thereto is under the age of nineteen (19) years, he shall require such person to certify his age in writing, and it is hereby made a misdemeanor for any minor to make false certification as to his age. 
(Code 1979, § 9-49) 
State law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, § 34-6-9. 
Sec. 10-260. - Posting of age requirement. 
    Every licensed billiard room proprietor shall post in his room where the tables are operated a placard having section 10-259 conspicuously written upon or printed thereon, in letters of not less than one-fourth inch in height, for the information of his patrons. 
(Code 1979, § 9-55) 
State law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, § 34-6-11. 
Sec. 10-261. - Gambling, intoxicating liquors prohibited. 
    No dice, cards, dominoes or other games of chance shall be permitted, nor any form of gambling allowed, in any billiard room or in any room in which billiard tables are located, or in any cigar store or other business located in the same room; and no game prohibited by law shall be played in such premises. It is expressly provided that such games as are known as Kelly pool, keno, star pool, scrub and similar gambling devices are expressly prohibited, and that no racing or other betting pool shall be exhibited, permitted or sold in such place of business, and that no intoxicating liquors shall be sold, served or allowed to be used in or on the premises. 
(Code 1979, § 9-50) 
Cross reference- Alcoholic beverages, Ch. 3; offenses and miscellaneous provisions, Ch. 13. 
Sec. 10-262. - Sanitation. 
    All billiard rooms shall be kept at all times in a clean, healthful and sanitary condition and shall comply with all ordinances regulating billiard rooms, and shall be subject to all sanitary rules and regulations of the health department. 
(Code 1979, § 9-51) 
Sec. 10-263. - Obstructions to view of interior prohibited. 
    No billiard room proprietor operating under the provisions of this article shall allow or permit any screens, curtains, blinds, partitions or other obstructions to be placed between the entrance or room where billiards are played and back or rear wall of such billiard room. A clear view of the entire interior from the entrance to the rear of such room must be maintained at all times. No partitions forming rooms, stalls or other enclosures where the public may congregate shall be permitted. This section, however, shall not be construed to prohibit the maintenance of washrooms and toilet rooms for proper purposes or the maintenance of closets for storage purposes exclusively. 
(Code 1979, § 9-52) 
Sec. 10-264. - Connection with certain premises prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any billiard room proprietor to maintain, or permit to be maintained, any open or secret connection, through door, window or trapdoor, panel, stairway or other device with any place where gambling is conducted or where persons congregate for immoral purposes. 
(Code 1979, § 9-53) 
State law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, § 34-6-7. 
Sec. 10-265. - Membership list required for clubs. 
(a)	Each club, private club or similar organization where the games of billiards, carom billiards, pocket billiards, pool or English billiards are permitted to be played, or the president, secretary, manager or other appropriate officer of each club or private club where the games of billiards, carom billiards, pocket billiards, pool or English billiards are permitted to be played, or every club that provides tables or other devices for or permits such games to be played or furnishes to its members or for the use of the members of the club or private club such tables or devices, shall furnish to the city clerk, on or before the fifteenth day of each month or the first business day thereafter, a complete and accurate list of the names of all of the members of the club. 
(b)	Each club, private club or organization that does not file or cause to be filed a complete and accurate list of the names of all of the members of the club by the fifteenth day of each month or the first business day thereafter shall be closed by the chief of police until the club or private club complies with the provisions of subsection (a) of this section. 
(Code 1979, §§ 9-58, 9-59) 
Sec. 10-266. - Violations by club officers. 
    The president, secretary, manager or other appropriate officer of each club organized, chartered or doing business in the city limits or the police jurisdiction, who violates the provisions of this article, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1979, § 9-60) 
Secs. 10-267-10-290. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IX. - TAXICABS 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (10) --- 
Cross reference- Motor vehicles and traffic, Ch. 11. (Back)
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 10-291. - Definition. 
    As used in this article, the word "taxicab" or "taxi" means any motor vehicle engaged in a business of carrying passengers for a reward and having a seating capacity of not more than seven (7) persons including the driver. 
(Code 1979, § 14-34) 
Sec. 10-292. - Operation by certain persons prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person who has been convicted of any felony or any crime involving moral turpitude or of public drunkenness or driving while intoxicated or of violation of any prohibition law within the preceding five (5) years to drive or operate a taxicab in the city or its police jurisdiction. 
(Code 1979, § 14-41) 
Secs. 10-293-10-305. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PERMIT 

Sec. 10-306. - Required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to transport persons for hire, by any taxicab or taxi, within the corporate limits of the city or its police jurisdiction, without first obtaining a franchise or permit to engage in such business as provided in this division. 
(Code 1979, § 14-35) 
Sec. 10-307. - Application. 
    Any person desiring to operate a taxicab business or to drive a taxicab in the city or its police jurisdiction shall first make a written application therefor upon a form to be furnished by the city clerk. The application shall be filed with the clerk and may be received by the clerk only if properly filled in. 
(Code 1979, § 14-36) 
Sec. 10-308. - Investigation of applicant. 
    The application referred to in this division shall be referred by the city clerk to the chief of police for investigation. The chief of police, with the assistance of other police officers of the city, shall make a comprehensive investigation of the applicant as to his financial responsibility, equipment to be used in the operation of taxicabs, and moral standing, whether or not the applicant has been previously convicted of any crime involving moral turpitude, violation of the prohibition laws or traffic violations, and such other matters as may involve the ability of the applicant to properly operate taxicabs within the city. 
(Code 1979, § 14-37) 
Sec. 10-309. - Granting. 
    After making the investigation required under this division, if the police officers of the city are satisfied that the applicant is a fit and proper person to safely operate and cause the operation of taxicabs in the city and that in all other respects the applicant has complied with the provisions of the traffic ordinances of the city, the police officers shall so report, in writing, to the city clerk, and the application shall be referred to the city council for the granting or refusal of the permit. No application shall be referred to the city council by the city clerk unless a majority of the police officers of the city then employed recommend the granting of such permit or franchise. If the application is not recommended to the city council by the police officers within ten (10) days from the date the application is referred by the clerk to the chief of police, the applicant may, in writing, by stating the facts, apply directly to the city council for such permit. No application shall be considered by the council, individually or collectively, until such application is filed with the city clerk as provided in this division and referred by the city clerk to the chief of police for investigation as provided in this division. 
(Code 1979, § 14-38) 
Sec. 10-310. - Making false statements in application. 
    No person shall be granted a permit to drive or to have taxicabs driven for him on the streets of the city who makes any false statement in his application for a permit. 
(Code 1979, § 14-39) 
Sec. 10-311. - Suspension or revocation. 
(a)	Any permit which may be granted to any person for the privilege of operating taxicabs or having taxicabs operated for him under this division is subject to suspension or revocation, or both. It shall be the duty of the person to whom such franchise or permit is granted: 
(1)	To employ careful drivers of reasonably good moral character;
(2)	Not to employ drivers who are known to be or suspected to be engaged in the violation of any laws involving moral turpitude or laws against the use of intoxicating liquors, or who are habitual violators of traffic laws; and 
(3)	Not to employ as a driver of any taxicab or to permit any taxicab to be operated by any person who has, during the preceding five (5) years, been convicted of any felony, any crime involving moral turpitude or the violation of any law regulating the use of intoxicating liquors. 
(b)	The permit or franchise granted under authority of this division may be revoked or suspended for a breach of any of the duties imposed on the holder of such permit in this section. It shall be the duty of the police officers of the city, upon receiving information of any breach of any law or of any duty on the part of anyone to whom any permit or franchise is granted, or on the part of any driver or operator of any taxicab under authority of this division, to report such violation, in writing, to the city council. The council shall appoint three (3) of the members of the council as a committee to investigate such charge, and may revoke or suspend such franchise or permit or may, at its discretion, revoke the license of the driver for any such violation if, in its opinion, it will be in the public interest that such permit or franchise be revoked or the license of such driver be revoked or suspended. It shall be the duty of the city council to suspend or revoke any permit or franchise granted under authority of this division whenever the city council is satisfied that it will be to the interest of the public welfare, whether the holder of such permit or franchise or any driver or operator of any taxicab be convicted of the violation of any law referred to in this section or not, the operation of taxicabs upon the streets of the city being a mere privilege and not a right. 
(Code 1979, § 14-40) 
Secs. 10-312-10-330. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE X. - TRANSIENT OCCUPANCY TAX 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (11) --- 
Cross reference- Taxation, Ch. 19. (Back)
Sec. 10-331. - Article cumulative. 
    This article shall not be construed to repeal any of the provisions of Article II, but shall be held to be cumulative, and the amounts of the taxes levied in this article shall be in addition to the amounts of all other license taxes imposed by the city by Article II. 
(Ord. No. 7-89, § 4, 8-28-89) 
Sec. 10-332. - Levy. 
(a)	For the privilege of engaging or continuing within the city in the business activities referred to in this section, there is hereby levied, in addition to all other taxes of every kind imposed by law, and shall be collected as provided in this article, a privilege or license tax against the person on account of the business activities, in the amounts to be determined by the application of rates against gross receipts as provided in this section. 
(b)	There is hereby levied and imposed, in addition to all other taxes of every kind imposed by law, a privilege or license tax upon every person engaging in the business of renting or furnishing any rooms, lodgings or accommodations to transients in any hotel, motel, inn, tourist camp, tourist cabin or any other place in which rooms, lodgings or accommodations are regularly furnished to transients for a consideration, in an amount to be determined by the application of the rate of four (4) percent of the charge for such rooms, lodgings or accommodations, including the charge for use or rental of personal property and services furnished in such room; provided, however, that any rental or service taxed under the provisions of Article II, levying the city privilege or license tax, is exempted from the tax levied under this article. The tax shall not apply to rooms, lodgings or accommodations supplied for a period of thirty (30) continuous days or more in any place. 
(Ord. No. 7-89, § 1, 8-28-89) 
Sec. 10-333. - Applicability of state statutes. 
    This article and the taxes levied in this article shall be subject to all definitions, exceptions, exemptions, proceedings, requirements, rules, regulations, provisions, penalties, fines, punishments and deductions that are applicable to the taxes levied by the state lodgings tax statutes, except where inapplicable or where otherwise provided in this article, including all provisions of the state lodgings tax statutes for enforcement and collection of taxes. 
(Ord. No. 7-89, § 2, 8-28-89) 
State law reference- Transient occupancy tax, Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-26-1 et seq. 
Sec. 10-334. - Addition of tax to rental. 
    Any person on whom the taxes levied by this article are imposed may add the tax levied in this article to the receipts from rental of rooms, lodgings or accommodations and may collect the tax from the occupants of such rooms, but this section is not mandatory. 
(Ord. No. 7-89, § 3, 8-28-89) 
Secs. 10-335-10-355. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XI. - PURCHASE OF PRECIOUS METALS OR PRECIOUS STONES 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (12) --- 
State Law reference- Public auctions, Code of Ala. 1975, § 8-14-1 et seq.; lien of jewelers, watchmakers and silversmiths, Code of Ala. 1975, § 35-11-150 et seq. (Back)
Sec. 10-356. - Definition. 
    As used in this article, the term "precious metals or precious stones" means all gold, silver, pearls, diamonds, rubies and other precious stones and any ornament or item made from or containing gold or silver or on which is set or displayed pearls, diamonds, rubies or other precious stones, including coins. 
(Ord. No. 1-81, § I, 1-12-81) 
Sec. 10-357. - Compliance with article. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person within the city limits or the police jurisdiction to engage in the business of purchasing precious metals or precious stones without complying with the terms of this article. 
(Ord. No. 1-81, § VI, 1-12-81) 
Sec. 10-358. - Police chief to be notified of intent to engage in business. 
    Any person within the corporate limits or the police jurisdiction of the city who engages in the business of purchasing precious metals or precious stones or who purchases precious metals or precious stones or who, pursuant to any advertisement wherein the proposed purchaser holds himself out as such purchaser, offers to buy precious metals or precious stones shall, before engaging in such business or enterprise, notify the chief of police of the city, by letter, that such business or enterprise will be conducted. The letter shall contain the name of the person who is conducting the business and the address at which such business will be conducted, the days of the week of the conducting of the business, and the time for the opening and the closing thereof. 
(Ord. No. 1-81, § II, 1-12-81) 
Cross reference- Police, Ch. 16. 
Sec. 10-359. - Record of purchases. 
    Every person engaging in the business or enterprise of purchasing precious metals or precious stones shall provide and keep a book and enter therein, as each purchase or acquisition is made, the following information: 
(1)	The name, address, date of birth, and the driver's license number of the seller. If the seller does not have a driver's license, then other adequate and positive identification, which shall be required before a purchase is made, shall be shown. 
(2)	The time and date of the purchase.
(3)	An accurate and detailed description of the item purchased, which shall include any marking or inscription, the make and pattern, if available, and the maker or style, if appropriate. Each description shall be detailed and accurate and shall include a reference to the size, weight and height. Where appropriate, an indication shall be made whether the item was made for use by a male or female. If precious stones are purchased, the kind, size and setting of the stone shall be included, together with such other information which may be necessary or useful in making a positive identification of the item purchased. 
Such book shall be kept for six (6) months, subsequent to any purchase and shall be open to the inspection, during business hours, of any authorized law enforcement officer who may make a request to examine the book. 
(Ord. No. 1-81, § III, 1-12-81) 
Sec. 10-360. - Separation of purchases; disposal of purchases. 
    Every item purchased from one (1) seller shall be separately packaged, or kept separately, and not intermingled or confused with items purchased from another seller, for a period of five (5) working days following the mailing of the report of purchase as required under this article; provided, however, that this provision shall not apply to coins, which may be intermingled or disposed of immediately after the notification of the chief of police of the purchase as required under this article. No person engaging in the business or enterprise of purchasing precious metals or precious stones shall sell or otherwise dispose of, permit to be sold or otherwise disposed of, remove or permit to be removed from his place of business, intermingle with other jewelry or stones, or alter, change, or deface or permit to be altered, changed or defaced any such precious metals or precious stones purchased, until after the expiration of five (5) working days from the notification to the chief of police of the purchase, as required under this division; provided, however, such items may be removed from the place of business for storage or safekeeping to another place within the jurisdiction of the city approved by the chief of police prior to such removal. 
(Ord. No. 1-81, § IV, 1-12-81) 
Sec. 10-361. - Daily report. 
    Each person engaging in the business or enterprise of purchasing precious metals or precious stones shall mail or otherwise deliver to the chief of police of the city a daily report, which report shall furnish to the city the information required under section 10-359 regarding each item purchased during the preceding workday. 
(Ord. No. 1-81, § V, 1-12-81) 
Secs. 10-362-10-385. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XII. - SOLICITATIONS 

Sec. 10-386. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Charitable or religious purpose means the use of the money or property for the benefit of: 
(1)	Charity or philanthropy, or underprivileged, needy, refugee, diseased, disabled or handicapped persons or persons in need of rehabilitation; 
(2)	A church, religious society or other religious sect, group or order;
(3)	Patriotism, that is, for the teaching of patriotism or the relief or assistance of veterans or veteran's organizations; or 
(4)	Existing educational institutions, or for the establishment or endowment of educational institutions or in aid of educational institutions or in aid of the education of any person or group of persons. 
    Conduct a solicitation means to manage, organize, direct, administer or be responsible for a solicitation on behalf of any person. 
    Cost of the solicitation means the amount of funds collected in excess of the amount spent for the direct benefit of the stated purpose of the solicitation, including but not limited to informational materials and activities, recruitment, training and compensation of solicitors, and management and administration of the solicitation and disbursement of the funds. 
    Funds spent for the direct benefit of the stated purpose of the solicitation means money expended directly for the specific purpose stated in the registration. 
    Person includes an individual, organization, society, church, corporation or any agent, member or representative thereof. 
    Solicit or solicitation means to: 
(1)	Request property, financial aid, money or anything of value;
(2)	Sell or offer to sell a product, article, tag, service, publication, document, advertising space, membership, subscription or tickets; or 
(3)	Hold, promote or participate in an entertainment, sports event, benefit dance, fair, bazaar or other type of organized social entertainment. 
(Ord. No. 3-81, § II, 3-9-81) 
Sec. 10-387. - Purpose of article. 
    The purpose of this article is to protect the health, safety, and welfare of the City of Clanton, Alabama and the public at large by regulating door to door solicitation in the city limits of the City of Clanton. The city has promulgated reasonable time, place and manner restrictions on door to door solicitations occurring in residential areas in order to reduce crimes such as fraud, identity theft, larceny, burglary, harassment, and home invasion; to protect its citizens from annoying, intrusive or dangerous solicitations and to assist law enforcement personnel in the performance of their duties. 
(Ord. No. 3-81, § I, 3-9-81; Ord. No. 3-13, § I, 6-24-2013) 
Sec. 10-388. - Registration procedure; identification badge. 
(a)	Registration under this article shall be complete when the person seeking to solicit or conduct a solicitation pays the registration fee and files with the city clerk the following information under oath on forms furnished or approved by the city: 
(1)	The name, local and permanent address and telephone number and headquarters of the person registering. 
(2)	If the registrant is not an individual, the names and addresses of the registrant's principal officers and managers and a copy of the resolution, if any, authorizing such solicitation, certified to as a true and correct copy of the original by the officer having charge of registrant's records. 
(3)	The purpose for which such solicitation is to be made, the total amount of funds proposed to be raised thereby, and the use or disposition to be made of any receipts therefrom. 
(4)	The names and addresses and official position of the persons by whom the receipts of such solicitations shall be disbursed for the stated purpose. 
(5)	The name, address and telephone number of the person who will be in direct charge of conducting the solicitation and the names and addresses of all promoters connected or to be connected with the proposed solicitation. 
(6)	An outline of the method to be used in conducting the solicitations.
(7)	The time when such solicitations shall be made, giving the preferred dates for the beginning and ending of such solicitation; and, if such period shall exceed thirty (30) days, the specified reasons for the need of such excess time. 
(8)	The estimated cost of the solicitation.
(9)	The amount of any wages, fees, commissions, expenses or emoluments to be expended or paid to any person in connection with such solicitations, and the names, addresses and social security numbers of all individual solicitors to be used in the solicitation. 
(10)	A financial statement for the last preceding fiscal year of any funds collected for charitable purposes by the registrant within the city, giving the amount of money so raised, together with the cost of raising it, and the final distribution thereof. 
(11)	A full statement of the character and extent of the charitable work being done by the registrant within the city. 
(12)	A statement that the actual cost of the solicitation will not exceed twenty-five (25) percent of the total amount to be raised. 
(b)	Upon receipt of the information required by subsection (a) of this section, the city clerk shall designate or approve an identification badge containing the name of the organization conducting the solicitation, the name or photograph of the authorized solicitor, the purpose of the solicitation and an authorization number. The identification badge shall be nontransferable and valid only during the period of the solicitation and shall in no way constitute an approval by the city of the purpose of the solicitation. Each solicitor shall display this identification badge in a prominent position on the outer clothing, clearly visible to the person from whom solicitations are sought. The identification badge shall be provided at the expense of the solicitor. 
(Ord. No. 3-81, § IV(1), (2), 3-9-81) 
Sec. 10-389. - Investigation; revocation or suspension of registration. 
(a)	Following registration to solicit under this article, the city clerk shall forthwith submit the registration information to the chief of police or his designated agent, for investigation into the truth and accuracy of the registrant and a preliminary determination of whether the registrant qualifies as an approved solicitor. 
(b)	If the police chief determines that the registrant is in accordance with the standards set forth in this article, no further action shall be taken. If the police chief makes a preliminary determination that the registrant does not so qualify or has materially violated a provision of this article or has made a material misstatement of fact in his registration information, then he shall so notify the registrant in writing, giving his reasons therefor, and advising the registrant of the next regular city council meeting, not sooner than four (4) days after mailing of the notice, at which time the question of revocation of the registration shall be on the council agenda and all interested parties heard, for the city council to determine whether the registrant qualifies as a solicitor under this article or whether such registration should be revoked, suspended or modified. Misstatements of material fact which could mislead the public are grounds for revocation. The decision of the city council shall be final. 
(Ord. No. 3-81, § VI, 3-9-81) 
Sec. 10-390. - Prohibited acts; exceptions. 
(a)	No person shall solicit or conduct a solicitation within the boundaries of the city on the plea or representation, express or implied, that the proceeds from the solicitation are for a charitable or religious purpose, unless the person is properly registered with the city and is prominently displaying identification as provided by this article.
