(b)	It shall be unlawful and an offense for anyone to solicit by telephone canvass or door to door solicitation, go from house to house or door to door ring the doorbell, rap or knock upon the door, or create any sound in a manner calculated to attract attention of the occupant thereof for the purpose of engaging in solicitation at a residence, a residential neighborhood, an apartment complex, or public housing facility except between the hours of 10:00 a.m. CST and 4:30 p.m. CST, in the absence of a specific invitation or appointment from the occupant of the residence and without first obtaining a business license. This section shall not apply to non-profit organizations such as but not limited to: Girl Scouts, Boy Scouts, school fund raisers, fire departments, etc. 
(1)	It shall be unlawful and an offense for any person engaged in solicitation within a residential area to remain on private property, in a private residence, or upon the premises of a private residence after the owner or occupant has requested the person to leave. 
(2)	It shall be unlawful and on offense for a person engaged in solicitation within a residential area at a private residence that has a posted sign indicating that the resident or occupant does not want such activities upon their property. Examples of such signs include but are not limited to, "No Solicitation," "Keep Out," or "No Trespassing." 
(c)	The provisions of this section do not apply to:
(1)	A person that solicits solely from its own membership or from foundations;
(2)	A person who does not collect more than one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) within a twelve-month period; and 
(3)	A person who solicits solely through the use of the public broadcasting media.
(Ord. No. 3-81, § III(1-3), 3-9-81; Ord. No. 3-13, § II, 6-24-2013) 
Sec. 10-391. - Soliciting on streets, etc. 
    No person shall solicit on streets, alleys or right-of-ways of the city at any time. 
(Ord. No. 3-81, § III(4), 3-9-81) 
Cross reference- Streets and sidewalks, Ch. 18. 
Sec. 10-392. - Receipt for contributions. 
    Any solicitor receiving money or anything having a value of ten dollars ($10.00) or more from any contributor shall give the contributor a written receipt containing the name and authorization number of the soliciting organization, the name of the solicitor signed on the receipt, the date, the amount received, and the portion of the contribution which is tax deductible. 
(Ord. No. 3-81, § IV(3), 3-9-81) 
Sec. 10-393. - Use of funds. 
    No person shall use or disburse funds collected pursuant to a charitable or religious solicitation for a purpose other than that stated in the statement filed with the city clerk and the actual and necessary expenses incident to the solicitation, collection and disbursement of funds; provided that expenses shall not exceed twenty-five (25) percent of the amount received after deduction of the actual cost of any tangible property given or otherwise transferred to contributors. 
(Ord. No. 3-81, § IV(4), 3-9-81) 
Sec. 10-394. - Financial report; access to records. 
(a)	Every person authorized to conduct a solicitation under this article shall file a financial report under oath with the city clerk within thirty (30) days after the solicitation has been completed. 
(1)	The report shall state in detail the amount of funds collected, the cost of any tangible property given to contributors, the expenses incurred in management and administration of the solicitation, and the distribution of the balance of the funds collected. 
(2)	The report shall state the name, address and social security number of each person receiving any wages, fees, commissions or expense either independently or based on the funds collected. 
(b)	All books, records and papers relating to the solicitation shall be available to the city clerk at city hall upon written request to the person authorized to conduct the solicitation. 
(Ord. No. 3-81, § V, 3-9-81) 
Secs. 10-395-10-410. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XIII. - YARD SALES 

Sec. 10-411. - License required; limitation on yard sales. 
(a)	Effective January 1, 2012, any person, firm or corporation engaged in the sale or the promoting for sale of any yard sale or rummage sale not held in conjunction with any established business subject to a retail merchant's license shall first obtain a license for the conducting of said business for ten dollars ($10.00) each day and not to extend for more than two (2) consecutive days. The city clerk is directed, in the issuing of said license, to designate on said license the days during which the sale may be conducted and not in excess of two (2) consecutive days. 
(b)	Not more than four (4) yard sales shall be permitted to be conducted in any location within the limits of the city or the police jurisdiction thereof within any one (1) calendar year. 
(Ord. No. 4-93, § II, 3-22-93; Ord. No. 16-93, § II-A, 11-9-93; Ord. No. 14-94, §§ II, II-A, 9-12-94; Ord. No. 6-11, § II, 11-28-2011) 
Sec. 10-412. - Cleanup of premises. 
    At the end of each sale day, the premises shall be cleaned up and left in an orderly manner. 
(Ord. No. 4-93, § III, 3-22-93; Ord. No. 14-94, § III, 9-12-94) 
Sec. 10-413. - Exceptions to license requirement. 
    The mayor shall be authorized to permit churches, fraternal, charitable, educational, religious and civic organizations to conduct yard sales or rummage sales according to the terms of this article except without the payment of the foregoing license. 
(Ord. No. 4-93, § IV, 3-22-93; Ord. No. 14-94, § IV, 9-12-94) 
Sec. 10-414. - Penalty for violation. 
    Any person in violation of any of the terms of this article shall, on conviction, be fined not more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) and may also be sentenced to hard labor for the county not exceeding thirty (30) days, one (1) or both. 
(Ord. No. 4-93, § V, 3-22-93; Ord. No. 14-94, § V, 9-12-94) 
Secs. 10-415-10-424. - Reserved. 
Sec. 10-425. - Rummage sales. 
    Persons and/or organizations holding rummage sales shall not be required to obtain a license therefor, but shall be required to obtain a permit from the city clerk. The fee for said permit shall be one dollar ($1.00). 
Note-The Mayor shall be authorized to permit churches and other charitable organizations to hold rummage sales on specific occasions without paying the permit fee. 
(Ord. No. 22-99, § 214, 12-22-99) 
Sec. 10-426. - Issuance fee. 
    Before any person, firm or organization shall engage in or carry on any business or do any act within the corporate limits or within the police jurisdiction of the city for which a license, as opposed to a permit, is required by this schedule, such person, firm or organization shall pay to the city clerk the amount required herein for such license, plus a fee of five dollars ($5.00) for the issuance thereof. 
(Ord. No. 22-99, § 262, 12-22-99) 
Secs. 10-427-10-440. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XIV. - FLEA MARKETS 

Sec. 10-441. - Definition. 
    For the purpose of this article, a flea market is hereby defined as any type of open air or enclosed public market place where new or used items of merchandise are placed on display for sale; a public sales area where a number of vendors may assemble or congregate for the purpose of the sale of merchandise and where individual vendors offer for sale merchandise from a designated sales area. 
(Ord. No. 8-93, § I, 6-28-93; Ord. No. 3-94, § I, 2-28-94) 
Sec. 10-442. - License fee. 
    All owners or operators of a flea market, as defined in section 10-441, shall pay to the city a license fee per year for each location for the operation thereof as follows: 
Number of VendorsAmount of License 1-24$ 35.0025-49100.0050 or above250.00 
(Ord. No. 8-93, § II, 6-28-93; Ord. No. 3-94, § II, 2-28-94) 
Sec. 10-443. - Rental tax. 
    All owners or operators of a flea market who offer a sale space or sale area to individual vendors for the sale of merchandise shall collect a rental tax for the city in the amount of one dollar ($1.00) for each table, booth or space rented for each day rented. 
(Ord. No. 8-93, § III, 6-28-93; Ord. No. 3-94, § III, 2-28-94) 
Sec. 10-444. - Rental receipt; display. 
    The owner or operator of a flea market shall keep on file a numbered copy of each rental receipt written. The holder of a rental receipt must display the rental tax receipt at a prominent location on or near the table, booth or space rented. 
(Ord. No. 8-93, § IV, 6-28-93; Ord. No. 3-94, § IV, 2-28-94) 
Sec. 10-445. - Report of rental tax collected; penalty. 
(a)	The owner or operator of a flea market shall report to the city clerk, at the end of each month, on forms furnished by the city clerk, the total amount of rental tax collected for the month. 
(b)	Failure to file this report and pay the amount specified on the form by the fifteenth day of the following month shall result in a ten (10) percent penalty being added to the full amount of the tax due the city. 
(Ord. No. 8-93, § V, 6-28-93; Ord. No. 3-94, § V, 2-28-94) 
Sec. 10-446. - Applicability. 
    The provisions of this article shall not apply to fraternal, educational, religious or civic organizations operating a flea market as a fund-raising enterprise. 
(Ord. No. 8-93, § VI, 6-28-93; Ord. No. 3-94, § VI, 2-28-94) 
Secs. 10-447-10-460. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XV. - PRIVATE SECURITY GUARDS AND/OR PRIVATE DETECTIVES 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (13) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 3-03, §§ 1-13, adopted Aug. 11, 2003, was not specifically amendatory of the Code and has been included as art. XV, §§ 10-461-10-473 at the discretion of the editor. 
Sec. 10-461. - Definitions. 
    For the purposes of this article the following terms, phrases, words and derivations shall have the meaning given herein. When not inconsistent with the context, words are used in the present tense include the future, words in the plural number. The masculine gender shall include the feminine and neuter. The word "shall" is always mandatory and not merely directory. 
    "City" is the City of Clanton, Alabama, a municipal corporation. 
    "Employee" shall include any person paid by, retained, supervised, employed or under the control of any private detective or private security guard as defined herein, for the discharge of any of the duties or responsibilities of a private detective or a private security guard. 
    "Person" is any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or organization of any kind. 
    "Private detective" is any person who accepts employment for hire, fee, or reward to furnish or supply information as to the persons, character or actions or identity of any person or as to the character or kind of business or occupation of any person. The term shall include within its meaning a private investigator employed exclusively for one (1) employer in connection with a business of a collection agency. Nor shall it include any officer belonging to any official enforcement agency of the United States, the State of Alabama, the City of Clanton, Alabama, or of any state, county or city. The term "private detective" shall include a private investigator or detective agency as defined by the ordinances and codes of the City of Clanton or the State of Alabama. 
    "Private security guard" is any person who accepts employment for hire, fee or reward to furnish or supply security services for the protection of any person, or any property either real or personal by placement of guards, guard dogs, periodic patrols or otherwise. The term shall specifically include private security guards employed exclusively by one (1) employer to provide security only for the person or property of the employer. However, the term shall not include any officer employed by any law enforcement agency of the United States, the State of Alabama, Chilton County or the City of Clanton. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 1, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-462. - License required. 
    No person shall operate as a private detective, a private security guard, or an employee (as defined herein) or either of them in the city without first obtaining a license as hereinafter provided from City of Clanton, Alabama. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 2, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-463. - Application for license. 
    Applications for licenses issued hereunder shall be made upon forms prepared and made available by the City of Clanton, Alabama, and shall state: 
(1)	The full name, age residence, present and previous occupations of the applicant;
(2)	Whether the person signing the application is a citizen of the United States;
(3)	A specific description of the location of the principal place of business of the applicant (not simply post office box number); 
(4)	The number of years experience the applicant has had a private detective or in related fields; 
(5)	The length of time applicant has been a bona fide resident of this city and the State of Alabama immediately preceding the filing of the application; 
(6)	The names, addresses and ages of any proposed or actual employees of the applicant or the name of the applicants employer, as the case may be; 
(7)	The application required hereunder shall be accompanied by a full set of fingerprints and a recent photograph; 
(8)	A full and complete criminal history listing any and all misdemeanor charges and/or convictions entered against the applicant during his lifetime, including the date, charge, court of record, disposition and any and all related and pertinent information regarding the same; 
(9)	Such other information as the City of Clanton shall find reasonably necessary to effectuate the general purpose of this ordinance and to make a fair determination of whether the terms of this ordinance have been complied with; 
(10)	The application required hereunder shall be accompanied by an application fee to be set an established by a vote of the Clanton City Council. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 3, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-464. - Investigation by chief of police or designated investigative agency. 
    Within thirty (30) days after receipt of an application as provided herein, the chief of police or other investigative agency designated by the City of Clanton shall cause an investigation to be made of the applicant and/or his proposed operation as well as an investigation of each employee of the applicant. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 4, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-465. - Standards for issuance of license. 
    The chief of police or investigative agency shall recommend to the City of Clanton that a license for a private investigator or private security guard shall be issued to the applicant when it finds: 
(1)	That the applicant is of good moral character;
(2)	That the applicant has never been convicted of any felony, or any crime of moral turpitude;
(3)	That the applicant is a natural born or fully naturalized citizen of the United States;
(4)	That the applicant does not believe in or advocate the overthrow of the government of the United States, or of the State of Alabama, by force or violence, and that the applicant is not a member of any organization or party which believes in or teaches directly or indirectly the overthrow of the government of the United States, or of the State of Alabama, by force or violence; 
(5)	That the issuance of a license to the applicant will not jeopardize the health, safety, welfare and morals of the City of Clanton and of the citizens thereof; 
(6)	That each proposed or actual employee of the applicant satisfies the foregoing requirements of subsection (e)(1) through (5); 
(7)	Any applicant intending to carry a firearm shall upon application present a proper permit for the possession and use of such firearm. Otherwise the person so licensed shall have not right to possess or use firearms. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 5, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-466. - Standards applicable to employees. 
    All employees of any person having or applying for a license hereunder shall meet the standards set forth above, and shall be subject to all regulations of this article. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 6, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-467. - Notice of rejection. 
    The City of Clanton shall act upon the application seeking a license hereunder within forty-five (45) days after the filing thereof. Upon the recommendation of the chief of police or other investigative agency designated by the city, and if the chief or investigative agency disapproves the application for a license, notice of the same shall be furnished the applicant within ten (10) days of the taking of said action. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 7, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-468. - Appeal procedure. 
    Any person aggrieved shall have the right to repeal the denial of any license provided for herein to the city council. The appeal shall be taken within thirty (30) days after notice thereof. The council shall act upon the appeal within thirty (30) days after its receipt. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 8, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-469. - License fee. 
    A license shall be issued to a successful applicant for private detective or private security guard license by the City of Clanton upon payment of a license fee of seventy-five dollars ($75.00) for one (1) to four (4) employees; one hundred twenty-five dollars ($125.00) for five (5) to ten (10) employees and one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) for more than ten (10) employees (the term "employee" in this section is intended to mean only those persons covered by this article). 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 9, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-470. - Conditions of licensing. 
(a)	Transferability. Licenses issued hereunder shall not be transferable. 
(b)	Revocation and suspension. Licenses issued hereunder shall be subject to revocation or suspension by the City of Clanton for violation or any of the provisions of this article or misconduct by the licensee or his employees, after reasonable notice and an opportunity to be heard has been given to the licensee. The chief of police shall immediately notify any licensee, by personal service, of such suspension or revocation. 
(c)	Renewal. The City of Clanton shall issue renewal licenses to all licensees whose licenses have not been suspended at the time said licenses have expired, upon payment of the license fee set our herein. 
(d)	Term of license. All licenses issued hereunder shall be for a term of one (1) year. 
(e)	Evidence of insurance required. No license shall be issued hereunder unless the applicant first files with the City of Clanton an evidence of liability insurance in full force and effect in the amount of not less than five hundred thousand dollars ($500,000.00), issued by an approved insurance company authorized to do business in the State of Alabama and conditioned upon the compliance by the applicant with all the terms and provisions of this article, as may be approved by the City of Clanton, and also conditioned upon the careful, faithful and honest conduct of the services to be performed by the applicant, or his or its employees hereunder. Said insurance relieving and holding the City of Clanton harmless against any liability in connection therewith and fully indemnifying the City of Clanton for the same. Before the license provided hereunder is issued, said insurance policy shall be approved by the City of Clanton as to form, execution and sufficiency. The insurance policy so issued shall provide that the issuing company shall notify the City of Clanton in the event of nonpayment of premium by the licensee, cancellation of the policy for any reason by the insurance company and that said insurance company will further furnish the City of Clanton with a copy of the policy issued in accord with the terms of this provision and that the same shall include a loss payable endorsement in favor of the City of Clanton. 
(1)	Protection to public. The insurance provided herein shall be taken in the name of the people of the State of Alabama, and every person injured by the negligent, willful, malicious or wrongful act of the principal, his agent, servant, or employee, in the conduct of business, may bring an action on the insurance in his own name to recover damages for such negligent, willful, malicious or wrongful act. 
(2)	Action by the city. The city and the city council thereof shall also have a right to bring an action on the insurance required for the negligent, willful, malicious or wrongful act of the principal, his agent, servant or employee, in the conduct of business of private detective. 
(3)	Suspension of license on failure of security. The City of Clanton shall suspend any license, upon the recommendation of the chief of police or the city attorney, when the insurance required herein shall have lapsed or is reduced by reason of a judgment thereon, or for any reason is no longer in force and effect. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 10, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-471. - Promulgation of regulations by the chief of police and the City of Clanton. 
    The chief of police and the City of Clanton shall have the authority to enact and enforce reasonable rules and regulations for the operation of private detectives and private security guards in the interest of public safety, morals and welfare, and to effectuate the general purpose of this article. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 11, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-472. - Duties of licensees. 
(a)	Carry and post license certificated. The licensees hereunder shall cause a certificate of such license to be displayed at all times in a conspicuous place in or on his place of business described in such license. The licensee shall carry on his person at all times when performing services as a private detective a certificate of the license issued hereunder. 
(b)	Impersonation of state police officers. No person licensed hereunder shall impersonate or hold himself out as a peace officer of this state or of this city; nor shall such person operate or permit to be operated a motor vehicle with a siren, blinker light, or with any insignia thereon bearing likeness to the insignia used by the peace officers of the State of Alabama, or of this city. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 12, 8-11-03) 
Sec. 10-473. - Penalty. 
    The penalty prescribed for violation of this ordinance shall be revocation of the license required herein. In addition, the licensee shall be liable for any and all penalties prescribed by the ordinances of this city for any violation of the City Code of the City of Clanton or of any criminal ordinance thereof. 
(Ord. No. 3-03, § 13, 8-11-03) 
Chapter 11 - MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Fire prevention and protection, Ch. 7; licenses and business regulations, Ch. 10; abandoned vehicles, § 13-101 et seq.; parades and demonstrations, Ch. 14; police, Ch. 16; streets and sidewalks, Ch. 18; taxicabs, § 10-291 et seq.; advertising on street from vehicle, § 18-3; off-street automobile storage, App. A, § 9(2). (Back)
State Law reference- Ordinances to provide for public safety, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-1; power of city to regulate the standing and running of trains, automobiles, etc., Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-47-114, 32-5-1; local traffic-control devices, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5-31; Alabama Rules of the Road Act, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-1 et seq.; uniform system of traffic-control devices, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-30; magistrates, uniform traffic infractions, Rules 18-20, Rules of Judicial Administration, Code of Ala. 1975, Vol. 23. (Back)
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 11-1. - Adoption of state law; violations. 
(a)	The laws of Alabama entitled Regulation of Operation of Motor Vehicles, Etc., Generally, Ch. 5, and the laws of Alabama entitled Rules of the Road, Ch. 5A, of Title 32 of the Code of Ala. 1975, are hereby adopted. 
(b)	In addition to subsection (a) and all provisions of law relating to the speed and operation of motor vehicles in the city, there are hereby adopted all laws of the state and all rules and regulations of the state highway department pertaining to the control of traffic and motor vehicles on highways that are misdemeanors under the state laws, and a violation of such laws, rules and regulations in the city or in the police jurisdiction thereof shall be violations of this chapter. 
(Code 1979, §§ 14-1, 14-12) 
Sec. 11-2. - Penalty. 
(a)	Except as provided in subsection (b) of this section, any person found to be in violation of section 11-1 shall be punished as provided in section 1-9 
(b)	Any person found to be in violation of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-191, as amended, shall, upon conviction, be punished by a fine of not more than five thousand dollars ($5,000.00) and may be imprisoned or sentenced to hard labor for not more than one (1) year. 
(Ord. No. 13-83, § 5, 8-8-83) 
Sec. 11-3. - Use of motor vehicle without consent of owner. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, without the consent, expressed or implied, of the owner, to use the motor vehicle of such owner on any public highway, street or avenue or elsewhere in the city. 
(Code 1979, § 14-8) 
Sec. 11-4. - Sitting in or tampering with vehicle of another. 
    Any person who, without the consent of the owner or person in charge of an automobile or other vehicle parked or left standing at or near any church, schoolhouse, on the streets, roads, avenues or public highways, in front of any private residence, or at any other public place, shall loiter or sit in the automobile or other vehicle, or blow the horn, turn the switch, put on the lights, or in any way meddle with the ways, works or machinery of the automobile or other vehicle, or who shall deface, scratch or mutilate the vehicle while the vehicle is left parked or standing at such place, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, on conviction, shall be fined not less than five dollars ($5.00) and not more than five hundred dollars ($500.00), and may also be imprisoned or sentenced to hard labor for the city for not more than six (6) months. 
(Code 1979, § 14-9) 
Sec. 11-5. - Loading or unloading of goods in street. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for the driver of any truck or van used for loading, unloading or delivery of goods, wares or merchandise to stop or park the truck or van in any traffic lane or public way in the city between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m. for the purpose of loading, unloading or making deliveries from the truck or van. 
(b)	Nothing in this section shall prevent any police officer of the city from authorizing such truck or van driver to stop or park in a traffic lane as described in this section, for the purpose of loading, unloading or delivery, when such loading, unloading or delivery cannot be accomplished otherwise. 
(Code 1979, § 14-13) 
Cross reference- Streets and sidewalks, Ch. 18. 
Sec. 11-6. - Vehicle weight limits. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to operate or cause to be operated any motor vehicle having a gross vehicular weight of five (5) tons or more on the following public thoroughfares within the corporate limits of the city: 
Ollie Avenue, from U.S. Highway No. 31 to the Lay Dam Highway. 
Thirteenth Street, from Second Avenue South to Kincheon Road. 
(b)	Proper signs shall be posted along such streets in such size and at such places so as to adequately inform the public of such gross vehicular weight limit. 
(Ord. No. 7-85, §§ 1, 2, 11-25-85) 
Sec. 11-7. - Use of restraining devices. 
    All operators or passengers of all motor vehicles, including automobiles, trucks and equipment owned by the city, shall use restraining devices, commonly referred to as seat belts, in the event that such motor vehicle, automobile, truck or equipment is equipped with such restraining devices or seat belts. 
(Ord. No. 1-92, § 1, 1-20-92) 
Editor's note- 
Ord. No. 1-92, § 1, adopted Jan. 20, 1992, not specifically amendatory of this Code, has been codified as § 11-7 at the discretion of the editor. 
Secs. 11-8-11-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PARKING 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 11-31. - Manner of parking at night. 
    Whenever a vehicle is parked or stopped on a street or avenue of the city, whether attended or unattended, during the period of time from one-half hour before sunset to one-half hour before sunrise, such vehicle shall be so parked or stopped as to leave open a space for travel upon the street or highway not less than eighteen (18) feet in width, such space to be at least nine (9) feet on each side of the center of the street or avenue. 
(Code 1979, § 14-18) 
Sec. 11-32. - Parking in designated areas of city parks. 
(a)	Definitions. As used in this section, the following terms shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them as follows: 
(1)	City park or park is defined as that area embraced within a city park where the public frequents or is invited and including the area where the athletic fields are located, the recreation area, swimming pool area, concession stands, and the area embraced within such city park. 
(2)	Motor vehicle is defined as a self-propelled vehicle, including automobile, truck, motorcycle, motor bike or like vehicle. 
(b)	Prohibition. It shall be unlawful for the operator of a motor vehicle, as defined in this section, to park or leave standing, either attended or unattended, any motor vehicle in any area of such park where parking is prohibited or to park or leave standing such vehicle in an area designated as a no parking area. 
(c)	Presumption of violation. The operator of any motor vehicle, upon being ordered to remove a vehicle improperly parked, and who fails or refuses to immediately do so, is presumed to be in violation of this section. 
(d)	Penalty. Any person found to be in violation of this section shall, upon conviction, be punished by the payment of a fine of not more than fifty dollars ($50.00) and imprisoned or sentenced to hard labor for the city for a period not exceeding thirty (30) days, one or both, at the discretion of the court trying the case. 
(Ord. No. 15-96, §§ 1-3, 5, 11-6-96) 
Secs. 11-33-11-40. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - RESTRICTED PARKING ZONES 

Sec. 11-41. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Operator means every individual who operates a vehicle as the owner thereof, or as the agent, employee or permittee of the owner, or who is in actual physical control of the vehicle. 
    Park or parking means the standing of a vehicle, whether or not upon a street, otherwise than in obedience to traffic regulations, signs or signals, or an involuntary stopping of the vehicle by reason of causes beyond the control of the operator of the vehicle. 
    Parking space means any space which is duly designated for the parking of a single vehicle by lines painted, or otherwise durably marked, on the curb or on the surface of the street adjacent to or adjoining the curb or sidewalk, and shall include that area designated for angular parking as well as that area designated for parallel parking. 
    Street means any public street, avenue, road, alley, highway, lane or path, or other public place located in the city and established for the use of vehicles. 
    Vehicle means any device in, upon, or by which any person or property is or may be transported upon a street or highway, except a device which is operated upon rails or tracks. 
(Ord. No. 5-84, § 1, 4-23-84) 
Sec. 11-42. - Interpretation of division. 
    This division shall be deemed and construed to be an exercise of the police power of the city for the preservation of public safety and all of its provisions shall be liberally construed with a view of the effectuation of such purpose. 
(Ord. No. 5-84, § 8, 4-23-84) 
Sec. 11-43. - Enforcement of division. 
(a)	It shall be the duty of the chief of police and the police officers of the city, or any person named or designated by the mayor and city council, to check the parking spaces within the restricted parking zones established in this division, and, by the employment of some mark or chalk or other device, to determine whether a vehicle parked within the restricted parking zone has been permitted by the person or the operator thereof to remain standing or parked in the restricted area in excess of two (2) hours on the days and within the hours when such parking restriction is in effect, in violation of this division. Such violation shall be subject to the penalties provided in this division. 
(b)	The chief of police, the police officers, and other persons named or designated by the mayor and city council shall make or cause to be made records or reports of the vehicles parked in violation of the provisions of this division, the name of the owner and operator of such vehicle, if known, the make and state license tag number of such vehicle, and the location of the vehicle in violation, and any other facts necessary to a thorough understanding of the circumstances attending such violation. 
(c)	There shall be attached to such vehicle, in a conspicuous place, a notice of the parking violation sufficient to inform the owner or operator of the vehicle that the vehicle has been parked in violation of this division and the time of the violation, and instructing the owner or operator thereof to report at a certain designated time and place to the municipal court of the city in regard to such violation. 
(Ord. No. 5-84, § 6, 4-23-84) 
Sec. 11-44. - Penalty; payment of fine. 
(a)	Any person or operator of a motor vehicle who violates or fails to comply with any of the terms of this division shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(b)	Any person or operator of any motor vehicle who causes or permits a motor vehicle to remain parked in any such parking space beyond the parking time of two (2) hours shall be considered as parking overtime and beyond the period of legal parking time and such parking shall be deemed a violation of this division. 
(c)	For each violation of this division, the person or operator of the motor vehicle is hereby assessed a fine of five dollars ($5.00), provided that the fine is paid within seven (7) days of the time of the violation as shown on the parking ticket. If the fine is not paid within the period of seven (7) days from the violation, there is hereby assessed a fine of ten dollars ($10.00), provided that the fine is paid within the period of fourteen (14) days of the time of the parking ticket. 
(d)	Any person or operator who shall violate or fail to comply with any of the terms of this division or who shall conceal, aid or abet any such violation or fail to comply with this division, or who fails or refuses to pay the fine as provided in this section within fourteen (14) days from the time of the parking ticket, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished by a fine of not more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) or by imprisonment in the city jail for a period not to exceed three (3) months, either or both penalties to be imposed by the court trying the case. 
(e)	The fine imposed by this section shall be paid to the municipal court clerk, or the person designated by that office to receive the fines, at the city hall or other building of the city. 
(Ord. No. 5-84, § 7, 4-23-84) 
Sec. 11-45. - Zones established. 
    The following streets and avenues and areas or portions of streets lying within the corporate limits of the city shall constitute the restricted parking zones: 
Fifth Street, between Third Avenue North and First Avenue. 
Second Avenue North, between Eighth Street and Fifth Street. 
Seventh Street, between Fourth Avenue North and First Avenue. 
Sixth Street, between Fourth Avenue North and First Avenue. 
(Ord. No. 5-84, § 2, 4-23-84) 
Sec. 11-46. - Marking of spaces; manner of parking. 
    The superintendent of streets or such other employees of the city as may be designated under the jurisdiction of the mayor and city council are hereby directed and authorized to mark off individual parking spaces in the restricted parking zones established in this division, the parking spaces to be designated by lines painted or durably marked on the curbing or surface of the street. At each space so marked, it shall be unlawful to park any vehicle in such a way that the vehicle is not entirely within the lines designating the parking space. 
(Ord. No. 5-84, § 3, 4-23-84) 
Sec. 11-47. - Parking time limit. 
(a)	No vehicle, except in a period of emergency determined by an officer of the police department or of the fire department or in compliance with the directions of a police officer or traffic-control signal or sign, shall be parked or left standing in any parking space in the restricted parking zones established in this division for a period of time in excess of two (2) hours during the hours set out in this section, except on Sundays and holidays. 
(b)	This section shall be in effect between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 4:00 p.m. each day except Sunday and holidays. Holidays as used in this section means the holidays that the city generally observes. 
(c)	If any vehicle shall remain parked in any such parking space beyond the period of two (2) hours, the parking time of the vehicle shall be considered as parking overtime and beyond the period of legal parking time and such parking shall be deemed a violation of this division. 
(d)	Each person or operator of any vehicle permitted to remain parked in any such parking space beyond the parking time set out for such parking shall be deemed a violator of this division. 
(Ord. No. 5-84, § 5, 4-23-84) 
Sec. 11-48. - Loading zones. 
    The superintendent of streets or such other employees of the city as may be designated under the jurisdiction of the mayor and city council are hereby directed and authorized to mark off loading zones as may from time to time be designated by the mayor and city council within the restricted parking zones established in this division, in such locations as in the opinion of the mayor and city council will serve the general public. 
(Ord. No. 5-84, § 4, 4-23-84) 
Secs. 11-49-11-70. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - SPEED LIMITS 

Sec. 11-71. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Operator means every individual who operates a vehicle as the owner thereof, or as the agent, servant, employee or permittee of the owner, or who is in actual physical control of the vehicle. 
    School zone means a street, avenue, highway or other public way in close proximity to a public or private school, where in close proximity to the school, where the students or school personnel are using the street, avenue or other public way, and the location where students and school personnel are entering and leaving school buses. 
    Street means any public street, avenue, road, alley, highway or other public place located in the city and established for the use of vehicles. 
    Vehicle means any device in, upon, or by which any person or property is or may be transported upon a street or highway, including motor vehicles, passenger vehicles, pickups or pickup trucks or trucks. 
(Ord. No. 16-86, § 1, 11-10-86) 
Sec. 11-72. - Compliance with article. 
(a)	The city council has determined and does hereby declare a reasonable and safe maximum speed within the corporate limits of the city and the police jurisdiction thereof as provided in this article. 
(b)	No person shall operate a vehicle within the corporate limits of the city or the police jurisdiction thereof at a speed greater than designated in this article within the area designated. 
(Ord. No. 16-86, §§ 2, 5, 11-10-86) 
Sec. 11-73. - School zones. 
    No person shall operate a vehicle in a school zone during the days of Monday through Friday or any other day when school is in session and between the hours of 7:30 a.m. and 8:15 a.m. and 2:30 p.m. and 3:15 p.m. in excess of the speed and in the areas as follows: 
Twenty miles per hour: 
Lake Mitchell Road, which runs east and west, beginning at the intersection of First Street, east a distance of 0.2 mile. 
Temple Road, which runs east and west, between the intersection of U.S. 31 and Thrash Road, a distance of 0.5 mile. 
Thirty-five miles per hour: 
U.S. Highway No. 31, which runs north and south, between the intersection of Poplar Springs Road and Newport Avenue, a distance of 0.5 mile. 
(Ord. No. 16-86, § 4, 11-10-86) 
Sec. 11-74. - Twenty-five miles per hour zones. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than twenty-five (25) miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
Alabama Highway No. 22, beginning at Ninth Street (Enterprise Road) (m.p. 67.95), thence easterly along Alabama Highway No. 22 to U.S. Highway No. 31 (Alabama Highway No. 3) (m.p. 68.15) a distance of 0.20 miles. 
Alabama Highway No. 145, beginning at U.S. Highway No. 31 (Alabama Highway No. 3) (m.p. 0.00), thence northerly along Alabama Highway No. 145 to a point 250 feet north of First Street (right) (m.p. 0.50), a distance of 0.50 miles. 
U.S. Highway No. 31 (Alabama Highway No. 3), beginning at Jackson Avenue (m.p. 222.00), thence northerly along U.S. Highway No. 31 (Alabama Highway No. 3) to Glenview Avenue (right) (m.p. 222.50), a distance of 0.50 miles. 
(Code 1979, § 14-32; Ord. No. 1-95, § IV, 1-9-95; Ord. No. 6-95, § V, 4-24-95)

(Ord. No. 16-86, § 5, 11-10-86)

    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than thirty-five (35) miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
Alabama Highway No. 22, beginning at Eleventh Street North (m.p. 67.80), thence easterly along Alabama Highway No. 22 to Ninth Street (Enterprise Road) (m.p. 67.95) a distance of 0.15 miles. 
Alabama Highway No. 145, from the intersection of Alabama Highway No. 145 and Fifth Street east to the intersection of Alabama Highway No. 145 and First Street, a distance of 0.27 mile. 
Alabama Highway No. 145, beginning at a point 200 feet north of First Street (right) (m.p. 0.50), thence northerly along Alabama Highway No. 145 to a point 250 feet south of Goosepond Creek (m.p. 0.65) a distance of 0.15 miles.

(Code 1979, § 14-31; Ord. No. 16-86, § 5, 11-10-86; Ord. No. 1-95, § III, 1-9-95; Ord. No. 6-95, § VI, 4-24-95) 
Sec. 11-76.5. - Forty miles per hour zones. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than forty (40) miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city:

(Ord. No. 6-95, § III, 4-24-95)

(Code 1979, § 14-30; Ord. No. 16-86, § 5, 11-10-86; Ord. No. 1-95, § II, 1-9-95; Ord. No. 6-95, § II, 4-24-95; Ord. No. 7-02, 10-28-02) 
Sec. 11-78. - Fifty-five miles per hour zones. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than fifty-five (55) miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
Alabama Highway No. 22, beginning at the west city limits (m.p. 65.30), thence easterly along Alabama Highway No. 22 to a point 250 feet west of Chilton County Highway No. 53 (Tom Littlejohn Road) (left) (m.p. 66.60), a distance of 1.30 miles. 
Alabama Highway No. 145, beginning at a point 250 feet north of Chilton County Highway No. 51 (Friendship Road) (left) (Pinedale Road) (right) (m.p. 1.70), thence northerly along Alabama Highway No. 145 to the north city limits (m.p. 3.65), a distance of 1.95 miles. 
U.S. Highway No. 31 (Alabama Highway No. 3), beginning at the south city limits (m.p. 217.40), thence northerly along U.S. Highway No. 31 (Alabama Highway No. 3), to a point 528 feet south of Chilton County Highway No. 7 (left) (m.p. 219.75), a distance of 2.35 miles. 
U.S. Highway No. 31 (Alabama Highway No. 3), beginning at Chilton County Highway No. 51 (Blacksnake Road) (right) (Sims Drive) (left) (m.p. 223.70), thence northerly along U.S. Highway No. 31 (Alabama Highway No. 3) to the north city limits (m.p. 225.70), a distance of 2.00 miles. 
(Code 1979, § 14-29; Ord. No. 1-95, § I, 1-9-95; Ord. No. 6-95, § I, 4-24-95) 
Sec. 11-79. - Penalty for violation. 
    Any person or persons violating this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished for such violation by a fine not exceeding two hundred dollars ($200.00) and may also be imprisoned and sentenced to hard labor upon the streets or public works or in the workhouse or house of corrections of the city not exceeding six (6) months. 
(Ord. No. 1-95, § VII, 1-9-95) 
Sec. 11-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - SALE OF VEHICLES; REGULATIONS 

Sec. 11-81. - Display for sale upon occupied property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to display for sale more than one vehicle, recreational vehicle, ATV, boat, Sea-Do, four wheeler or motorcycle upon any occupied lot or parcel of real property within the city. 
(Ord. No. 16-99, § 1, 6-28-99) 
Sec. 11-82. - Display for sale upon property of another. 
    It shall be unlawful for any owner, tenant or person in charge of premises to display for sale upon such premises, or permit same to be done; of any vehicle, recreational vehicle, ATV, boat, Sea-Do, four wheeler or motorcycle not owned by said owner, tenant or person in charge. 
(Ord. No. 16-99, § 1, 6-28-99) 
Sec. 11-83. - Display for sale on public property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to display any vehicle, recreational vehicle, ATV, boat, Sea-Do, four wheeler or motorcycle for sale upon the public right-of-way or other public property within the city. In addition to the penalties provided herein, any vehicle found to be in violation of this section may be towed away and impounded at the owner's expense, with the towing service being responsible for the protection of the vehicle from deterioration. 
(Ord. No. 16-99, § 1, 6-28-99) 
Sec. 11-84. - Display for sale upon unoccupied property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to display for sale any vehicle, recreational vehicle, ATV, boats, Sea-Do, four wheeler, or motorcycle upon any vacant lot or parcel of real property within the city. 
(Ord. No. 16-99, § 1, 6-28-99) 
Sec. 11-85. - Exemption. 
    The foregoing, except section 11-83, shall not apply to any person properly licensed to engage in the business of selling vehicles, recreational vehicles, ATVs, boats, Sea-Dos, four wheelers, or motorcycles at the location designated upon such license. 
(Ord. No. 16-99, § 1, 6-28-99) 
Sec. 11-86. - Penalty. 
    The penalty for violation of any provision herein shall be as specified for general penalty under section 1-9 of this Code, or by a schedule of fines established by resolution of the city council. Each day a violation is permitted to occur constitutes a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 16-99, § 1, 6-28-99) 
Chapter 12 - MUNICIPAL COURT

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 12-1. - Time and place of holding court. 
    The municipal court of the city shall hold court at such time and place as the city council may determine with the advice of the municipal judge. 
(Code 1979, § 10-3) 
Sec. 12-2. - Powers of court; court costs. 
(a)	The municipal judge shall have the authority to punish any person convicted of violating any municipal ordinance as provided in section 1-9 
(b)	Upon each conviction in municipal court for a violation of any ordinance of the city, there shall be taxed against the defendant as court costs the sum of ten dollars ($10.00), and there shall also be taxed as costs the additional costs and fees imposed by the statutes of the state, and the latter such costs and fees shall be remitted pursuant to the state statutes. All costs taxed for the city as provided in this section shall be paid into the city treasury. 
(Code 1979, § 10-6) 
State law reference- Powers of municipal court, Code of Ala. 1975, § 12-14-10 et seq.; court costs, Code of Ala. 1975, § 12-14-14. 
Sec. 12-3. - Appointment, term of judge. 
(a)	There shall be one (1) municipal judge. The judge shall be appointed for a term of two (2) years. The municipal judge shall be eligible for reappointment upon the expiration of his term. 
(b)	Any person appointed to the office of municipal judge shall be eligible to serve two (2) years from the date appointed. 
(Code 1979, § 10-4) 
Sec. 12-4. - Compensation of judge. 
    The annual salary of the municipal judge shall be payable in twelve (12) equal monthly installments. 
(Code 1979, § 10-5) 
Sec. 12-5. - Reports by judge. 
(a)	The municipal judge shall report on the proceedings of the municipal court as required by law or rule. 
(b)	The municipal judge shall be required to make a report to the council on the operation of the municipal court every month. 
(Code 1979, §§ 10-12, 10-13) 
Sec. 12-6. - Magistrates. 
    The municipal court magistrates shall be selected as follows: 
(1)	The clerk of the municipal court and any person within the clerk's office designated by the state administrative director of courts (ADC), upon written recommendation of the clerk to serve as magistrate; and 
(2)	All persons appointed to serve as magistrates by the ADC upon the written recommendation of the municipal judge. 
(Code 1979, § 10-10)

Sec. 12-8. - Municipal corrections fund established. 
    In accord with the authority contained in Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-7.1, as last amended, a municipal corrections fund cost shall be added, on conviction, to the fines and court costs being presently collected in all traffic cases in the total amount of forty-four dollars and fifty cents ($44.50) and in all non-traffic misdemeanor cases in the total amount of forty-four dollars ($44.00) per case, all as collected in the municipal court in the City of Clanton, Alabama. 
(Ord. No. 5-10, 4-26-2010; Ord. No. 1-11, 5-23-2011) 
Editor's note- 
Ord. No. 5-10, adopted April 26, 2010, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, inclusion herein as § 12-8 was at the discretion of the editor. 
Sec. 12-9. - Fees established for failure to appear at court. 
    Having determined that failure to appear at court is causing a burden on the municipal court, the City Council of the City of Clanton has established a fee of one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) for each traffic violation and two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) for each non-traffic, municipal and misdemeanor violation for which the defendant fails to appear at court. 
    The city council has also determined that failure to appear at court has placed an additional burden on the Clanton Municipal Court and Clanton Police Department by, at times, having to travel out of Chilton County to transport those whom have failed to appear at court. Hence, the city council hereby adopts a transportation fee as established by the State of Alabama and the administrative office of courts. 
    The magistrate shall add these charges to the fine and court cost upon conviction, and said monies will be deposited into the general funds for the City of Clanton, Alabama. 
(Ord. No. 4-10, 4-26-2010) 
Editor's note- 
Ord. No. 4-10, adopted April 26, 2010, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, inclusion herein as § 12-9 was at the discretion of the editor. 
Sec. 12-10. - Fee established for housing and medical expenses of prisoners in county jail. 
    The city council has determined that the housing of inmates in the Chilton County Jail and the inmate medical expenses are causing a financial burden on the city. To offset these costs, the city council has established a fee of twenty dollars ($20.00) per day, not to exceed two hundred dollars ($200.00), plus all medical expenses incurred while the prisoner is incarcerated in the Chilton County Jail. The magistrate shall add these charges to the fine and court cost upon conviction. 
(Ord. No. 3-10, 4-26-2010) 
Editor's note- 
Ord. No. 3-10, adopted April 26, 2010, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, inclusion herein as § 12-10 was at the discretion of the editor. 
Secs. 12-11-12-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - TRAFFIC SAFETY/EDUCATIONAL PROGRAMS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 4-12, adopted March 12, 2012, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, inclusion herein as Art. II, §§ 12-21-12-26, was at the editor's discretion. 
Sec. 12-21. - Alcohol abuse educational program established. 
    There is hereby established an alcohol abuse educational program to be hereby known as "MADD Alabama Victim Impact Panels and Minor in Possession Classes" which shall [be] under the supervision of the Clanton Municipal Court Clerk and/or the Clanton Municipal Probation Officers. Each person attending the class shall not be charged more than seventy-five dollars ($75.00), for evaluation, registration, and cost of the class. Such fees are to be assessed by the municipal court judge as appropriate, unless the same is waived by the municipal court judge or by the clerk of the municipal court in such cases where the individual is being referred by an outside agency. 
(Ord. No. 4-12, 3-12-2012) 
Sec. 12-22. - Traffic safety educational program established. 
    There is hereby established a traffic safety educational program which shall be under the supervision of the municipal court clerk and/or the Clanton Municipal Court Probation Officers. Each person attending the seminar shall be charged no more than one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) for registration, evaluation, and cost of the class. Such fees are to be assessed by the municipal court judge, unless the same is waived by the municipal court judge or by the clerk of the court in such cases where the individual is being referred by an outside agency. 
(Ord. No. 4-12, 3-12-2012) 
Sec. 12-23. - Advisory committee established. 
    There is established an advisory committee consisting of the chief of police or his/her designee, the municipal court judge or his/her designee, and the municipal court clerk and his/her designee. 
(Ord. No. 4-12, 3-12-2012) 
Sec. 12-24. - Administrative duties. 
    The clerk of the court or the municipal court probation officers will be responsible for scheduling such classes, instructors, facilitators and setting reasonable fees for payment of the instructors or facilitators. The clerk of the court shall establish such rules for these classes as approved by the municipal court judge. 
(Ord. No. 4-12, 3-12-2012) 
Sec. 12-25. - Payment of fees. 
    All monies shall be collected by the clerk of the court in advance of such classes. All monies will be turned into the Chief Financial Officer of the City of Clanton to be maintained in a separate account to be used to defray the cost of such classes, purchase supplies for such classes, purchase equipment for such classes, pay outside instructors/facilitators, to provide other traffic safety programs, and to purchase other traffic safety equipment to be utilized throughout the City of Clanton as relates to traffic safety. The collection of monies will be under the supervision of the Clanton Municipal Court Clerk. 
(Ord. No. 4-12, 3-12-2012)

Chapter 13 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Animals, Ch. 4; fire prevention and protection, Ch. 7; flood damage prevention, Ch. 8; housing, Ch. 9; fire-related offenses, § 7-5 et seq.; gambling in billiard rooms, § 10-261. (Back)
State Law reference- General municipal police powers, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-110 et seq.; Alabama Criminal Code, Code of Ala. 1975, Title 13A. (Back)
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 13-1. - Injuring or trapping animals protected by law. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to injure, kill, take, catch, capture or to attempt to injure, take, kill or capture any squirrel, mockingbird, brown thrush, catbird, redbird, bluebird, or any other bird protected by the laws of the state or of the United States, within the city. 
(Code 1979, § 9-10) 
Cross reference- Animals, Ch. 4. 
State law reference- Hunting and trapping of birds, Code of Ala. 1975, § 9-11-230 et seq. 
Sec. 13-2. - Discharge of firearms. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to shoot or discharge any shotgun, pistol, rifle or other firearm in the city. 
(Code 1979, § 9-11) 
Sec. 13-3. - Discharge of air guns, pellet guns. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person within the corporate limits of the city or the police jurisdiction thereof to fire, shoot or discharge or cause to be fired, shot or discharged any air gun, air rifle, pellet gun or any pneumatic gun which discharges shot, bullets, missiles or pellets by means of the elastic force of compressed air or a spring, appliance, apparatus or other device. 
(Code 1979, § 9-13) 
Sec. 13-4. - Operation of firing ranges for training of law enforcement officers. 
    Notwithstanding sections 13-2 and 13-3, federal, state, county or municipal law enforcement officers or organizations under the direct control of such federal, state, county or municipal law enforcement officers may operate, construct or maintain a firing range or other like facilities for training in the use of firearms or in the discharge of shotguns, pistols, rifles, air guns, air rifles, pellet guns or pneumatic guns within the corporate limits or within the police jurisdiction of the city. 
(Ord. No. 5-83, § 1, 4-11-83) 
Sec. 13-5. - Posting of advertisements. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to post or paste or otherwise attach any signboard, bill, advertisement or other paper: 
(1)	Upon a pole erected by any telegraph, telephone, electric light or power company;
(2)	To fire alarm poles;
(3)	To any tree growing on any street in the city; or
(4)	To any fixed object on city-owned property.
(Code 1979, § 9-18) 
Cross reference- Licenses and business regulations, Ch. 10. 
Sec. 13-6. - Throwing harmful material on streets. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to throw, deposit or leave, in any public street, bottles, fragments of glass, tacks, nails or other things likely to injure persons or vehicles passing along the street. 
(Code 1979, § 9-20) 
Cross reference- Streets and sidewalks, Ch. 18. 
State law reference- Criminal littering, Code of Ala. 1975, § 13A-7-29. 
Sec. 13-7. - Insurance, permit for use of high-pressure boilers. 
    Each and every person, before operating, using or maintaining any high-pressure steam boiler or other high-pressure boiler carrying more than fifteen (15) pounds of pressure or capable of carrying more than fifteen (15) pounds of pressure, shall first procure on the boiler a standard policy of insurance in the sum of not less than one thousand dollars ($1,000.00), payable to the person using or operating the boiler, and conditioned to indemnify any person against loss by accident on account of the use, maintenance or operation of the boiler, in a form approved by the city clerk. Every person, before using, maintaining or operating any boiler described in this section, shall first present the policy of insurance provided for in this section to the city clerk, and if found by the clerk to be sufficient as provided in this section, the city clerk shall then issue a permit for the use, operation and maintenance of the boiler for a period not exceeding the expiration date of the policy of insurance. The applicant shall pay the city clerk one dollar ($1.00) for the application. 
(Code 1979, § 9-25) 
Sec. 13-8. - Failure to return library property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully retain or fail to return any book, periodical, magazine, pamphlet, manuscript or other property belonging to or on deposit with the city public library, for a period exceeding thirty (30) days after notification by certified mail, return receipt requested, for delivery to addressee only, with the return card showing receipt of the notice or the refusal of the notice by the addressee, addressed to the last known borrower, the notification being given after the expiration time during which, by the rules of the library, such article or other property may legally be kept. The notice shall contain a copy of this section. 
(Code 1979, § 9-31) 
Sec. 13-9. - Giving false information for purpose of obtaining refund. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to give any false information to obtain or as a part of any attempt to obtain a refund for merchandise returned to a business establishment when such false information is calculated to induce such business establishment to give a refund which would otherwise not be given. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for any person to give a false or fictitious name or address as his own, or to give the name or address of any other person without that person's knowledge and approval, for the purpose of obtaining or attempting to obtain a refund on a ticket or other document which is evidence of a service purchased from a business establishment, which service is yet to be performed. 
(Ord. No. 5-87, §§ 1, 2, 3-23-87) 
Sec. 13-10. - Fireworks-Defined. 
    For the purpose of section 13-11, the term "fireworks" means any explosive composition or any substances or combination of substances, or any article prepared for the purpose of producing an audible effect by explosion, deflagration or detonation, and shall include blank cartridges, toy cannons, in which explosives are used, the type of balloons which require fire underneath to propel the balloons, firecrackers, sparklers, torpedoes, sky rockets, Roman candles, bombs, or other devices containing any explosive substances; provided, however, that the term "fireworks" shall not include pistol caps containing twenty-five-hundredths grains or less of explosive compound, toy pistols, toy canes, toy guns, or other devices in which paper caps containing twenty-five-hundredths grains or less of explosive compound are used, providing they are so constructed that the hand cannot come in contact with the cap when in place for the explosion. 
(Code 1979, § 9-15) 
Cross reference- Fire prevention and protection, Ch. 7. 
Sec. 13-11. - Same-Selling, possessing, discharging prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or offer for sale, possess or discharge any fireworks, as defined in section 13-10 within the corporate limits, or police jurisdiction of the city. 
(Code 1979, § 9-16) 
Sec. 13-12. - Discharge of firearms. 
(a)	Permitted discharge. It shall be legal to discharge a firearm commonly referred to as a shotgun in the corporate limits of the city during the period of time designated on an annual basis for the hunting of doves by the state department of conservation in the county, except as hereinafter provided in this section. 
(b)	Permitted hours. The hours for legal hunting of doves shall be prescribed by the state department of conservation for the hunting of doves in the county. 
(c)	Prohibited discharge. It is provided, however, that it shall be illegal to discharge a firearm commonly referred to as a shotgun within three hundred (300) feet of a currently inhabited dwelling house. 
(d)	Size of shot allowed. In the discharge of shotguns as provided in this section, no shot larger than number seven (7) size shall be allowed. 
(e)	Application required. Each landowner, before shooting is allowed over his property, shall first make written application filed with the chief of police of the city, stating the date and hours of the proposed hunt, the estimated number of hunters, and the application must be made not less than twenty-four (24) hours prior to the hunt. The chief of police is directed, before such hunt is authorized, to make an investigation and inspection of the premises, and if the chief of police then determines that the area of land is suitable, he may then issue the necessary permit in writing. 
(f)	Abuse of permit. During any hunt permitted by this section, if the chief of police determines that the permit authorized herein is being abused, the chief of police may, in his discretion, revoke such permit and terminate the hunt. 
(g)	Conflict with other rules. Nothing in this section shall be construed to be in conflict with any rules or regulations promulgated by the state department of conservation or any federal hunting rules or regulations. It is not the intent of this section to be in conflict with any hunting rules or regulations promulgated by the state or the federal government. 
(h)	Penalty for violation. Any person in violation of any provision of this section, on conviction, shall be punished as provided in section 1-9 of this Code. 
(Ord. No. 11-92, §§ 1-7, 10-12-92) 
Sec. 13-13. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- 
Ord. No. 2-07, §§ 1-13, adopted January 22, 2007, set out provisions pertaining to noise control. At the discretion of the editor, § 13-13, which pertained to loud or excessive noise and derived from Ord. No. 3-93, §§ I-III, 2-22-93, has been reserved and the users' attention is directed to Art. VI, §§ 13-151 et seq. of this chapter. 
Secs. 13-14-13-35. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - STATE OFFENSES 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 6-96, §§ 1-5, adopted Apr. 22, 1996, amended this article in its entirety, in effect repealing former §§ 13-36 and 13-37 and enacting similar new provisions in lieu thereof as herein set out. Formerly, such sections derived from Ord. No. 13-83, §§ 1-4, adopted Aug. 8, 1983. 
Sec. 13-36. - Offenses. 
(a)	Any person or corporation committing an offense within the corporate limits of the city or within the police jurisdiction thereof, which is declared by a law or laws of the state now existing or hereafter enacted to be a misdemeanor, shall be guilty of an offense against the city. 
(b)	Any person or corporation committing an offense within the corporate limits of the city or within the police jurisdiction thereof, which is declared by a law or laws of the state now existing or hereafter enacted to be a violation, shall be guilty of an offense against the city. 
(c)	Any person or corporation committing, within the corporate limits of the city or within the police jurisdiction thereof, an offense as defined by Section 13A-1-2 of the Alabama Criminal Code, which offense is not declared by a law or laws of the state now existing or hereafter enacted to be a felony, misdemeanor or violation, shall be guilty of an offense against the city. 
(Ord. No. 6-96, §§ 1-3, 4-22-96) 
Sec. 13-37. - Penalties for violation. 
(a)	Any person found to be in violation of section 13-36 shall, upon conviction, be punished by a fine of not less than one dollar ($1.00) nor more than five hundred dollars ($500.00) and/or may be imprisoned or sentenced to hard labor for the city for a period not exceeding six (6) months, at the discretion of the court trying the case, unless otherwise provided by subsection (b) of this section. Any corporation found to be in violation of section 13-36 shall, upon conviction, be punished by a fine of not less than one dollar ($1.00) nor more than five hundred dollars ($500.00), at the discretion of the court trying the case. 
(b)	Any person found to be in violation of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-191, as amended, shall, upon conviction, be punished by a fine of not less than five hundred dollars ($500.00) and not more than ten thousand dollars ($10,000.00) and may be imprisoned or sentenced to hard labor for not more than one (1) year. This subsection specifically adopts the provisions of Act No. 95-784 approved August 9, 1995. 
(Ord. No. 6-96, §§ 4, 5, 4-22-96) 
Secs. 13-38-13-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PUBLIC NUISANCES 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference- Abatement of nuisances under zoning ordinance, App. A, § 9(12). (Back)
State Law reference- Action to abate or enjoin public nuisance, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 6-5-122, 11-47-118; abatement of nuisances generally, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-117. (Back)
Sec. 13-61. - Interpretation of article. 
    This article shall not be construed to repeal, amend or otherwise alter any other ordinance of the city, and nothing contained in this article shall be construed, interpreted or taken to limit the city in its rights to proceed by injunction or other civil remedy against any person who causes, creates or maintains a public nuisance within the corporate limits of the city. 
(Code 1979, § 9-36) 
Sec. 13-62. - Continuing violations. 
    Each day's or part of a day's continuance of anything prohibited by this article shall be a separate offense. 
(Code 1979, § 9-35) 
Sec. 13-63. - Public nuisance defined; nuisances enumerated. 
(a)	The causing, creating or maintaining of a public nuisance, as prohibited under this article, shall be interpreted and construed according to the definition of a "public nuisance" as that term is defined or understood according to the common law and statutory law in force and effect in the state. 
(b)	Without affecting or limiting the generality of subsection (a) of this section or the meaning of the term "nuisance" as used in this article, it is hereby declared that all of the following are public nuisances within the meaning of this article: 
(1)	Any unsightly building, billboard or other structure, any old, abandoned or partially destroyed building or structure, any building or structure commenced and left unfinished, any building or structure which has been deemed to be unsuitable or unfit for human occupancy or habitation by any duly constituted official of the state department of health or the county department of health, any building which has been deemed by the building inspector of the city to fail to comply with the minimum building codes in force and effect in the city, or any abandoned well or excavation not properly protected and which may attract children and endanger them in the course of play. 
(2)	Accumulations of manure or rubbish which are breeding places for flies, mosquitoes, mice, rats or other vermin. 
(3)	Filthy, littered or trash-covered cellars, house yards, factory yards, vacant areas in the rear of stores, vacant lots, houses, buildings or premises containing trash, litter, rags, accumulations of empty barrels, boxes, crates, packing cases, paper, lumber or firewood not neatly piled, scrap iron, tin and other metal not neatly piled, or anything whatsoever in which flies or rats may breed or multiply or which may be a fire danger. 
(4)	Allowing diseased animals to run at large, allowing stagnant pools of water to accumulate, or maintaining a privy or outdoor closet where connections to a sanitary sewer are available. 
(Code 1979, § 9-34) 
Cross reference- Animals, Ch. 4; fire prevention and protection, Ch. 7. 
State law reference- Distinction between public and private nuisances, Code of Ala. 1975, § 6-5-121. 
Sec. 13-64. - Creation, maintenance prohibited. 
(a)	Every person who causes, creates or maintains a public nuisance within the corporate limits of the city shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(b)	The continued maintenance of such nuisance, once created or caused, shall be interpreted and construed to be a separate offense which shall be punishable under this section. 
(Code 1979, § 9-33) 
Secs. 13-65-13-100. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - ABANDONED VEHICLES; GRASS, WEED AND BUILDING NUISANCES 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2-03, adopted June 23, 2003 was not specifically amendatory of the Code and has been treated as superceding the provisions of former art. IV entitled abandoned vehicles. See the Code Comparative Table for a detailed analysis of repeal and inclusion. 
Cross reference- Motor vehicles and traffic, ch. 11; police, ch. 16; streets and sidewalks, ch. 18. (Back)
Sec. 13-101. - Definitions. 
    For the purpose of this article, certain terms as defined as follows: 
    Abandoned vehicles: Any motor vehicle which; 
(1)	Is in a wrecked, dismantled, partially dismantled, discarded or otherwise inoperable condition; or 
(2)	Does not have affixed thereto an unexpired license plate, and has been parked, stored or left, whether attended or not, upon any public or private property in the city for a period of time in excess of seven (7) days. 
    The term includes any boat which is in a wrecked, dismantled, partially dismantled, discarded or otherwise inoperable condition. The term does not include any motor vehicle: 
(1)	Enclosed within a building on private property;
(2)	Held in connection with a business enterprise, lawfully licensed by the city on property zoned for a junkyard, vehicle repair facility or a temporary storage facility for repairs not to exceed thirty (30) days; 
(3)	In operable condition specifically adapted or designed for operation on drag strips or raceways; or 
(4)	Retained primarily as an antique collector's item and registered under state law as an antique vehicle. 
    Building nuisance: Any nuisance condition involving a residential or nonresidential structure, including remains from demolition, remains from fire, parts of buildings, part of uninhabitable structures. 
    Enforcing official: Any official of the city police department or any other city employee designated by the mayor as the person to exercise the authority and perform the duties delegated by this article to the enforcing official. For a grass and weed nuisance the enforcing officials may also be any organization (including its employees) or individual with which the city may contact to provide such service. 
    Grass or weed nuisance: Any abundance of overgrown grass or weeds within the city which is injurious to the general public health, safety and general welfare by providing breeding grounds and shelter for rats, mice, snakes, mosquitoes and other vermin, insects and pests; or attaining such heights and dryness so as to constitute serious fire threat or hazard; or bearing wingy or downy seeds, when mature, that cause the spread of seeds and, when breathed, irritation to the throat, lung and eyes of the public; or hiding debris, such as broken glass or metal, which could inflict injury on any person going upon the property; or being unsightly; or any growth of grass or seeds, other than ornamental plant growth, which exceeds twelve (12) inches in height. 
    Improved subdivision: A division of a tract of land or acreage into tracts or parcels, and the improvement thereof by construction of streets, water lines and, where applicable, sewer lines to serve the subdivided property. 
    Natural condition: Uncultivated and unseeded land, still in a state of nature. But any growth on land, once it has been cleared or plowed, is not a natural condition, even though it has not been planted or cultivated by anyone. 
    Nuisance: Anything that unlawfully causes hurt, inconvenience or damage; that class of wrongs that arises from the unreasonable, unwarrantable or unlawful use by a person of such person's own property, either real or personal, or from such person's own improper, indecent, unsightly or unlawful personal conduct, working an obstruction of or injury to the right of another or of the public, and producing material annoyance, inconvenience, discomfort or hurt to another person or to the general public; anything which is injurious to health, or is indecent or offensive to the senses, or an obstruction to the free use of property, so as to interfere with the comfortable enjoyment of life or property of another. 
    Owner of property: Includes legal title holder, or lessee, or occupant of property, or agent of legal title holder or lessee, in charge, possession or control of said property. For a building nuisance only, includes any mortgage holder of record. 
(Ord. No. 2-03, § 1, 6-23-03) 
Sec. 13-102. - Nuisance unlawful. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or maintain the existence of any nuisance on any property under such person's ownership or control. Property under a person's ownership and control includes those areas referred to in section 13-103. A person with a duty to abate any nuisance is liable for separate and distinct offenses for each day the nuisance is allowed to remain after it has become such person's duty by notice of the enforcing official to abate it. 
(Ord. No. 2-03, § 2, 6-23-03) 
Sec. 13-103. - Duties of owner. 
    It shall be the duty of the owner of any real property located within the city to maintain any grass or weeds growing upon said property in such a manner as not to constitute a nuisance. The duties and obligations of the owner extend to and include any real property situated with a dedicated right-of-way or easement burdening the property, except to the extent that it may be impracticable to do so because of public facilities located thereon. Such rights-of-way and easement must be maintained by the owner in a manner consistent with the maintenance of the owner's remaining property and within the requirements in this article, except to the extent it may be impracticable to do because of public facilities located thereon. 
(Ord. No. 2-03, § 3, 6-23-03) 
Sec. 13-104. - Maintenance practices of city. 
    The dedication and existence of a right-of-way for public road or of an easement for drainage or for public utilities represents the grant of only a limited interest in property and does not change the actual ownership of the property upon which the right-of-way or easement is located. The public authority maintains rights-of-way and easements only to the extent necessary to maintain the public facility and to maintain safety. The owner of the burdened property continues to control the property, except to the extent that such control interferes with the public use. The public authority does not cut grass, weeds and other growth upon rights-of-way or easements, except to the extent necessary for operations and safety purposes. All other maintenance is the responsibility of the owner of the property upon which the right-of-way or easement is located. 
(Ord. No. 2-03, § 4, 6-23-03) 
Sec. 13-105. - Overgrowth. 
    It shall be unlawful and a nuisance, in violation of this article, for the owner of any real property situated within the corporate limits of the city to allow such real property to become overgrown with tall grass, or with any weed or plant such as jimson, burdock, ragweed, cocklebur or other weed of like kind, or any weed or plant bearing wingy or downy seeds, or any weed or plant that is otherwise noxious, dangerous, harmful or poisonous. Overgrown means a height of twelve (12) inches or more. 
(Ord. No. 2-03, § 5, 6-23-03) 
Sec. 13-106. - Debris. 
    An accumulation or storage of debris, refuse, rubbish, brush, used building material, parts of buildings, remains from building demolition, parts of untenantable or uninhabitable structures, used machinery, used tires, used vehicles, parts of vehicles, abandoned vehicles, or any other materials which may provide a breeding place for mosquitoes, harmful insects, rodents or snakes, or is so unsightly as to be offensive to the surrounding area is a nuisance in violation of this article. 
(Ord. No. 2-03, § 6, 6-23-03) 
Sec. 13-107. - Enforcement. 
(a)	Whenever in the opinion of the enforcing official nuisance exists, the official shall order the owner of the property of which the nuisance is located to abate the condition. 
(b)	The enforcing official shall give the owner written notice in person or by first class mail. The notice shall require the owner to comply with this article within the time stated in the notice or to request an administrative hearing before the code enforcement officer or other person designated by the mayor to determine whether there has been a violation. The notice shall apprise the owner of the facts of the alleged nuisance and shall name the particular date, time and place for such hearing if requested.
