For a building nuisance the notice shall contain the names of all owners and lienholders of the property, a legal description of the property and the nature of the proceeding. 
(c)	The notice shall be sent to that person shown by the records of the county tax collector to have been the last person assessed for payment of ad valorem tax on the property where the nuisance is situated. It shall be the responsibility of that person to promptly advise the enforcing official of any change of ownership or interest in the property. It shall be unlawful to knowingly fail to notify the enforcing official of any such change of ownership or interest. The enforcing official shall cause of copy of each building nuisance notice to be recorded in the office of probate judge. 
(d)	The notice shall also be posted in a conspicuous place on the property, preferably within three (3) feet of an entrance to the building or structure. If there is no entrance or no structure, notice may be posted at any location on the property. 
(e)	The notice shall require the owner to complete abatement of the nuisance within the following periods, provided the enforcing official may stipulate additional time, but in no case more than total of one hundred fifty (150) days: 
(1)	Fourteen (14) days from the date of notice if it is a grass and weed nuisance.
(2)	One hundred twenty (120) days from the date of notice if it is a building nuisance.
(3)	Seven (7) days from the date of notice if it is an abandoned vehicle.
(4)	Thirty (30) days from the date of notice if it is any other type of nuisance including but not limited to, burned structures. 
(Ord. No. 2-03, § 7, 6-23-03; Ord. No. 1-05, 1-10-05) 
Sec. 13-108. - Hearing. 
    A hearing before the code enforcement officer must be requested within five (5) days of the date of the notice by the enforcing official. The enforcing official shall notify the owner by personal service or by first class mail of the determination of the hearing official. If the hearing official determines that a nuisance exists, the owner must comply with the initial order to abate issued by the enforcing official, with such modifications as may be made by the hearing official. 
(Ord. No. 2-03, § 8, 6-23-03) 
Sec. 13-109. - Failure to comply with notice to abate. 
(a)	If the owner fails, neglects or refuses to comply with the notice to abate the nuisance, the enforcing official may proceed to prosecute said person for a violation of provisions of the Code. The enforcing official may issue a summons and complaint to the owner of the property, requiring the owner to appear in municipal court to answer charges for the violation of this article. The summons and complaint shall name the party charged, the address of the property where the alleged violation is located, and the nature of the offense or violation. It shall also apprise the owner of the date, time and place at which to appear for court. The summons and complaint, returnable to municipal court, shall be served on the owner by any enforcing official, who shall forthwith appear and take an oath as to the alleged offense before a judge or magistrate of the municipal court. This provision for the issuance of a summons or complaint to municipal court shall not prevent any enforcing official from appearing before a municipal court judge or magistrate and making oath as to the facts and applying for a warrant with respect to any alleged offense, in lieu of issuing a summons and complaint. 
(b)	All violations of the provisions of this article shall be punishable by:
(1)	A fine of the minimum sum of two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) to the maximum of five hundred dollars ($500.00) 
(2)	Imprisonment in the municipal jail for a term not to exceed six (6) months;
(3)	Both such fine and imprisonment; and
(4)	An order to abate the nuisance.
(c)	The enforcing official may institute the enforcement procedure set forth in paragraph (a) and those set out below. The institution of one procedure does not preclude the subsequent or simultaneous institution of the other procedure, provided the criminal procedure is not used to collect any outstanding civil assessments against the subject property. 
(d)	If the owner fails, neglects or refuses to comply with the notice to abate a grass or weeds nuisance, the enforcing official shall cause the cutting of the offending grass or weeds. A minimum hourly assessment of seventy-five dollars ($75.00) plus total wages paid, value of the use of equipment and materials purchased will be charged by the City of Clanton in the event that the city is required to abate the grass and weed nuisance. The costs incurred by the city shall constitute a special assessment against the land and shall constitute a lien on said property. 
(e)	After the public hearing, the city council may by resolution order the enforcing official to proceed with the work specified in such notice or may order such nuisance demolished or removed, or may find that no nuisance exists. If the owner appears at the public hearing, no further notice or the order of the city council shall be required. If the owner fails to appear, notice of the order of the city council shall be mailed to such person's last known address and shall be published once in a newspaper of general circulation in the city. 
(f)	Upon the expiration of seven (7) days from the date of the resolution, the enforcing official shall proceed to carry out the decision of the council. 
(Ord. No. 2-03, § 9, 6-23-03; Ord. No. 10-04, 6-14-04) 
Sec. 13-110. - Assessment of cost. 
(a)	Upon completion of the abatement work performed by the city (including work by contractors employed by the city), the enforcing official shall compute the actual expense, including, but not limited to, total wages paid, value of the use of equipment, advertising expenses, postage, materials purchased, which was incurred by the city as a result of such work. An itemized statement of such expenses shall be given by first class mail to the last known address of the owner of the property. This notice shall be sent at least five (5) days in advance of the time fixed by the city council to consider the assessment of the cost against the property. 
(b)	At the time fixed for receiving and considering the statement, the council shall hear the same, together with any objections which maybe raised by the owner whose property is liable to be assessed for the work and thereupon make such modifications in the statement as they deem necessary, after which a resolution may assess the cost. The cost stated in the resolution shall constitute a special assessment against the land and shall constitute a lien on said property. After adoption of the resolution, a copy shall be turned over to the city clerk who shall charge the assessments against the respective lots and parcels of land for municipal purposes. Thereafter said amounts shall be collected at the same time and in the same manner as ordinary municipal assessment are collected, and shall be subject to same penalties and same procedure under foreclosure and sale in case of delinquency as provided for ordinary municipal assessments. 
(c)	The city clerk shall cause a certified copy of the resolution assessing the cost of abatement to be filed for recording in the office of the probate judge. 
(d)	Satisfaction of liens. Upon payment of the itemized accounts arising under this ordinance, any liens or assessments filed hereunder may be marked "satisfied" and "paid in full" by the city clerk. 
(Ord. No. 2-03, § 10, 6-23-03) 
Sec. 13-111. - Construction of article. 
    The article shall be construed to contain all power granted to municipalities under sections; 11-40-10, 11-47-117, 11-47-140, and 11-48-1 through 11-48-106, Code of Alabama, as amended, providing for controlling nuisances, sanitation and good public health and safety conditions, and for assessment of public improvement liens. 
(Ord. No. 2-03, § 11, 6-23-03) 
Secs. 13-112-13-119. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - TOBACCO 

Sec. 13-120. - Definitions. 
    [The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning.] 
(a)	Smoking or smoke or smokeless tobacco shall include the carrying, holding or possession of lighted smoking materials in any form, including, but not limited to, the possession of lighted cigarettes, cigars, pipes and smokeless tobacco products. 
(b)	Public or public place shall include any enclosed or unenclosed area, including, but not limited to, the City Hall, city shops, and city parks used in connection with and under the control of the City of Clanton wherein the city employees are assigned or work. 
(Ord. No. 6-99, § I, 3-22-99; Ord. No. 3-05, § I, 3-28-2005) 
Sec. 13-121. - Offenses. 
(a)	Hereafter and upon the adoption of this article, smoking is prohibited in the City Hall building, city shops, or enclosures used in connection with and under the control of the City of Clanton, except as hereinafter provided. 
(b)	Hereafter and upon the adoption of this article, smoking is prohibited in the city parks, except as hereinafter provided. 
(1)	Clanton City Park. Smoking and smokeless tobacco will be allowed outside the wood-fenced areas at Clanton City Park. For areas at Clanton City Park not enclosed by a wood fence, namely, the football field and baseball/softball fields #4 and #5, smoking and smokeless tobacco will be allowed outside one hundred (100) feet from the bleachers. 
Smoking and smokeless tobacco will be allowed outside the pool facilities. 
There will be no smoking or smokeless tobacco within playground areas. 
(2)	Goosepond Park. No smoking or smokeless tobacco is allowed beyond the bridge entrance. 
(3)	E. M. Henry Park. No smoking or smokeless tobacco is allowed within the fenced areas. 
(Ord. No. 6-99, § II, 3-22-99; Ord. No. 3-05, § II, 3-28-2005) 
Sec. 13-122. - Exceptions. 
    The provisions of this article do not apply to areas designated as "smoking areas". 
(Ord. No. 6-99, § III, 3-22-99; Ord. No. 3-05, § III, 3-28-2005) 
Sec. 13-123. - Designation of smoking and non-smoking areas. 
    The officers of the city shall within thirty (30) days following the adoption of this article, designate by signs, notices, or other appropriate means posted in conspicuous places, the areas where smoking is permitted and where smoking is prohibited. 
(Ord. No. 6-99, § IV, 3-22-99) 
Sec. 13-124. - Penalty. 
    Any person in willful violation of this article or any person who willfully smokes in an area where smoking is prohibited, shall be guilty of an offense and upon conviction may be fined not less than one dollar ($1.00) nor more than one hundred dollars ($100.00) for each offense. 
(Ord. No. 6-99, § V, 3-22-99) 
Secs. 13-125-13-150. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - NOISE CONTROL 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (5) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2-07, §§ 1-10, adopted January 22, 2007, set out provisions pertaining to noise control and did not specifically amend the Code, hence inclusion as Article VI, §§ 13-151-13-160 has been at the editor's discretion. 
Sec. 13-151. - Short title. 
    This article may be cited as the "Noise Control Ordinance". 
(Ord. No. 2-07, § 1, 1-22-07) 
Sec. 13-152. - Authority. 
    This article is approved and adopted by the Clanton, Alabama in the exercise of its general police powers under the laws of the State of Alabama, specifically including but not limited to Title 11-45-1, et seq., Code of Alabama, 1975. 
(Ord. No. 2-07, § 2, 1-22-07) 
Sec. 13-153. - Purpose. 
    This article is enacted to protect, preserve and promote the health, safety, welfare, peace and quiet for the citizens of Clanton, Alabama through the reduction, control and prevention of excessive sound or other noise. It is the intent of this article to establish standards that will eliminate and reduce unnecessary and excessive community sounds or other unreasonable noises which are physically harmful and otherwise detrimental to individuals and the community in the enjoyment of life, property and conduct of business. 
(Ord. No. 2-07, § 3, 1-22-07) 
Sec. 13-154. - Definitions. 
    All technical terminology used in this article shall, for the purpose of this article, have the meanings hereinafter ascribed to them. 
    City means the City of Clanton, Alabama. 
    Commercial area means any area designated for commercial uses under the zoning ordinance of the city. 
    Construction means any site preparation, assembly, erection, substantial repair, alteration or similar action, but excluding demolition. 
    Demolition means any dismantling, intentional destruction or removal of structures, utilities, public or private right-of-way surfaces or similar property. 
    Emergency means any occurrence or set of circumstances involving actual or imminent physical trauma or property damage which demands immediate action. 
    Emergency work means any work performed for the purpose of preventing or alleviating the physical trauma or property damage threatened or caused by an emergency. 
    Impulsive sound means sound of short duration, usually less than one (1) second, with an abrupt onset and rapid decay. Examples of sources of impulsive sound include explosions, drop forge impacts and the discharge of firearms. 
    Motor vehicle means any vehicle which is propelled or drawn on land by a motor, such as, but not limited to, passenger cars, trucks, truck-trailers, semi-trailers, campers, go-carts, snowmobiles, amphibious craft on land, dune buggies or racing vehicles, but not including motorcycles. 
    Motorcycle means an unenclosed motor vehicle having a seat for the use of the operator and two (2) or three (3) wheels in contact with the ground, including, but not limited to, motor scooters and mini-bikes. 
    Muffler or sound dissipative device means a device for abating the sound of escaping gasses of an internal combustion engine. 
    Noise means any sound which annoys or disturbs humans or which causes or tends to cause an adverse psychological or physiological effect on humans. 
    Noise disturbance means any sound which endangers or injures the safety or health of humans or animals, or annoys or disturbs a reasonable person of normal sensitivities, or endangers or injures personal or real property. 
    Person means any individual, association, partnership, corporation or other legal entity. 
    Powered model vehicle means any self-propelled airborne, waterborne or land borne plane, vessel or vehicle, which is not designed to carry persons, including, but not limited to, any model airplane, boat, car or rocket. 
    Public right-of-way means any street, avenue, boulevard, highway, sidewalk or alley or similar place which is owned or controlled by a governmental entity. 
    Public space means any real property or structures thereon which are owned or controlled by a governmental entity. 
    Real property boundary means a line along the ground surface and its vertical extension, which separates the real property owned by one person from that owned by another person, but not including intrabuilding real property divisions. 
    Residential area means an area designated for any residential use under the zoning ordinance of the city. 
(Ord. No. 2-07, § 4, 1-22-07) 
Sec. 13-155. - Scope. 
    It shall be unlawful and a nuisance for any person to make, continue or cause to be made or continued any loud, unreasonably loud, disturbing, unnecessary or excessive noise which unreasonably interferes with the comfort, health or safety of others within the jurisdiction of the City of Clanton, Alabama. It shall also be unlawful and a nuisance for any person to permit any such noise to be made in or upon any house or premises owned or possessed by him or under his management or control. 
(Ord. No. 2-07, § 5, 1-22-07) 
Sec. 13-156. - Specific violations. 
    In addition to the general prohibition set out above, the following specific acts, among others, are declared to be loud, disturbing or unnecessary noises and are declared to be in violation of this article; provided, however, that such enumeration shall not be deemed to be exclusive. It is hereby declared a nuisance and shall be unlawful: 
(a)	Music in motor vehicles and pedestrians. 
(1)	To operate or play any radio, musical instrument or similar device whether from a motor vehicle or by a pedestrian in such a manner as to be plainly audible to any person other than the player or operator of the device at a distance of twenty (20) feet in the case of a motor vehicle or thirty (30) feet in the case of a pedestrian. 
(2)	Regardless of any other provision contained in this article or any section thereof, no person, firm or corporation shall operate or play any radio, stereo system, musical instrument or other or similar device which generates any noise or sound from any motor or other vehicle located on or within any public road or right-of-way within the city, at such a sound level or in a manner where same may be detectable by or audible to the normal unaided human ear beyond or outside of the right-of-way boundaries or lines of such public road or right-of-way. 
(b)	Electronic devices and musical instruments. 
(1)	To operate or play any radio, television, phonograph, musical instrument or similar device which produces or reproduces sound whether from a business, residence or other premises in such a manner as to be plainly audible at a distance of fifty (50) feet to any person in a commercial, residential, multi-family dwelling, professional office building, institutional or public place. 
(2)	Anything contained in this article to the contrary notwithstanding, it is further provided that it is hereby declared a nuisance and shall be unlawful to operate or play any radio, television, musical instrument or similar device or to produce live music, sound or noise in any manner which produces or reproduces sound or noise, whether from a business, residence or any other premises, in such manner as to be plainly audible outside of the real property boundary of such business, residence or other premises between the hours of 10 o'clock p.m. and the following morning at 9 o'clock a.m. 
(3)	Anything contained in this article to the contrary notwithstanding, it is further provided that it is hereby declared a nuisance for any person, firm or corporation to operate or play any radio, musical instrument or similar device or to generate live music, noise or sound, whether from a motor vehicle, a pedestrian or from a commercial or residential premise which may, between the hours of 10 o'clock p.m. and the following morning at 9 o'clock a.m. be heard in such manner as to be plainly audible to any person other than the player or operator of the device, or the provider of said music, or the persons located on the premises from which said music, sound or noise emanates. 
(4)	Anything contained in this article to the contrary notwithstanding, it is further provided that no person, firm or corporation shall transmit or allow to be transmitted any live or electronically produced music or other sound on any property at a sound level which is detectable by the normal unaided human ear beyond the real property boundary of the person, firm, or corporation upon whose property said sound or other noise is emanating from. 
(c)	Blowing horns. To sound any horn or signal device on any automobile, motorcycle, bus or other vehicle, except as a danger signal when and as required by ordinances of the city or by the Code of Alabama; to create by means of any such signal device of any unreasonable, loud or harsh sound; and the sounding of such device for an unnecessary or unreasonable period of time. The provisions of this section regulating the sounding of a horn or signal device on vehicles shall not apply to authorized emergency vehicles while the driver of such vehicle is operating the same in an emergency in the necessary performance of public duties, and when the sounding of such horn or signal device is made as a warning or danger signal. 
(d)	Pets. To keep any animal or bird which, by causing frequent or long continued noise, shall disturb the comfort or repose of any ordinary person in the vicinity. 
(e)	Unmuffled engine exhausts. To discharge into the open air the exhaust of any steam engine, stationary internal combustion engine, motor vehicle or motor boat engine, except through a muffler or other device which will effectively prevent the emission of loud or explosive noises therefrom. No person shall operate a motor vehicle which causes excessive noise levels as a result of a defective or modified exhaust system or as a result of an unnecessary rapid acceleration, deceleration, engine revving or tire squealing. 
(f)	Peddlers. etc. To shout or cry by peddlers, hawkers and vendors which disturbs the peace and quiet of the neighborhood. 
(g)	Fireworks. To explode firecrackers, skyrockets, Roman candles, pinwheels or any other form of fireworks, except the display of fireworks in public parks or other open places within the city under a permit issued by the fire marshal, pursuant to the fire prevention code of the city. 
(h)	Use of noisemakers for advertising purposes. To use any drum, pan, pail, bell, horn, trumpet, loudspeaker or other instrument or device for the purpose of attracting attention or intended to attract attention to any performance, show or sale or display of merchandise, or for any other advertising purposes; provided, that the provisions of this subsection (h) shall not apply to any type of carillon which is located in or on any premises in the city and is played, operated or sounded so as to cause music or musical notes or a time strike to emanate from such carillon or from amplifiers attached thereto and located in or on the same premises. 
(i)	Calliopes or amplifiers on vehicles. To use calliopes, mechanical loudspeakers or amplifiers on any vehicles used for advertising or other purposes, except when a permit for such use over a specified route is issued by the mayor and except within the times specified in the permit. 
(j)	Disorderly or unruly conduct. A person violates this article if, with intent to cause public inconvenience, annoyance or alarm, recklessly creating a risk thereof, he or she makes unreasonable noise. 
(k)	Loading and unloading. To load, unload, open, close or other handling of boxes, crates, containers, building materials, garbage cans or similar objects between the hours of 10 o'clock p.m. and 7 o'clock a.m. the following day in such a manner as to cause a noise disturbance across a residential real property boundary. 
(l)	Construction. To operate or permit the operation of any tools or equipment used in construction, drilling or demolition work between the hours of 10 o'clock p.m. and 7 o'clock a.m. the following day on weekdays or at any time on weekends or holidays, such that the sound therefrom creates a noise disturbance across a residential real property boundary, except for emergency work or public service utilities. 
(m)	Powered model vehicles. To operate or permit the operation of powered model vehicles so as to create a noise disturbance across a residential real property boundary, in a public space or within a noise sensitive zone between the hours of 10 o'clock p.m. and 7 o'clock a.m. the following day. 
(n)	Stationary non-emergency signaling devices. 
(1)	To sound or permit the sounding of any signal from any stationary bell, chime, siren, whistle or similar device, intended primarily for non-emergency purposes, from any place, for more than one (1) minute in any hourly period. 
(2)	Devices used in conjunction with a place of religious worship and educational institutions shall be exempt from the operation of this provision. 
(o)	Domestic power tools. To operate or permit the operation of any mechanically powered saw, sander, drill, grinder, lawn or garden tool, snowblower or similar device used outdoors in residential areas between the hours of 10 o'clock p.m. and 7 o'clock a.m. the following day so as to cause a noise disturbance across a residential real property boundary. 
(Ord. No. 2-07, § 6, 1-22-07) 
Sec. 13-157. - Exceptions. 
    Nothing in this article shall be construed to prohibit: 
(a)	Special performances by a band or orchestra in a hall, building or in the open air after proper permits have been obtained from the mayor. 
(b)	The ringing of bells or chimes by churches within the city.
(c)	Any noises or sounds produced by radios, sirens or other equipment attached to, or being operated by, any police, fire, rescue or other emergency vehicles or personnel. 
(d)	The conducting of live remote broadcasts by duly licensed radio stations, upon business premises, at the request of the owner of the business. Said live broadcasts shall be limited to daylight hours only. 
(e)	Organized school-related programs, activities and other events are exempt from the terms and provisions of this article. 
(f)	Organized public programs, activities and events and parades or other public programs, activities or events authorized by the mayor are exempt from the terms and provisions of this article. 
(Ord. No. 2-07, § 7, 1-22-07) 
Sec. 13-158. - Fines and punishment. 
    Any person found to be in violation of any section of this article shall, upon conviction, be punished by a fine of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than five hundred dollars ($500.00) and/or may be imprisoned or sentenced to hard labor for the city for a period not exceeding six (6) months, at the discretion of the court trying the case. The violation of this article or any part thereof on more than one (1) day shall each constitute separate offenses. 
(Ord. No. 2-07, § 8, 1-22-07) 
Sec. 13-159. - Summons and complaint in lieu of arrest warrant. 
    Pursuant to the provisions of § 11-45-9.1 of the 1975 Code of Alabama, as last amended, which authorizes municipalities to issue summons and complaints in lieu of arrest warrants for violation of certain municipal ordinances. 
(a)	That any law enforcement officer of the City of Clanton, Alabama may issue a summons and complaint to any person charged with committing the offense of nuisance-unreasonable noise, in violation of Ordinance Number 2-07 of the City of Clanton, Alabama and release such person from custody upon his or her written promise to appear in court at the designated time and place as evidenced by his or her signature on the summons and complaint. 
(b)	The summons and complaint form, as described in the preceding sub-section, shall be in the same form as the summons and complaint forms presently used by the municipal court of the City of Clanton, Alabama. 
(Ord. No. 2-07, § 9, 1-22-07) 
Sec. 13-160. - Variances and exceptions. 
(a)	The mayor or his designated representative shall have the authority, consistent with this article, to grant special variances and/or exceptions. 
(b)	Any person seeking a special variance and/or exception pursuant to this article shall file an application with the mayor or his designated representative. The application shall contain information regarding the date, time and place where the special variance and/or exception is desired or needed. The applicant shall also include in the application a full and detailed explanation as to why such special variance and/or exception is wanted and/or needed. 
(c)	The special variance and/or exception may be granted by the mayor or his designated representative by notice to applicant in writing containing all necessary conditions including a time limit on the permitted activity. The special variance and/or exception shall not become effective until all conditions are agreed to by the applicant. Noncompliance of any condition of the special variance and/or exception shall terminate it and subject the person holding it to those provisions of this article regulating the source of sound or activity for which the special variance and/or exception was granted. 
(Ord. No. 2-07, § 10, 1-22-07) 
Chapter 14 - PARADES AND DEMONSTRATIONS 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Animals, Ch. 4; licenses and business regulations, Ch. 10; motor vehicles and traffic, Ch. 11; streets and sidewalks, Ch. 18. (Back)
State Law reference- Power of local authorities to regulate the use of the highways by processions or assemblages, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5-1. (Back)
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 14-1-14-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PERMIT 

Sec. 14-26. - Required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in, participate in, aid, form or start any parade within the corporate limits of the city or the police jurisdiction thereof unless a parade permit has been first obtained from the mayor of the city in accordance with the provisions contained in this article. 
(Code 1979, § 11-1) 
Sec. 14-27. - Exceptions. 
    This article shall not apply to funeral processions or to students going to and from school classes or participating in educational activities, provided such conduct is under the immediate direction and supervision of the proper school authorities, and shall not apply to government agencies acting within the scope of their functions. 
(Code 1979, § 11-6) 
Sec. 14-28. - Application. 
    Prior to forming, holding, conducting or participating in a parade within the city limits or police jurisdiction of the city, the person conducting the parade shall, not more than ten (10) days and not less than five (5) days prior to the commencement of the parade, first file an application for a permit with the mayor of the city. The application, the permit, when issued, shall disclose to the city the following information: 
(1)	The name, address and telephone number of the person seeking to conduct such parade;
(2)	If the parade is proposed to be conducted for and on behalf of any person, the name, address and telephone number of the office, home office or headquarters of the organization; 
(3)	The name, address and telephone number of the person who will be the parade marshal or parade chairman and will be responsible for its conduct; 
(4)	The date and time when the parade is to be conducted;
(5)	The route to be traveled, the starting point, and the terminal point;
(6)	The approximate number of persons who will participate in the parade and the type of vehicles to be used in the parade; 
(7)	The location of the assembly area for such parade;
(8)	The time at which units of the parade will begin to assemble at the assembly area; and 
(9)	Any additional information which the mayor shall find reasonably necessary to a fair determination as to whether a permit should be issued. 
(Code 1979, § 11-2) 
Sec. 14-29. - Granting; denial. 
(a)	The mayor shall issue a permit to the person applying therefor as provided in this article when, from a consideration of the application and from such other information as may otherwise be obtained, he finds that: 
(1)	The conduct of the parade will not substantially interrupt the safe and orderly movement of other traffic contiguous to its route; 
(2)	The conduct of the parade will not require the diversion of so great a number of police officers of the city to properly police the line of movement and the areas contiguous thereto as to prevent normal police protection to the city; 
(3)	The concentration of persons, animals and vehicles at assembly points of the parade will not unduly interfere with proper fire and police protection of, or ambulance service to, areas contiguous to such assembly area; 
(4)	The conduct of the parade is not reasonably likely to cause injury to persons or property or to provoke disorderly conduct or create a disturbance; and 
(5)	The parade is scheduled to move from its point of origin to its point of termination expeditiously and without unreasonable delays en route. 
(b)	The mayor shall act upon the application for a parade permit within two (2) days after the filing thereof. If the mayor disapproves the application, he shall mail a statement to the applicant, within two (2) days after the date on which the application was filed, addressed to the address of the applicant, stating the refusal or denial of the permit. 
(Code 1979, §§ 11-3, 11-4) 
Sec. 14-30. - Authority of mayor to act on late applications. 
    The mayor, where good cause is shown therefor, shall have the authority to consider any application under this article which is filed less than five (5) days before the date such parade is proposed to be conducted and act on the application as if the application was filed within the time specified in this article. 
(Code 1979, § 11-8) 
Sec. 14-31. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- 
Ord. No. 18-96, adopted Nov. 6, 1996, deleted, in effect repealed, § 14-31, which prohibited issuance of parade permits to be held on Saturdays and derived from § 11-5 of the city's 1979 Code. 
Sec. 14-32. - Carrying of permit during parade. 
    The parade chairman, parade marshal, or the person heading the parade shall carry the parade permit upon his person during the conduct of the parade. 
(Code 1979, § 11-7) 
Chapter 15 - PERSONNEL 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- At the request of the city the provisions of Ord. No. 1-96, Arts. I-XII, adopted Jan. 22, 1996, have been added as a new Ch. 15 to read as herein set out. See the Code Comparative Table. 
Cross reference- Administration, Ch. 2. (Back)
ARTICLE I. - INTRODUCTION 

Sec. 15-1. - Established of rules. 
    In accordance with the provisions of Ordinance No. 1-96 of the City of Clanton, the following rules, regulations and other administrative provisions for personnel administration (hereinafter called "rules") are established for the information and guidance of all concerned. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 1(I), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-2. - Applicability of rules. 
    The rules herein established shall apply to all appointed paid employees of the City of Clanton. The personnel clerk has the authority to take appropriate action in dealing with cases of violation of the established rules. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 2(I), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-3. - Dissemination of rules. 
    Department heads will be furnished complete copies of all rules and changes thereto, and shall be responsible for maintaining a complete set of rules, and for bringing these rules to the attention of all employees under their supervision. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 3(I), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-4. - Definitions. 
    Where used within these personnel rules, the following words and terms shall have meaning indicated below: 
    Allocation. The assignment of an individual position to appropriate class of positions on the basis of the kind, difficulty, required skill, and responsibility of the work performed. 
    Anniversary date. One year from date of appointment to permanent full time position and annually thereafter. 
    Appointing authority. The mayor having authority under the laws of the State of Alabama to make appointments to positions. 
    Class, or class of positions. A group of positions sufficiently alike in duties to justify the same class title and range of pay. 
    Class description. A written description of a class of positions containing a title, examples of work performed, required knowledge, skills, and abilities, and qualifications for applicants or incumbents to insure satisfactory performance. 
    Classification. The entire process of assigning and reassigning individuals to positions, positions to classes, and classes to grades to the end that employees will be employed and compensated on the basis of merit, fitness, and actual duties performed so that there may exist equal pay for equal work. 
    Demotions. The change of an employee from a position in one class to a position in another class having a lower pay grade and requiring the performance of less responsible duties. 
    Grade or pay grade. The numerical designation of a fixed salary range assigned to a position, class or group of classes. 
    Merit increases. Advancement in pay of an employee to a higher step in pay grade based upon display of merit in performance in duties and/or requiring a change in basic duties. 
    Merit system. A uniform system of personnel administration and employee recognition which has been adopted by the City of Clanton to recruit, employ, retain, and advance the best qualified persons available. 
    Position description. A detailed written description of the specific duties assigned to and performed by a particular employee to serve as a basis for classification. 
    Probationary period. A working test period (three (3) months for general employees and twelve (12) months for policemen), during which an employee is required to demonstrate by actual performance, his fitness for the duties to which he is appointed, and his general fitness and suitability as a public employee. 
    Promotion. The change of an employee from a position in one class to a position in another class having a higher pay grade and requiring the performance of more responsible duties. 
    Reclassification. The reallocation of a position to a different class of positions based upon substantial change in duties and responsibilities. 
    Regrading. The assignment of a new grade to an entire class of positions. 
    Steps or pay steps. The fixed rates of pay within a pay range authorized for a class of positions assigned to a particular grade, through which an employee may advance, while still performing the same duties. 
    Transfer. The reassignment of an employee to a position in the same pay grade without increase or decrease in rate of pay. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 4(I), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-5. - Administration of personnel. 
    The personnel clerk is responsible for personnel administration within the city government. All matters dealing with personnel shall be routed through the personnel clerk, who shall maintain a complete system of personnel files and records. The policy of the municipality is that all employee hiring, termination, classification, assignment, and promotion shall be based on ability and suitability, and without regard to race, creed, color, religion, or sex. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 5(I), 1-22-96) 
Secs. 15-6-15-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - APPOINTMENT AND PROMOTION 

Sec. 15-21. - General. 
    Appointments and promotions to all classified positions shall be solely on the basis of merit, which shall be determined by evaluation of the applicant's (1) training, education, experience, and physical fitness, (2) oral interview and (3) whenever practical, and examination of demonstration performance test. 
    In compliance with the Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990, the City of Clanton does not discriminate against otherwise qualified individuals with disabilities and recognizes our duty to provide reasonable accommodations to otherwise qualified individuals. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 1(II), 1-22-96) 
Sec 15-22. - Tests. 
    The personnel clerk may establish test or examinations which are warranted to determine whether or not an applicant or employee meets established standards. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 2(II), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-23. - Age. 
    The minimum age for employment as a probationary employee shall be eighteen (18) years of age. The minimum age for employment of seasonal employees shall be sixteen (16) years of age. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 3(II), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-24. - Promotion. 
    All vacancies occurring in the classified service shall, whenever possible, be filled by promotion of a qualified employee within the public service. However, the personnel clerk may recruit applicants from outside the public service whenever he/she has reason to believe that better qualified applicants are available than within the public service. Promotion within the public service shall be based on the qualifications of the person being appointed. Usually, the first consideration in filling of vacancies will be given to the most qualified applicant in the department in which the vacancy exist. Next, consideration will be given to the most qualified applicant from outside the department. If no applicant is found within the public service, the vacancy will be filled from outside the public service. The criteria used in the selection of the most qualified applicant shall be based upon experience, performance, evaluation, and where feasible, examination. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 4(II), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 10-25. - Re-employment. 
    Prior to initiating any actions to fill a vacancy from outside the public service the personnel clerk will review the re-employment eligibility list to determine if there are individuals on such list who are qualified for the vacancy. The re-employment list consist of former permanent status classified or part-time service employees who were laid off within the past two (2) years and are otherwise eligible for re-employment to a comparable vacant position. Qualified individuals interested in re-employment should stay in contact with the personnel clerk. If no qualified person is available, the personnel clerk will initiate actions to fill the vacancy from the public service. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 5(II), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-26. - Personnel recruitment. 
    The personnel clerk is responsible for recruiting individuals to fill authorized vacancies. Active recruitment from the general public will be accomplished by: 
(1)	Posting vacancy notices on bulletin boards in the City Hall and advertising in the local newspapers. 
(2)	All notices, or advertisements will provide a description of the position, necessary and desired qualifications, deadline for applying, and the name and address of the contact person. All vacancy notices or advertisements will also contain the statement that "The City of Clanton is an Equal Opportunity employer". 
(3)	All applications will be made on application forms furnished by the personnel clerk. Completed applications will be submitted to the personnel clerk in accordance with the vacancy notice instructions. No application will be considered valid unless received by the personnel clerk by the application deadline. 
(4)	Any requirement for examinations and/or performance test to be used in establishing an applicant's qualification for a vacancy will be established by the city council. Required testing will be held in the City Hall, except for special circumstances which are approved by the council. All testing will conform with applicable laws and guidelines that pertain to job relatedness. 
(5)	The council or personnel clerk may refuse to examine or interview, or after examination or interview, refuse to refer the name of anyone who is found to lack any of the established job-related requirements for the position for which he/she in applying, or anyone who has been convicted, within the past five years, of any crime involving moral turpitude, or is under indictment for any crime, or anyone who has been guilty of any infamous or disgraceful conduct, or anyone who has been dismissed from the public service for delinquency material fact or attempted to practice any deception or fraud in his/her application or in his/her examination. 
(6)	The personnel clerk will review each application to insure that it is complete. All complete applications for a vacancy will be reviewed for selection of the best qualified individual. 
(7)	All applications received in response to a vacancy notice that meet the required qualifications for the vacant position will remain active until the selected applicant has completed the required probationary period. If the selected applicant does not complete the required probationary period, the vacancy will be filled from the remaining qualified applicants. If no qualified applications remain on file, the vacancy will be advertised again. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 6(II), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-27. - Selection. 
    Selection for vacancies will be made by the city council. Each selection will be based on the knowledge, skills and abilities determined to be the required and/or desired job related qualifications for the job without regard to age, sex, creed, religion, race, political affiliation, or handicap (except where age, sex, or handicap constitute a bona fide occupational qualification). Reasonable accommodations for handicapped individuals who are otherwise qualified will be made, when practical. 
(1)	The personnel clerk and supervisor of the department may hold interviews with the top applicants. All interview results will be recorded on interview forms provided by the personnel clerk. If an applicant cannot be located to establish an interview time, the applicant will be passed over. 
(2)	Appropriate inquiries of former employers and selected personnel references, when required, shall be made by the personnel clerk only for an applicant who has been designated as being tentatively acceptable. If agreeable to the applicant, inquiries may also be made to the applicant's present employer. 
(3)	After all interviews and/or inquiries have been completed, the personnel clerk will notify the appointing authority in writing of the name of the top applicants to the city council for final selection. The city council will be provided all qualified applications, if requested. The city council will insure that their selection is made on a nondiscriminatory basis and is in keeping with established guidelines for equal treatment of all groups of people and the provisions of these policies and procedures. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 7(II), 1-22-96; Ord. No. 10-01, 11-7-01) 
Sec. 15-28. - Probationary period. 
    Each general employee receiving an appointment of a promotion to a position in the classification service must serve a probationary period of three (3) months before the individual's appointment or promotion shall be considered full-time. Probationary periods for policemen shall be twelve (12) months upon appointment and six (6) months upon promotion. During the employee's probationary period, the employee's work habits, abilities, attitude, promptness and other pertinent characteristics will be observed and evaluated by a supervisor, department head and other appropriate officials. If the probationary employee fails to meet required standards of performance, employment will be terminated, or if the individual is a promoted regular employee, the individual may be restored to the classification and position from which he was promoted or to a comparable position. Termination or demotion will be conditional, subject to review and approval of the appointing authority. 
(1)	Termination. If at any time during the probationary period the supervisor or department head determines that the services of the employee have been unsatisfactory, the employee may be terminated from his/her position, provided such termination is approved by his appointing authority. The appointing authority shall notify the employee in writing at least seven (7) calendar days before the effective date of separation. The appointing authority may, however, issue one week's severance pay in lieu of termination notice. 
(2)	Probationary reports. At least ten (10) days prior to the end of each employee's probationary period, the department head shall complete a probationary report and notify the appointing authority in writing that either (a) the employee has successfully completed his probationary period and shall hence forth be considered a regular employee with all rights and privileges due him; (b) the employee has not progressed as desired but it is recommended that his/her probationary status be extended for an additional ninety (90) days. At the expiration of the ninety (90) day extended probation, action must be taken to grant employee status, terminate the employee or in the case of promotion probation status, return the employee to the classification from which promoted or (c) the employee has not demonstrated ability to perform satisfactory duties of the position and is to be separated from employment, or a similar classification. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 8(II), 1-22-96; Ord. No. 10-01, 11-7-01) 
Sec. 15-29. - Relatives in the local government service. 
    Two (2) or more members of an immediate family shall not be employed under the same supervisor; neither shall two (2) members of an immediate family be employed at the same time, regardless of the administrative department if such employment will result in an employee supervising a member of his immediate family. This policy applies to promotions, demotions, transfers, reinstatement and new appointments. The provisions of this section shall not be retroactive, and no action is taken concerning those members of the same family employed at the adoption of this section. Immediate family is defined as wife, husband, mother, father, brother, sister, son, daughter, mother-in-law, son-in-law, daughter-in-law, grandparents, grandchildren, stepmother, stepfather, brother-in-law, sister-in-law, uncle, and aunt. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 9(II), 1-22-96) 
Secs. 15-30-15-40. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - CLASSIFICATION OF POSITIONS 

Sec. 15-41. - Classification plan. 
    A classification plan shall be established and maintained and filed within the office of the personnel clerk. No deviation shall be made from the classification plan. Where circumstances warrant, the plan itself or the classification of a particular position or class of positions may be amended by the municipal governing body. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 1(III), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-42. - Position descriptions. 
    Where a new position is created, departments shall furnish a tentative description of expected duties prior to employment to aid in the recruitment and the initial classification of that employee. The personnel clerk shall furnish within thirty (30) days after employment a position description of any changes in duties performed by new employee, and shall furnish new or supplementary position description whenever these duties change. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 2(III), 1-22-96) 
Secs. 15-43-15-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - PAY OF EMPLOYEES 

Sec. 15-61. - Pay plan. 
    The pay of all employees, other than whose pay is fixed by the municipal governing body, is established by the pay plan for the class of position in which they are employed. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 1(IV), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-62. - Pay steps. 
    For each class of positions, a pay grade is assigned, and for each class of positions within that grade a number of pay steps are provided. Initial employment is normally at the first pay step of the range but in exceptional circumstances based upon experience or unusual qualifications of any applicant, and with the prior approval of the municipal governing body, an employee may be hired in a higher step. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 2(IV), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-63. - Promotion. 
    The pay of an employee promoted to a position of higher grade may be adjusted to that step in the new pay grade which is next higher than the former rate of pay. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 3(IV), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-64. - Pay and allowances. 
    Rates of pay established are gross and total compensation for full time service in the various classifications. The hours of work for full time service are established by the pay plan, although the appointing authority shall fix hours of work for employee and offices. Rates of pay establish provide full compensation for whatever hours may be reasonable required in all classes of positions, and no position shall be subject to additional compensation as a result of any reasonable variation in hours worked. The appointing authority may authorize pay for overtime work in emergencies or other unusual occasions beyond reasonable requirements of hours worked. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 4(IV), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-65. - Overtime. 
    The standard work week shall be established by the appointing authority. Department heads should work those hours necessary to assure the satisfactory performance of their department, but not less than forty (40) hours per week. The department head shall assign to each employee regular duties and responsibilities which can normally be accomplished within the established work day and work week. However, occasionally some overtime work may be necessary for proper performance of work duties and responsibilities. When department heads (who are paid hourly wages) or regular classified employee are required to work extra or prolonged shifts, they shall receive overtime pay equal to one and one-half (1/2) normal pay rate. 
(1)	Overtime-Compensatory time. Salaried employees who are required to work on a holiday, or who must participate in special overtime duties not included in their regular work program may be granted compensatory time off in lien of compensation. On occasions where the performance of normal duties require overtime work neither compensation nor compensatory time off may be granted. Any program of overtime work to be compensated by time off must have the prior approval of the appointing authority. 
(2)	Overtime holiday. Eligible employees will be paid holiday pay at their normal daily rate of pay for each authorized paid holiday. However, a paid holiday will not be counted as hours worked during a workweek/work period unless the employee actually works on the holiday. Those eligible employees who actually work the holiday will in addition to receiving their holiday pay, be paid their regular rate of pay for all hours worked on the holiday, or scheduled to take time off for the holiday as determined by their appointing authority. If the time worked causes the employees total hours worked for the workweek/work period to exceed the regular hours of work for the workweek/work period overtime pay or compensatory time off will be provided. 
(3)	[Public safety workers; salaried employees.] In lieu of the foregoing, where necessary, and in replacement thereof, where necessary, employees categorized as full-time public safety workers, i.e., police, fire, EMS, and communication officers, will be compensated overtime one and one-half (1.5) of normal hourly rate, based upon the Fair Labor Standards Act 207k, for one hundred seventy-one (171) hours in a twenty-eight-day pay cycle or after eighty-five and one-half (85.5) hours for police/communications and two hundred twelve (212) hours in a twenty-eight-day cycle for fire/EMS. Those that hold department head status, i.e., police chief, deputy chief, assistant chief, major, captain, and certain lieutenants (that hold straight administrative functions), will be considered salaried employees. Those employees that hold salaried status will work all the hours required to ensure the satisfactory performance of their departments or divisions, but shall not work less that forty (40) hours per week. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 5(IV), 1-22-96; Ord. No. 9-10, 10-11-2010) 
Sec. 15-66. - Pay for part-time employment. 
    Whenever and employee, not on leave with pay, works for less than regularly established number of hours per day, days per week, or weeks per month, suitable entry shall be made on the payroll, and the amount paid shall be proportionate to the time actually worked. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 6(IV), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-67. - Deductions on termination. 
    On termination of employment the municipality shall deduct and withhold from the final paycheck of any employee unreturned equipment, or any other indebtness to the municipality, and the final paycheck shall not be issued until determined and cleared. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 7(IV), 1-22-96) 
Secs. 15-68-15-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - EMPLOYEE VACATION AND SICK LEAVE 

Sec. 15-81. - General policy. 
    The following types of leaves are officially established: Holidays, annual leave, sick leave, bereavement leave, civil leave, and leave without pay. All departments are required to maintain records of absences of their employees. No part-time employee shall be eligible for the leaves enumerated herein. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 1(V), 1-22-96; Ord. No. 12-01, 12-20-01) 
Sec. 15-82. - Holidays. 
    The following and such other days as the city council proclaims are holidays for all employees except emergency and part-time employees: New Year's Day, Martin Luther King's Birthday, (3rd Monday in January), July 4th, Labor Day, Thanksgiving Day, Friday following Thanksgiving day, Christmas Eve and Christmas Day, Veterans Day, Memorial Day. 
(1)	Full-time employees: It shall be the policy of the City Council to ensure that all full-time employees enjoy the same number of holidays in a particular year which will be celebrated by full-time employees working [a] forty-hour week, Monday through Friday. For this group, when a holiday falls on a Saturday, it shall be celebrated on the preceding Friday. When a holiday falls on Sunday, the following Monday shall be observed as a holiday. For full-time employees on a work week other than Monday through Friday the city council shall designate the work day that shall be observed as a holiday. 
(2)	Holidays on scheduled work days: Employees who are required to work on the observed holiday shall be granted a work day of leave. 
(3)	Eligibility for holiday pay: In order to receive pay for an observed holiday, an employee must not have been absent without leave either on the work day before or after the holiday. 
(4)	Overtime for holidays: See section 15-65(2). 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 2(V), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-83. - Annual leave. 
    Annual vacation is to be provided as follows: 
(1)	Each employee shall receive annual leave at the rate of one day per month or twelve (12) days per year. Accumulation of annual leave will begin on the first day of employment. 
(2)	The annual vacation leave days are to be accumulated during a calendar year, with a maximum carry-over of ten (10) days each January 1st. Salary in lieu of vacation time will be paid. 
(1)	Separation and reinstatement: Employees dismissed for incompetence or inefficiency not involving personal misconduct will also receive all earned annual leave. All earned annual leave of employees who die while employed shall be paid cash to the spouse or the estate of said employee. Should any employee quit for any reason other than leave of absence and is re-employed, he will be counted as a new employee. 
(4)	Annual leave must be taken at the convenience of the department except in the case of sickness. 
(5)	Emergency employees are not eligible for annual leave. Example: Park summer employees and anyone working less than forty (40) hours per week. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 3(V), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-84. - Sick leave. 
(a)	Sick leave may be accumulated from year to year at the rate of one-half (1/2) day per month worked and may be accumulated not to exceed one hundred fifty (150) days. 
    Sick leave may be used for illness of employee or to attend to ill member of employee's immediate family. Employee applying for sick leave must furnish a doctor's certificate in event of absence in excess of three days. No advance sick leave will be allowed without prior approval of the city council. If an employee is sick beyond the number of days accumulated, he may use his accumulated annual vacation leave; however sick leave cannot be used as a vacation. 
(b)	Employees are expected to notify his/her superior one hour or more before starting time of inability to report to work. If employee retires on social security or city retirement plan, he shall be paid one-half (1/2) of total sick leave days earned or not to exceed seventy-five (75) days on special permission of the governing body. 
    If an employee is separated from the city for reason of personal misconduct or quits his job with the city voluntarily, the employee is not entitled to receive sick leave pay and the same is not transferred to pay. 
(c)	Workmens compensation: For absences for which workmen's compensation benefits are received, the employee may choose between receiving only his workmen's compensation benefits in which case no sick leave will be deducted or receiving his regular salary and turning in his workmen's compensation check to the city clerk and have the difference between his regular salary and the workmen's compensation check deducted from sick leave. 
    The personnel clerk and department heads are authorized to take all necessary steps to prevent abuses, to include dispatching a nurse or physician to verify illness, or to require a medical examination as evidence of physical condition. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 4(V), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-85. - Bereavement leave. 
    The classified employees will be credited with three (3) working days of leave for the death of an immediate family member, provided they occur on a scheduled work day. A work day will calculated at eight (8) hours. The three (3) days are considered to be a day before, the day of, and the day after the funeral. If an employee is notified of the death on a scheduled work day and is released from his duties, a sick leave day will be credited for that day. Any additional time that an employee requests after the bereavement leave has been exhausted will be against the employee annual leave, if available and will be granted as departmental schedules permit. Immediate family members will be considered to be: Wife, husband, daughter, son, brother, sister, mother, father, mother-in-law, son-in-law, father-in-law, grandparents, grandchildren, stepmother, step-father, brother-in-law, sister-in-law. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 5(V), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-86. - Military leave. 
    Military leave means training and service duty performed by an inductee, enlisted or reservists, or any entrant into a temporary component of the armed forces of the United States, to include time spent in reporting and returning from such training in service or, if rejection occurs, from the place of reporting for service. It also includes active duty training as a reservist in the armed forces of the United States or as a member of the National Guard of the United States. 
(1)	Eligibility. Any full-time employee who has completed his probationary period and who leaves the classified service for compulsory military duty shall be placed on military leave without pay; such leave to extend through a date of ninety (90) days after his release from the classified service. Also, a full-time employee who has completed his probationary period shall be granted a leave of absence for the purpose of being inducted or otherwise entering military service. If not accepted for such duty, the employee shall be reinstated in his position without loss of status or reduction pay. 
(2)	Restoration. An employee returning from military leave shall be entitled to restoration to his former position, providing he makes application within ninety (90) days after his release from duty and is physically and mentally capable of performing the duty involved. 
(3)	Disposition of pay and sick leave. A regular employee who leaves the service directly for such military leave without pay may elect to be paid for any accrued vacation as he may be entitled to if he were actually separated from the service. If the employee elects not to be paid for such leave, the accrued leave credit shall be reinstated upon return of the employee. Employees returning to duty under this provision shall have unused sick leave credits restored for their use. 
(4)	Any employee who is a member of the National Guard of Alabama or reserve officer or enlisted man in the Army or Navy or Marine Corps or Air Force reserve shall be granted leave of absence with pay for the purpose of attending an encampment of such organization for training when so ordered by military authority. The maximum military leave with pay shall not exceed twenty-one (21) days in any calendar year. (refer to: title 35, Section 185(13)(a) Code of Alabama 1958, recompiled as amended). 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 6(V), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-87. - Leave without pay. 
    The governing body may grant leaves without pay for a period not to exceed one year when it is in the interest of the local government to do so. At the expiration of the leave without pay, the employee has the right to, and shall be reinstated to, the position he vacated if the position still exists, or, if not, to any other vacant position in the same class. Approved leave without pay shall not constitute a break in service. 
(1)	Unexplained absences. Unexplained absences shall not be compensable nor charged as paid leave time. Leave of any category in excess of that authorized shall be charged as leave without pay and deduction made from pay for that period. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 7(V), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-88. - Educational leave. 
    The appointing authority may grant leave with or without pay, at his discretion for an employee to further his education when it is in the best interest of the City of Clanton. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 8(V), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-89. - Official duty leave. 
    An employee who is absent from work while on official business for the municipality, or while participating in training courses to which he has been assigned by the municipality, or while attending professional conferences and meetings authorized by the appointing authority, shall be granted leave with full pay without charge against annual leave. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 9(V), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-90. - Civil leave. 
    An employee called for service on a jury may be granted leave with full pay for the duration of the period for which called, unless released earlier, without charge against annual leave (not to exceed one week per year). 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 10(V), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-91. - Leave records. 
    All leave records shall be maintained by the personnel clerk and filed in the employee's personnel file. Leave slips to cover sick leave shall be prepared on the day of return. All other leave slips shall be prepared in advance. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 11(V), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-92. - Office hours. 
    Normal office hours are a nine (9) hour day. Where activities of a particular department require some other schedule to meet work load, the appointing authority may authorize a deviation from the normal schedule. A maximum of one hour is permitted for lunch and such time shall be considered noncompensable. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 12(V), 1-22-96) 
Secs. 15-93-15-110. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - EMPLOYEE BENEFITS 

Sec. 15-111. - Group health insurance. 
    After ninety (90) days of employment with the City of Clanton, the city will assume a determined amount (which is set by the governing body) of the payment of health insurance. No part-time employee shall be eligible for group health insurance. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 1(VI), 1-22-96; Ord. No. 12-01, 12-20-01) 
Sec. 15-112. - Social security. 
    The City of Clanton will follow routine procedures concerning Social Security on all employees. 
(Ord. No. 1-96, § 2(VI), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-113. - Retirement. 
    Each person employed full-time is required to join the Employee's Retirement System of Alabama. No part-time employee shall be eligible therefor, unless otherwise qualified. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 3(VI), 1-22-96; Ord. No. 12-01, 12-20-01) 
Sec. 15-114. - Workmen's compensation. 
    Each person is covered under Workmen's Compensation. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 4(VI), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-115. - Supplementary training program. 
    The city recognizes that improved skills and capabilities of its employees can be valuable from the viewpoint of both city and employee. Consequently, it is the city's policy to aid its employees to improve themselves through professional educational programs, seminars, workshops, and conference at the discretion of the governing body. 
(1)	Eligibility. All full-time employees will be eligible to attend programs for professional improvement. 
(2)	Approved courses. A program may be eligible if, in the opinion of the appointing authority it will either: 
a.	Improve the employee's ability to perform his present job, or
b.	Help prepare the employee for a job with the city which will demand a higher level of responsibility and/or skill. 
(3)	Financial consideration. The city may pay the cost of tuition, registration fee, books, and laboratory fees, travel, and meals, and lodging away from home. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 5(VI), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-116. - Physical examination for police officers. 
    All police officers now in the employment of the City of Clanton and all police officers hereafter employed by said city and on the anniversary date of said employment submit themselves to a physical examination by a qualified doctor of medicines to determine their physical fitness for the employment in which they are engaged by said city, including, but not limited to, a heart examination (EKG); heart rate; blood pressure; cholesterol count; optical, including sight and color blindness; ear and hearing and weight. 
(1)	The doctor giving the physical examination shall be designated by the city. The officer subject to the examination shall not be required to be examined by the doctor so designated, but may select a doctor of his own choice. 
(2)	In the event that the officer selects the doctor designated by the city, the expense of the examination shall be paid by the city and in the event that the officer selects a doctor of his own choice, the expense of the examination must be paid by the said officer. 
(3)	The doctor making the examination of said officer shall submit his report directly to the Chief of Police of the City of Clanton, together with a certificate to the effect: 
a.	That the officer is physically qualified to perform service as a police officer for the city. 
b.	That the officer is not physically qualified to perform his services as a police officer for the city. 
c.	That the officer is not physically qualified to perform his services as a police officer for the city; but, in the opinion of the doctor, the physical difficulty can be corrected within a period of three (3) months. 
d.	If the officer fails to qualify physically, the examining doctor shall direct a re-examination within period of three months to determine the question whether the officer then is physically fit to perform his duties as an officer for said city. All further examinations, treatments, corrections or other medical related matters following the re-examination be at officer's expense and the officer's responsibility. 
(4)	The height and weight of each officer shall be within ten (10) percent of the normal height-weight-age proportions accepted as normal by the examining doctor. 
(5)	The results of the examination, the re-examination and all subsequent examinations or medical reports, when received, shall be given to the personnel clerk and shall be made a part of the officer's personnel file, together with the certificate of the examining doctor, certifying that the officer is or is not physically capable of performing as a police officer. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 6(VI), 1-22-96) 
Secs. 15-117-15-130. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - IN-SERVICE TRAINING 

Sec. 15-131. - In-service training. 
    Department heads shall be responsible for developing the skills of their employees through in-service training, for investigating training programs outside the city government and referring municipal employees to those programs; and for making recommendations on whether the municipality should pay for such training. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 1(VII), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-132. - Working conditions; foremanship. 
    Department heads shall be held responsible for providing suitable and adequate working conditions within their means, and for making recommendations for correction not within their means of any conditions not suitable or adequate. Department heads shall further be held responsible for those matters normally associated with foremanship, such as providing employee safety training, handling employee complaints, explaining employee benefits and personnel systems, and development of employee morale and effectiveness. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 2(VII), 1-22-96) 
Secs. 15-133-15-150. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VIII. - RETIREMENT 

Sec. 15-151. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- 
Ord. No. 4-02, adopted April 8, 2002, repealed § 15-151 in its entirety. Formerly, said section pertained to normal retirement age as adopted by Ord. No. 01-96, adopted Jan. 22, 1996. See the Code Comparative Table. 
Sec. 156-152. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- 
Ord. No. 4-02, adopted April 8, 2002, repealed § 15-152 in its entirety. Formerly, said section pertained to physical requirements beyond normal retirement age as adopted by Ord. No. 01-96, adopted Jan. 22, 1996. See the Code Comparative Table. 
Sec. 15-153. - [Honorable service; twenty years or more.] 
    Any person who, at the time of his or her retirement, is employed by the City of Clanton Police Department and who retires after twenty (20) years or more of honorable service, shall receive, as part of his or her retirement benefits, without cost to said retiring officer, his or her badge and pistol. 
(Ord. No. 04-2001, 5-23-01) 
Sec. 15-154. - [Award of badge for officer killed in the line of duty.] 
    Any police officer of the City of Clanton who is killed in the line of duty shall have provided to the deceased officer's survivor, as determined by the deceased officer's department head, the badge which was assigned to said officer at the time of his or her death. 
(Ord. No. 04-2001, 5-23-01) 
Sec. 15-155. - Disability at retirement. 
    Any police officer of the City of Clanton who is deemed disabled, and eligible for retirement as a result of any injury received by said officer in the line of duty, shall be provided by the City of Clanton at no cost to such officer a retirement badge such as is provided to regularly retired officers with twenty (20) years or more service. 
(Ord. No. 04-2001, 5-23-01) 
Secs. 15-156-15-170. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IX. - EMPLOYEE COMPLAINT OR GRIEVANCE PROCEDURE 

Sec. 15-171. - Purpose. 
(a)	To insure employees a procedure by which their complaints can be considered rapidly, fairly, and without reprisal. 
(b)	To encourage the employee to express himself about the conditions of work as they affect him as an employee. 
(c)	To promote better understanding of policies, practices, and procedures which affect employees. 
(d)	To instill confidence in employees that personnel actions are taken in accord with established, fair and uniform policies and procedures. 
(e)	To develop in supervisors a greater sense of responsibility in their dealings with employees. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 1(IX), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-172. - Definition. 
    A grievance is a complaint, view or feeling that insufficient consideration or unfair treatment has been given to an individual or group within a department pertaining to employment conditions, to relationships between an employee and his supervisor or to relationships of an employee and other employees. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 2(IX), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-173. - Grievance policy. 
(a)	Purpose. The most effective accomplishment of the work the of municipality requires prompt consideration and equitable adjustment of the employee grievances. It is the desire of the municipality to adjust the cause of grievances informally, and both supervisors and employees are expected to make every effort to resolve problems as they arise. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 3(IX), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-174. - Grievance procedures. 
(a)	Within seven (7) calendar days after an employee knows, or should have known, of an alleged violation or misapplication of a city personnel rule, regulation or procedure, the employee must submit his grievance to his immediate supervisor for initial settlement. 
(1)	The supervisor will provide the employee an answer with in five (5) calendar days of this initial meeting. 
(2)	A record is not required to be made of this discussion. However, if the supervisor does make a written record, a copy of such record will be provided the personnel clerk for inclusion in the employee's personnel file. The employee will also be provided a copy of the record. 
(b)	Upon receipt of the supervisor's decision, or non-response, or when the employee is appealing a disciplinary action taken against him/her, the employee may file a written petition to the city personnel clerk. The employee will address the written petition to the personnel clerk and deliver it to the clerk within five (5) calendar days from the supervisor's decision or non-response. 
(1)	The personnel clerk may confer with the employee, the appointing authority, and any other affected city officer and/or official. 
(2)	A copy of this petition and reply from the personnel clerk will be included in the employee's personnel file. 
(3)	The written petition will contain as a minimum the following information:
a.	A statement of the rules, regulations or procedures that have been violated or misapplied with the dates and description of such violation or misapplication; or, the disciplinary action that is being appealed; 
b.	The specific remedy which is being sought;
c.	Previous supervisory decisions, if any;
(c)	Upon receipt of the personnel clerk's decision, or non-response, the employee may appeal to the City of Clanton Personnel Board. 
(1)	Within five (5) days after the personnel clerk's decision, or none response the employee may file a written appeal to the City of Clanton Personnel Board. The petition will contain the same information as in subsection (b)(3) and should be addressed to the chairman of the personnel board and delivered to the personnel clerk. 
(d)	Upon the hearing of said appeal the board will receive all evidence in support of the action and any evidence of other facts offered by such employee against such action. 
(e)	The hearing will be informally conducted and governed by rules of practice and procedure adopted by the board. The board will not be bound by the technical rules of evidence. The board will hear the employee's appeal, gather pertinent documents, interview witnesses as necessary, and prepare a written statement of facts. The employee and his/her supervisor and/or appointing authority will each have the right to appear before the board with reasonable representation of their choice, it they so desire. The board may continue the hearing from time to time as may be necessary. 
(f)	At the conclusion of the hearing, the board will render a recommendation to the governing body that either: 
(1)	Affirms the action taken, if it is reasonably satisfied that the action taken was lawful, proper, and/or not too severe; 
(2)	Reverses the action taken, if it is reasonably satisfied that the action taken was not lawful or proper; 
(3)	Modifies the action taken and prescribes a lesser penalty or action, if the board is reasonably satisfied that the employee should be subject to some penalty or action, but the penalty or action was too severe. If the board's recommendation reduces the severity of the action taken against the employee, the board may provide in its recommendation that the employee be reinstated with or without pay for his/her lost time. 
(g)	Within ten (10) calendar days of the receipt of the recommendations of the personnel board, the municipal governing body shall make the final determination in the case. The decision of the municipal governing body shall be final. If the municipal governing body fails to take action within ten (10) calendar days or the receipt of the recommendations of the personnel board, the recommendations of the personnel board shall be final.
