(h)	The board may be represented by the city attorney. The attorney will perform such duties as the board may direct and/or require. Any compensation paid said attorney will be paid by the governing body from the general fund. 
(i)	Forms to used in grievance procedures will be made available by the personnel clerk.
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 4(IX), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-175. - Protection. 
    No employee shall be disciplined or discriminated against in any way because of his proper use of the grievance procedure. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 5(IX), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-176. - Grievance procedure for complaints prohibited by the Americans With Disabilities Act. 
(a)	A complaint should be filed in writing or verbally, contain the name and address of the person filing it, and briefly describe the alleged violation of the regulations. 
(b)	A complaint should be filed within seven (7) days after the complainant becomes aware of the alleged violation. 
(c)	An investigation, as may be appropriate, will follow a filing of a complaint. The investigation will be conducted by the community development director. These rules contemplate informal but thorough investigations, affording all interested persons and their representatives, if any, an opportunity to submit evidence relevant to a complaint. 
(d)	A written determination as to the validity of the complaint and a description of the resolution, if any, will be issued by the community development director and a copy forwarded to the complainant no later than ten (10) days after filing. 
(e)	The Section 504/ADA coordinator will maintain the files and records of the City of Clanton relating to the complaints filed. 
(f)	The complainant can request a reconsideration of the case in instances where he or she is dissatisfied with the resolution. The request for reconsideration should be made within seven (7) days to the mayor. The mayor and council will hear the employee's grievance, gather pertinent documents, interview witnesses as necessary and prepare a written statement of fact. Within ten (10) working days of the hearing, the mayor and council will make the final determination in the case. 
(g)	The right of a person to a prompt and equitable resolution of the filed complaint will not be impaired by the person's pursuit of other remedies such as the filing of a Section 504 or ADA complaint with the responsible federal department or agency. Using this grievance procedure in [is] not a prerequisite to the pursuit of other remedies. 
(h)	These rules will be construed to protect the substantive rights of interested persons, meet appropriate due process standards and assure that the City of Clanton complies with the ADA, section 5-4 and their implementing regulations. 
    Complaints should be addressed to: 
Community Development Director 
P.O. Box 580 
Clanton, Al. 35046 
Telephone (205) 755-6840 
E-mail: obie@hiwaay.net 
(Ord. No. 5-02, 4-8-02) 
Editor's note- 
Ord. No. 5-02, adopted April 8, 2002, was not specifically amendatory of the Code and has been added as § 15-176 at the editor's discretion. 
Cross reference- Discrimination and Sexual Harassment, Ch. 2, art. V. 
Secs. 15-177-15-190. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE X. - CONDUCT, WORK HABITS, ATTITUDE 

Sec. 15-191. - General. 
    It shall be the duty of each employee to maintain high standards of conduct, cooperation, efficiency in their work for the local government. When ever work habits, attitude, production or personal conduct of any employee falls below the established standard, supervisors should point out the deficiencies at the time they are observed. Corrections and suggestions should be presented in a constructive and helpful manner in an effort to elicit the cooperation and goodwill of the employee. Whenever possible, oral and/or written warnings with sufficient time for improvement shall precede formal discipline. Copies of all written warnings shall be furnished to the personnel clerk for inclusion in the employee's personnel file. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 1(X), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-192. - Discipline policy. 
    It shall be the duty of all public employees to comply with and to assist in carrying into effect the provisions of the personnel rules and regulations. No employee shall be disciplined except for violation of established rules and regulations; and such discipline shall be in accordance with procedures established by the personnel rules and regulations. 
(a)	Employee's and supervisor's responsibilities. 
(1)	It is the duty of every employee to attempt to correct any faults in his performance when called to his attention and to make every effort to avoid conflict with the City of Clanton rules and regulations. 
(2)	It is the duty of every supervisor to discuss improper or inadequate performance with the employee in order to correct the deficiencies and to avoid the need to exercise disciplinary action. Discipline shall be, whenever possible, of an increasingly progressive nature, the step of progression being (a) reprimand (b) suspension, (c) demotion, (d) removal. 
(b)	Grounds for action. The following are declared to be grounds for reprimanding, suspending demoting or removing any full-time employee. Offenses are grouped with a summary of the recommended disciplinary actions, for each group. These offenses and actions, as described, are neither all inclusive nor automatic. Supervisors are permitted, and expected, to treat individuals situations according to the circumstances and facts involved. 
(1)	Group one offenses. 
a.	Such offenses include, but are not limited to, the situations listed below:
1.	Failure to give proper notice of an absence which could be anticipated;
2.	Irregular attendance and/or excessive absenteeism; "Excessive absenteeism is defined as taking time off without accrued or approved leave"; 
3.	Tardiness (not at his/her assigned work station at the beginning of the first hour of the employee's work day). 
4.	Interfering with the work of others to include offensive personal habits which interfere with efficient operations; 
5.	Excessive inefficiency to include waste, loafing leaving the work area without permission, excessive time for break, and defective workmanship; 
6.	Violation of normal safety practices to include failure to report a work related accident or injury and accident proneness; 
7.	Improper use and/or care of City property;
8.	Misconduct to include lack of cooperation, contravention of civil law, and any disgraceful conduct which reflects unfavorably on the City as an employer; 
9.	Willful and/or repeated failure to honor court judgements;
10.	Promiscuous behavior as related to job duties;
11.	Similar violations that meet the intended definition for group one offense.
(2)	Summary of recommended disciplinary actions for group one offenses. 
a.	First offense-Formal counseling.
b.	Second offense-Written warning.
c.	Third offense-Final written warning or suspension without pay or dismissal as appropriate. A suspension without pay dismissal will require a due process hearing be held by the appointing authority prior to the effective date of the action. 
(3)	Group two offenses. 
a.	Such offenses include, but are not limited to, the situations below:
1.	Possession and/or use of alcohol, unprescribed dangerous drugs, or similar intoxicants while on city property or on the job (employees other that law enforcement personnel in the line of duty); 
2.	Operating a city vehicle or city equipment while under the influence of intoxicants such as alcohol, unprescribed dangerous drugs, and/or prescribed drugs which induce an unsafe mental and/or physical state. 
3.	Loss of a driver's license and/or driving privileges by due process of law, when the employee's job requires the operation of a motor vehicle in the performance of his/her duties; 
4.	No employee of the City of Clanton shall be permitted to bring onto any city property or into any city vehicle any pistol, gun, or firearm of any description or any deadly weapon other than law enforcement personnel in the line of duty. 
5.	Falsifications of records and/or personal misrepresentation of statements given to a supervisor, official, the public, or the personnel board; 
6.	Dishonesty as related to an individual's job duties and/or profession;
7.	Fighting, except when the employee is a victim of an unwarranted assault;
8.	Gross insubordination;
9.	Conviction of a serious criminal offense;
10.	Theft destruction, careless or negligent use, or willful damage of city property or property of others; 
11.	Dangerous horseplay on the job;
12.	Flagrant violation of safety practices that might endanger the life or health of the employee or others; 
13.	Serious violation of city administrative regulations, department rules, lawful orders or directions made or given by a supervisor; 
14.	Membership in any organization which advocates the overthrow of the government of the United States by force or violence; 
15.	Acceptance of any consideration of value or gratuity which was given to improperly influence the employee in the performance of his/her duties; 
16.	Refusal to be examined by a city authorized fully licensed physician when so directed for cause by the city; 
17.	Political activities that are gross violation of federal and/or sate laws;
18.	Sexual harassment;
19.	Sleeping on the job;
20.	Incompetency or repeated inefficiency in the performance of duties;
21.	Abusive personal conduct or language toward the public or fellow employees, or abusive public criticism of a superior or other city official; 
22.	Willful violation of any duty adopted city policy, or state/federal law or regulation governing public employment; 
23.	Conduct or actions determined to be a conflict of interest as defined by state law;
24.	Fraudulent misrepresentation in securing an appointment or promotion in the city service;
25.	Repeated violation of group one offense;
26.	Similar violation that meet the intended definition of a group two offense.
(4)	Summary of recommended disciplinary actions for group two offenses. 
a.	The first such offense normally constitutes grounds for dismissal.
1.	This is not automatic, the appointing authority is permitted and expected to treat individual situations according to the circumstances and facts involved. 
2.	Due process procedures as established by federal law will be strictly adhered to whenever any anticipated disciplinary action will result in suspension without pay or dismissal. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 2(X), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-193. - Types of discipline. 
(a)	Reprimand. A department head or an authorized designee may, for disciplinary purposes, reprimand an employee in his department for cause. 
(1)	Formal counseling a reprimand may include formal counseling, at the first indication of unacceptable conduct that does not warrant more serious disciplinary action, the supervisor in charge will discuss the situation with the employee so that both may offer suggestions to deal with the problem. A formal counseling report will be prepared to establish a record of this counseling. A copy of the formal counseling report will be forwarded to the personnel clerk for inclusion in the employee's personnel file. 
(2)	Written warning-Repeated or continued employee misconduct that does not warrant more serious disciplinary action, will result in the supervisor issuing the employee a written warning report. Such warning will include the reasons for the warning and inform the employee that further unacceptable conduct will result in more severe disciplinary action such as suspension without pay or separation. A copy of any written warning report issued will be forwarded to the personnel clerk for inclusion in an employee's personnel file. 
(b)	Suspensions. The supervisor in charge, with the concurrence of the appointing authority may, for disciplinary purposes, suspend an employee without pay for a length of time as he considers appropriate, however, that no employee may be suspended for more than thirty (30) working days in any twelve (12) consecutive months. 
(c)	Demotions or reductions in salary. With the prior approval of the appointing authority, a supervisor may reduce the salary of an employee within the range provided in the pay plan or demote the employee for cause to a lower grade. 
(d)	Dismissals. With the prior approval of the appointing authority, a supervisor may dismiss an employee for cause, as long as the appointing authority meets the intent of these policies and procedures. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 3(X), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-194. - Operators of city-owned motor vehicles. 
    Purpose. The City of Clanton is committed to insuring that its fleet operations are conducted in a safe and efficient manner. This policy addresses specific responsibilities of those employed whose job duties require that they operate city vehicles or equipment and applies to the City of Clanton employees of all categories. It is the responsibility of these employees to familiarize themselves with this policy and its requirements. 
    Definition of city vehicle. A city vehicle is any vehicle or equipment that is owned, leased, rented or loaned to the City of Clanton. 
    Drivers license requirements. 
(a)	Prospective and current employees whose job duties include the operation of a city vehicle must be in possession of a valid and current driver's license to include the appropriate class of commercial license for the vehicle being operated. Under no circumstance shall a city employee whose license has been cancelled, revoked, suspended, or expired operate a city vehicle. 
(b)	Any employee whose job duties include the operation of a city vehicle, shall, within, twenty-four (24) hours notify his/her department head of any change in the status of their drivers license. Failure to immediately report a change in the status of a license shall result in disciplinary action. 
    Motor Vehicle Record (MVR) requirements. 
(a)	Applicants for positions with the City of Clanton that require driving a city vehicle will have his/her current MVR reviewed prior to employment. If the MVR has greater than eight (8) points in the preceding twenty-four (24) month period listed for traffic violations or a conviction or pending charge for driving under the influence during that period, that applicant will be disqualified for consideration. 
(b)	All employees whose job requires a drivers license shall perform a MVR check every three (3) years during their birth month. This review shall be the responsibility of the employee. Supervisors shall be responsible for verifying that all other employees have a valid driver's license prior to operating a City of Clanton vehicle. 
(c)	Anytime a MVR for a current employee whose job duties include the operation of a city vehicle is found to have received more than eight (8) points in the preceding twenty-four (24) months (according to the points scale for the State of Alabama UTC defense codes); said employee shall be required to attend a city approved defense driving course at said persons expense. The employee will have two (2) weeks to present a certificate of completion to their department head or their driving privileges will be suspended until such certification is presented. 
    Seat belt use. Seat belt use in city vehicles is mandatory for all drivers and passengers in city vehicles. Failure to utilize seat belts shall result in disciplinary action. These offenses shall be treated as "minor offenses" in accordance with the City of Clanton disciplinary action. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 4(X), 1-22-96; Ord. No. 2-06, § 4, 1-23-06) 
Sec. 15-195. - Requirements of the Drug Free Work Place Act of 1988. 
    The Drug Free Work Act of 1988 requires the City of Clanton, as a recipient of certain federal grants, to certify to the United States Government that it will maintain a drug free work place. As part of that required certification and consistent with our existing personnel policies, we are hereby notifying each of our employees that the unlawful manufacture, distribution, dispensing, possession, or use of a controlled substance is prohibited in our work place. "Controlled substance" means a controlled substance as defined in Schedules I through V of section 202 of the Controlled Substances Act (21 USC Section 812) and as further defined in the Federal Regulations at 21 CFR Section 1308.11 through 1308.15 and other federal and state laws. Any employee who violates this policy may be subject to discipline up to and including termination by the appropriate authority. 
    Pursuant to the requirement of the Act, each of our employees is hereby notified that as a condition of employment, the employee will: 
(1)	Abide by our Drug Free Work Place Policy as set forth above and
(2)	Notify the City of Clanton (specifically the personnel administration) of any criminal drug statue conviction for a violation occurring in the work place no later than five (5) days after the conviction. The personnel administration shall notify the council as required by law, of such conviction within ten (10) days of receiving notice thereof. Within the same day period, appropriate remedial steps or sanctions shall be taken against the employee which may include termination of employment by the appropriate authority. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 5(X), 1-22-96) 
Secs. 15-196-15-210. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XI. - POLITICAL ACTIVITY 

Sec. 15-211. - Political limitations. 
    No officer, agent, or employee of the city, other than persons subject to popular election shall: 
(1)	become a candidate for election, or appointment to elective office;
(2)	take an active part in any political campaign, or distribute badges, pamphlets or handbills of any kind favoring or opposing any candidate for nomination or election to municipal office. 
(3)	Except that any person who wished to do or may take a leave of absence.
(4)	Except that no person shall be denied the right to participate in county and state political activities to the same extent as any other citizen of the State of Alabama, except where limited by federal or state law. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 1(XI), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-212. - Affiliation. 
    Nothing in this section shall be construed to prevent any employee from becoming or continuing to be a member of a political party or from attendance at a political party or from attendance at a political meeting, or from enjoying entire freedom from all interference in casting his vote. He officer, agent, or employee of the municipality shall make or solicit contributions or donations to any political campaign. 
(1)	Political pressure. Employees of the City of Clanton shall not be appointed or retained on the basis of their political activity, or affiliation. Employee shall not be coerced to take part in political campaigns, to solicit votes, to levy, contribution or solicit funds or support for the purpose of supporting or opposing the appointment or election of candidates for any elected office. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 2(XI), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-213. - Disciplinary action. 
    Any employee in violation of this section of the personnel rules and regulations shall be subject to disciplinary action up to and including dismissal. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 3(XI), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-214. - Outside employment. 
    No full-time employee in the classified service shall accept outside employment, whether part-time, temporary or permanent, if such employment conflicts or interferes, or is likely to conflict or interfere, with the employee's public service. No employee shall engage in or accept private employment or render any service for private interest when such employment or service is incompatible or creates a conflict of interest with his official duties. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 4(XI), 1-22-96) 
Secs. 15-215-15-230. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XII. - PERSONNEL BOARD 

Sec. 15-231. - Selection of members. 
    The appointing authority shall, with the approval of the governing body, and within thirty (30) days after the effective date of these rules and regulations, appoint a personnel board of three (3) members. The initial members shall be appointed on the basis as follows: 
The first member shall be appointed for a term of one year. 
The second member shall be appointed for a term of two (2) years. 
The third member shall be appointed for a term of three (3) years. 
Each successor appointment shall be for a full term of three (3) years. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 1(XII), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-232. - Qualifications. 
(a)	Persons appointed to the board:
(1)	Shall be in agreement with the basic policies and principal of merit employment.
(2)	Shall be qualified voters of the municipality.
(3)	Shall have resided in the municipality for at least four (4) years immediately prior to their appointment. 
(b)	Persons may not be a member of the board while:
(1)	Residing outside the corporate limits.
(2)	Employed by the municipality.
(3)	Holding an appointive or elective offices.
(4)	Running for an elective public office.
(5)	Serving as an officer of a political party.
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 2(XII), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-233. - Removals and vacancies. 
    If, during the term for which he is appointed to the board, a member is absent from three (3) consecutive meetings without excuse from the appointing authority, his position on the board shall become vacant. 
    A member of the board may be removed from the board for just cause by the appointing authority with the approval of two-thirds (2/3) of the members of the governing body. 
    The appointing authority, by appointment approved by the governing body, fills all vacancies on the board. A person appointed to fill such a vacancy shall hold the position on the board for the remainder of the unexpired term of the person who leaves the position vacant. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 3(XII), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-234. - Duties and procedures. 
(a)	The board shall elect its own chairman and establish its own rules of procedure.
(b)	The board will meet upon call of the chairman, or upon call of two members, or upon request of the appointing authority or the governing body. In addition the board will meet as required to hold hearing in accordance with its own rules and these policies and procedures. 
(c)	Notice of all board meetings will be given to each member and to other interested parties by the chairman. Two (2) members will constitute to a quorum for the transaction of any business which may properly come before the board. 
(d)	The board shall upon request of the local governing body or upon its on initiative, inquire into the administration of the personnel system and, on the basis of the inquiry make written recommendations regarding the system to the governing body. The board, as a whole, shall have access to any records necessary to its inquiry as long as it does not conflict with the privacy act. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 4(XII), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-235. - Clerk of the board. 
    The board shall designate in coordination with the governing body, a clerk to assist the board as necessary in carrying out its duties. The person so designated may be an employee of the city in some other capacity as agreed to between the board and the governing body. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 5(XII), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-236. - Expenses of the board. 
    The city council will make necessary appropriations from the general fund to pay reasonable board expenses that are incurred in carrying out it's responsibilities. Each board may be compensated from the general fund as established by the city council. 
    The board may call upon the city attorney to render such legal service to the board as the board deems necessary or advisable. Expense for the attorney's time shall be paid from the general fund. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 6(XII), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-237. - Records. 
    The board will maintain adequate records to ensure proper documentation of all its actions. All board records, except those which the rules of the board and/or state law require to be confidential will be open for review upon reasonable request. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, § 7(XII), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-238-15-250. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XIII. - DRUG/ALCOHOL TESTING POLICY 

Sec. 15-251. - Drug/alcohol testing policy. 
(a)	Purpose. The goal of this policy is to establish a drug/alcohol testing program to enforce the city's goal of having all employees free from abuse or illegal use of drugs and alcohol. 
(b)	Conditions allowing for testing. 
(1)	Employment applicants. Applicants for all City of Clanton positions shall be tested for drug usage as part of their pre-employment medical examinations as a condition of employment. Pre-employment drug testing will occur at or near the final stage of the hiring process. Applicants will be notified prior to drug testing. Refusal to take the test, or test results reporting a presence of illegal drugs, or the illegal use of controlled substances, shall be a basis for rejecting an applicant in the selection process. 
(2)	Municipal employees. Only an employee's department head with the advice and approval of the mayor and the personnel administrator may order a drug or alcohol test. Department heads are subject to the same testing procedure and may be ordered to take a drug or alcohol test by the mayor. In the event of the absence incapacity, or unavailability of the official whose consent to a drug or alcohol test is necessary, the person acting in the capacity of such official may order or approve a drug or alcohol test. Any action taken against any employee as a result of this policy shall be determined by the individual circumstances of each case, and disciplinary action up to and including termination is possible by the appropriate authority. 
Any employee may be subjected to drug or alcohol testing only if there exist a reasonable suspicion that the employee is using illegal drugs; 2) using legal drugs illegally, or; 3) under the influence of alcohol during working hours or while operating city vehicles or equipment. (Tests for alcohol shall be given by a certified operator on the intoxllyzer 5000). 
Use of the term "under the influence" does not mean that the employee must be legally intoxicated as defined by State Law. 
Reasonable suspicion shall mean one or more of the following: 
a.	Apparent unusual or bizarre conduct, or physical conditions, appearance or speech, which would indicate that the employee is under the influence of drugs or alcohol; 
b.	Involvement in an accident during working hours or while operating city vehicles or equipment for which no reasonable explanation exists; 
c.	Involvement in a series or pattern of work accidents;
d.	Continued or excessive absenteeism or tardiness after receiving discipline for such conduct; 
e.	Indictment, arrest, or conviction for controlled substances offenses;
f.	The smell of an alcoholic beverage on the breath;
g.	Illegal possession of drugs, or possession of alcohol on work premises or while operating a city vehicle or equipment; 
h.	Any other objective fact or facts, and reasonable inferences drawn therefrom, which would lead a reasonable person to suspect that the employee is using illegal drugs, is using legal drugs illegally, or is under the influence of alcohol during working hours or while operating city vehicles or equipment. 
(3)	Written documentation stating the grounds for reasonable suspicion shall be provided by the department head to the personnel administrator and mayor prior to the ordering of such a test for an employee. 
(4)	Refusal by an employee to take the test shall be deemed insubordination, and shall be the basis of disciplinary action that may be administrated by the appropriate authority. 
(c)	Testing procedure. Detailed testing procedures shall be developed by the city for the following purposes: 
(1)	Positively identify the person to be tested.
(2)	Reasonably accommodate personal privacy and provide security of samples.
(3)	Establish if the person to be tested is taking drugs legally.
(4)	Insure accuracy of results by confirming positive results with gas chromatography or thin layer chromatography. 
(d)	Testing agent. The laboratory selected to conduct the analysis must be certified, experienced and capable of quality control documentation, chain of custody, technical expertise, and demonstrated proficiency. 
(e)	Voluntary rehabilitation. Any employee who voluntarily comes forth and request assistance will be placed in a rehabilitation program. This action on the employee's part will not constitute a violation. 
(f)	Positive results. Employee applicants who test positive for illegal drug use shall be denied employment with the city. Employees who test positive for illegal drug use or being under the influence of alcohol during working hours or while operating city vehicles or equipment shall be subject to discipline up to and including termination by the appropriate authority. Nothing in the city's policy of providing and enforcing a drug-free work place shall be construed as precluding discipline for any act or acts committed by an employee who also tests positive for drugs or alcohol. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, XIII(§ A), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-252. - Medical review officer. 
    The Medical Review Officer for the City of Clanton shall be appointed by the testing agent or his designee who shall be Certified Medical Doctor. The role of the Medical Review Officer is to review and interpret positive test results prior to the transmission or results to the city personnel administrator. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, XIII(§ B), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-253. - Reservation of authority. 
    The city council reserves the authority to amend, modify, or change this policy. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, XIII(§ C), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-254. - Approval and effective date. 
    All requirement to comply with the Drug Free Work Place Act of 1988 shall become effective immediately upon adoption of this policy. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, XIII(§ D), 1-22-96) 
Sec. 15-255. - Drug/alcohol testing procedures. 
(a)	General procedures. 
(1)	Procedures for drugs and alcohol testing shall comply with the provisions of the City of Clanton drug testing policy. 
(2)	All applicants for employment will be drug tested. All positive screens will be confirmed once by methods and procedures as outlined below. Results of drug test on applicants not hired for whatever reason will be kept in the personnel files and shall be confidential. There will be no access to these files except by approval of the appropriate authority. If a positive confirmation is received, the applicant will be deemed conclusively to have not passed the pre-employment physical and will not be eligible, for employment with the city. 
(3)	For employees, only the employee's department head with the advice and approval of the mayor and personnel administrator may order a drug or alcohol test. Department heads may be ordered to take a drug or alcohol test by the mayor. In the event of the absence, incapacity, or unavailability of any official whose consent to a drug or alcohol test is necessary, the person acting in the capacity of such official may order or approve a drug or alcohol test. 
(4)	Collection of the specimen for testing employment applicants will be done as scheduled by the personnel department. Alcohol testing will be performed by the City of Clanton Police Department. For employees to be tested site. Under no circumstances will the employee be allowed to drive or operate any machinery if drug or alcohol uses is suspected. After the specimen is provided, the employee will be driven home and remain off duty on leave with pay until such time as the results of the tests are known. 
(5)	Before testing an employee, written documentation of reasonable suspicion will be provided to the personnel department by the employee's department head. 
(b)	Specific procedures: 
To ensure accurate, valid, legal, specimens. 
Procedures for collecting urine specimens shall allow individual privacy; however, at the same time the procedures shall be such as to reasonably insure the validity of the specimen. In the event the medical review officer of the testing agent as stated above or his designee has reason to believe that a particular individual may alter, substitute or otherwise engage in conduct that would impair the validity of the specimen, then a health-care provider of the same sex as the person being tested will witness the person urinate into the container being careful that sample substitution or tampering does not occur. There shall be only one witness. 
Note: This is the most critical step in the sample collection procedure as patients have been known to substitute another sample, dilute the sample by adding water, or contaminate the sample with other substances. Minimum same size is 30 cc. 
(c)	Counseling. 
(1)	If a positive test result for an employee is received by the personnel department, the mayor and the department head of the employee will be immediately notified. The personnel administrator or his/her designee and the employee's department head may meet to advise the employee as to treatment that is available or may proceed directly to disciplinary action. If the employee cannot be located, disciplinary action may be commenced in the employee's absence. 
(2)	First offense:
a.	The employee will be given an opportunity to provide documentation of any prescription medication taken and amounts prescribed if positive confirmation test is for FDA scheduled medication. The employee will still be subject to disciplinary action if the employee did not disclose to his or her supervisor that the employee was taking such medication and if the medication taken and documented is of such a nature that job duties would normally have been restricted by the personnel department or the supervisor. 
b.	Drug or alcohol rehabilitation. If the employee chooses this option, and the personnel administrator and department head concur attendance and completion of the course of rehabilitation will be mandatory. The employee will be allowed to use available, hospital days or leave as required at the department head and personnel administrator's discretion during this period. The employee must also remain drug free for the remainder of his employment with the city. This is to be determined by quarterly urine screens for a one year period. The employee's continued employment will also be dependent on the employee following through with all the rehabilitation center's recommendations. 
1.	If the employee does not attend or complete rehabilitation to the satisfaction of the rehabilitation specialist, he/she will be placed on leave without pay and subject to termination by the appropriate authority. 
(3)	Second offense employee will be subject to termination by the appropriate authority.
(d)	Confidentiality and records retention. The release of information regarding drug/alcohol testing will be handled in accordance with the City of Clanton's procedures on release of medical information subject to federal and state law regarding the release of drug and alcohol information. A general medical release executed by the employee shall not be sufficient to release results of drug or alcohol test unless the release specifically authorizes the disclosure of such information. Log sheets, specimen labels and test results will not have the employees name but rather will be coded to insure privacy. Tests results will be kept in a sealed envelope in the employee's personnel file. 
(e)	Voluntary drug/alcohol rehabilitation. If, before an incident of suspected drug use, or alcohol abuse during working hours, and employee voluntarily identifies himself to his/her department head, the personnel administrator or the mayor as having a chemical abuse problem and being in need of drug rehabilitation, he/she shall be placed on available, hospital or administrative leave as required at the discretion of the department head and personnel administrator. This incident shall not be counted against the employee; however, the employee should provide proof of completion of the rehabilitation before returning to duty and the employee shall remain drug free for the remaining course of his employment with the city to be determined by quarterly drug screens. These drug screens shall be performed for a one year period. 
(f)	Selling or possessing illegal drugs. Any employee who sells or possesses an illegal substance whole on or off duty, is subject to immediate suspension or termination by the appropriate authority. 
(Ord. No. 01-96, XIII(§ 3), 1-22-96) 
Chapter 16 - POLICE 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, Ch. 2; fire prevention and protection, Ch. 7; motor vehicles and traffic, Ch. 11; police services in police jurisdiction, § 2-5; arrests by members of fire department, § 7-4; levy of tax for sale and storage of gasoline, § 10-110; police chief notified of purchaser of precious metals or precious stones, § 10-358. (Back)
State Law reference- Chief of police authorized, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-5; establishment, organization, etc., of police force, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-55; civil service merit systems, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-180 et seq.; law enforcement officers generally, Code of Ala. 1975, § 36-21-1 et seq. (Back)
Sec. 16-1. - Training of police officers. 
    The policy of the city council is to upgrade the police force of the city by requiring that the police officers shall be required to successfully complete the acceptable accredited schooling or academics in order to comply with the basic and minimum requirements provided by law. 
(Code 1979, § 2-8) 
State law reference- Peace officers' standards and training commission, Code of Ala. 1975, § 36-21-40 et seq. 
Sec. 16-2. - Custody of stolen property, contraband pistols. 
    The chief of police of the city is appointed as the custodian of stolen property and the person authorized under Code of Ala. 1975, § 13A-11-84, to receive pistols; and such stolen property or contraband pistols shall be held by him as provided by law. 
(Code 1979, § 2-7) 
Sec. 16-3. - Method for determination of blood alcohol levels. 
    The city hereby adopts the Intoxilyzer 5000 as its means for analyzing the blood alcohol levels for those arrested by the city police department. 
(Ord. No. 2-86, § 1, 1-13-86) 
State law reference- Alabama Chemical Test for Intoxication Act, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5-190 et seq.; chemical tests, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-194. 
Sec. 16-4. - Police Department Directives Manual adopted. 
(a)	The City of Clanton Police Department Directives Manual submitted to city council in October of 2009 is hereby adopted, by reference, for application within the City of Clanton Police Department effective at the beginning of the City of Clanton's fiscal year on October 1, 2010. 
    The aforedescribed Police Department Directives Manual shall not replace the existing City of Clanton rules and regulations regarding employees and city operations, but shall rather be adopted in addition thereto as required for law enforcement employees and officials of the City of Clanton, Alabama. 
    A copy of said Police Department Directives Manual shall be placed in the office of the city clerk and the office of the police chief of the city, and shall be available for inspection and review by the public and/or related parties, during office hours, at any time upon request. 
(b)	An addition to the Police Department Directives Manual regarding immigration enforcement policy and procedures number D-8.0, submitted to city council in October 2011, is hereby adopted, by reference, for application within the City of Clanton Police Department effective immediately upon publication. 
(c)	An addition to the Police Department Directives Manual regarding reserve/auxiliary police officers and procedures number D-1.1, submitted to city council in March 2013, is hereby adopted, by reference, for application within the City of Clanton Police Department effective immediately upon publication. 
(Ord. No. 7-10, 7-26-2010; Ord. No. 5-11, 10-24-2011; Ord. No. 1-13, 3-11-2013) 
Chapter 17 - SOLID WASTE 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, Ch. 2; fire prevention and protection, Ch. 7; utilities, Ch. 20; burning of garbage, § 7-51 et seq. (Back)
State Law reference- Municipal powers as to health and sanitation, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-130 et seq.; municipal incinerators, hauling and disposal of garbage and trash, fees, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-135; solid waste generally, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-27-1 et seq.; methods of local waste collection and disposal, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-27-3; mutual agreements or contracts for solid waste disposal, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-27-5; hazardous wastes management, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-30-1 et seq. (Back)
Sec. 17-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Construction waste means all solid waste of every kind, nature and description connected with residential or commercial construction, including building materials and related solid waste in connection with such a construction project. 
    Garbage means all waste accumulations of animal, fruit or vegetable matter that attend the preparation, use, dealing in or storage of meat, fowl, fish or vegetables, including tin cans, paper, all refuse commonly referred to as household garbage, and all household and cafe refuse, including industrial waste and also leaves, shrubbery cuttings, limbs and the like. 
    Garbage cart means the lightweight plastic container furnished by the city to certain householders, apartments, trailer parks and businesses, equipped with wheels, having a capacity of eighty-five (85) gallons and equipped with a lid or cover. 
    Premises means any dwelling, rooming house, apartment building, hospital, school, hotel, club, restaurant, boarding house, cafè, shop, church, place of business, manufacturing establishment, store or public building. 
    Residence means a single- or multiple-family dwelling, duplex or apartment building, or a mobile home or trailer. 
    Rubbish means all solid waste, such as wood, wood by-products, and masonry materials. 
    Recyclables means all recyclables such as paper, cardboard, glass, aluminum, metal and similar materials. 
    Sanitary landfill means a place of dumping of garbage and rubbish or such place designated by the city or county. 
(Ord. No. 8-81, § 1, 7-27-81; Ord. No. 9-81, § 1, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, § 1, 4-11-94; Ord. No. 3-2001, 5-14-01) 
Sec. 17-2. - Collection and disposal service-Established; schedule. 
    The city hereby establishes a garbage, rubbish collection, and hauling service, to be operated by the city, with the disposal of such being contracted. The collection and hauling of garbage and rubbish shall be made by the city on a regular schedule of weekdays, not to include Saturday and Sunday in the residential areas and the business district of the city. All collection schedules are subject to change due to legal holidays and weather conditions. 
(Ord. No. 9-81, § 2, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, § 2, 4-11-94) 
Sec. 17-3. - Same-Service area; certificate of exception. 
(a)	The area to be served under this chapter shall include all areas located within the corporate limits of the city. In addition thereto, if a public road or street is situated in the perimeter line of the city limits, then the garbage or rubbish may be picked up from customers on both sides of the road or street, and garbage or rubbish may be picked up from customers at the end of dead-end streets when the dead-end street is adjacent to the existing corporate limits. 
(b)	Notwithstanding the provisions of subsection (a) of this section or other provisions of this chapter, a person may store, haul and dispose of his own solid wastes on his land or otherwise, provided such storage, haulage or disposal is accomplished pursuant to a certificate of exception as provided in Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-27-3(g). 
(Ord. No. 9-84, 11-13-84; Ord. No. 7-94, § 14, 4-11-94) 
Sec. 17-4. - Garbage cart or dumpster required. 
    Each dwelling, apartment, place of business, mobile home, hospital, school, restaurant, eating establishment, shop, church, and public building within the corporate limits of the city is required to have available a garbage cart or dumpster. Each person engaged in maintaining any such premises is hereby required to pay to the city the charge prescribed in this chapter. The city is hereby obligated to render each month a statement for the services performed by the city, which statement is due and payable according to the terms contained thereon. The statement for services performed by the city for the pickup and disposing of garbage, rubbish, trash and the like may be combined with the utility bill rendered by the city for other utilities furnished to the customer. Statements for services rendered may be mailed by the city to the customer and payment of the statement shall be made to the city. 
(Ord. No. 9-81, § 5, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, § 5, 4-11-94) 
Sec. 17-5. - Responsibility for pickup; unlawful dumping. 
(a)	It shall be the responsibility of the city to pick up garbage, trash and rubbish, as provided in this chapter. No garbage or rubbish will be picked up that is not deposited in a garbage cart or dumpster provided by the city. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for any person to dump or cause to be dumped any garbage, rubbish or trash upon any property not his own or under his control other than a sanitary landfill. 
(c)	It shall be unlawful to bring onto the property of the residence or the business any garbage as defined in this chapter for the purpose of placing the garbage into the garbage cart or the dumpster of the owner of such property, and it shall be unlawful to place in any garbage cart or dumpster any garbage brought onto the property of the residence or business being billed for the same. 
(Ord. No. 9-81, § 6, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, §§ 6, 16, 4-11-94) 
Sec. 17-6. - Placement of waste in receptacles. 
    All garbage, including rubbish and recyclables, must be placed in garbage carts or dumpsters in such a manner that all lids shall be fastened to prevent damage from vandalism, water or rodents. 
(Ord. No. 9-81, § 13, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, § 7, 4-11-94) 
Sec. 17-7. - Offensive or unsanitary accumulations. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person in possession, charge or control of any premises in the corporate limits of the city to keep, cause to be kept, or allow the keeping of any garbage, rubbish, trash or refuse in such a manner that it will become offensive to health or likely to cause disease. 
(Ord. No. 9-81, § 7, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, § 7, 4-11-94) 
Sec. 17-8. - Garbage carts-Generally. 
(a)	The city will provide each residence a lightweight trash and garbage container, equipped with lid and wheels, capable of being rolled from the residence to the curb of the street. The city will be responsible for repair or replacement of the container damaged through no fault of the resident. The resident will be responsible for cleaning of the container. 
(b)	The city assumes the responsibility to collect garbage and trash from the carts placed near the curb of the street according to the schedule adopted by the city, subject to change provided in this chapter. 
(c)	Upon proof of disability due to health, age or other reason, the city will continue to collect garbage from the carts placed near the back entrance of such residence. No collection personnel shall enter houses or buildings. 
(Ord. No. 9-81, § 3, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, § 3, 4-11-94) 
Sec. 17-9. - Same-Care. 
(a)	Each person subject to the provisions of this chapter will be responsible for the garbage cart assigned and must not abuse, remove or destroy the cart. If the service is discontinued for any reason, the garbage cart must be left on the premises vacated, and if the garbage cart is not left on the vacated premises the cost of the cart may be charged to the utility deposit refund. 
(b)	If any person shall deliberately abuse or destroy any garbage cart, the city may make a reasonable charge therefor. 
(Ord. No. 9-81, §§ 8, 10, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, §§ 8, 10, 4-11-94) 
Sec. 17-10. - Same-Placement of cart at curb. 
    It shall be the responsibility of each person desiring garbage to be picked up by the city to roll the garbage cart to a place near the curb of the street by 7:00 a.m. on the route day and to remove the cart from the curb no later than 7:00 p.m. on the route day. It shall be the responsibility of each person to determine the route day, and no garbage will be picked up by the city unless the cart is rolled to the curb, except as otherwise provided in this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 9-81, § 9, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, § 9, 4-11-94) 
Sec. 17-11. - Dumpsters. 
(a)	The city will make available dumpsters of sufficient size to meet the need of the customer. If a dumpster is required, the dumpster may be purchased from the city for cash or the customer may pay for the purchase of the dumpster in twelve (12) equal monthly payments to be billed separately from the utility bill. The dumpster shall remain the property of the city until the charges are fully paid. 
(b)	Garbage carts will be delivered to trailer parks only if the owner or manager thereof shall, in writing, be responsible for all carts, and garbage carts will be delivered only to apartment buildings having twenty (20) or less apartments therein. 
(Ord. No. 9-81, § 12, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, § 12, 4-11-94) 
Sec. 17-12. - Removal of tree limbs, yard waste, etc. 
    It shall be the obligation of each person contracting for the cutting of trees, bushes, shrubs or other growth from private property to arrange for the removal thereof, and nothing in this chapter shall be construed as obligating the city to remove such materials. In addition, it shall be the obligation of each person contracting for construction projects on private property to arrange for the removal of construction waste therefrom and nothing in this chapter shall be construed as obligating the city to remove such materials. 
(Ord. No. 9-81, § 11, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, § 11, 4-11-94; Ord. No. 3-2001, 5-14-01) 
Sec. 17-13. - Amount of charges. 
    On and after the adoption of this section [October 10, 2011] and continuing monthly thereafter, the following charges will be paid to the City of Clanton for hauling and disposing of garbage and rubbish. 
(1)	For each cart furnished to a single-family dwelling unit, public establishment, place of business, apartment, mobile home, restaurant, eating establishment, shop, church, or public building, the city hereby levies for each cart the sum of fifteen dollars ($15.00) per month in the event that not more than one (1) pickup per week is required. 
(2)	In the event that two (2) carts are required, [the charge shall be] thirty dollars ($30.00) per month for one (1) pickup. In the event three (3) carts are required, [the charge shall be] forty-five dollars ($45.00) per month for one (1) pickup. 
(3)	For each business, person, firm, or corporation requiring a dumpster, the monthly charge [shall be] sixty dollars ($60.00) per month where not more than one (1) pickup [per week] is required. There shall be charged an additional sixty dollars ($60.00) per month for each additional pickup per week required. 
(4)	In the event that a pickup of trash is required and where the same is not placed in a cart or dumpster, the first load of the same will be removed by City of Clanton with no charge being made. In the event that additional loads are required, the City of Clanton hereby assesses a charge for each load of fifty dollars ($50.00) after the first load per week. The trash under this provision in this section shall be brought out to a point at or near the curb and not placed under a power line, trees, or overhanging obstruction so as to hinder the removal thereof by heavy equipment. 
(Ord. No. 9-81, § 4, 9-14-81; Ord. No. 7-94, § 4, 4-11-94; Ord. No. 3-2001, 5-14-01; Ord. No. 4-11, 10-10-2011) 
Sec. 17-14. - Payment of charges; delinquency. 
(a)	All bills for service under this chapter shall be due and payable monthly. The charges shall be designated on the water and gas bill mailed out by the city for each month and such fees shall be paid when the bill is paid. The city shall not accept the payment of any utility bill unless the fee for garbage and trash service under this chapter is also paid. All fees collected under this chapter shall be net and all accounts shall be considered delinquent if not paid within the time limit specified in the utility bill so rendered by the city. All delinquent accounts for garbage pickup and disposal are subject to the same penalties as are in effect for the several departments of the city pertaining to delinquent accounts for utility services rendered by the city; provided, however, that failure to pay the garbage collection fee within thirty (30) days after the fee shall become due and payable shall subject the delinquent party to the penalty of the suspension of solid waste collection and disposal services, or the city may proceed to recover the amount of any such delinquency with interest in a civil action, or both. 
(b)	The water works and sewer board of the city is designated as the agent for collection of the garbage fees for services provided for in this chapter and shall remit the fees to the city clerk as they are collected. However, if the occupant or person in possession of a dwelling or store building has no water service furnished to him by the city or by the water works and sewer board of the city, the garbage fee provided in this chapter shall be paid at the city office of the city clerk once each month in accordance with the rates provided in this chapter and at the time designated as the due date of the payment. The payment shall become delinquent after ten (10) days. Any person paying the charge after the delinquent date shall pay a penalty of one dollar ($1.00) in addition to the garbage fee designated by this chapter. 
(c)	Any person who has not been issued a certificate of exception under Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-27-3(g) and who utilizes the solid waste disposal system of the city, and who fails to pay the fee, rate or charge established by the city council therefor, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be fined not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) and if the violation or failure or refusal to make such payment is a continuing one, each day's violation shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punished accordingly. 
(Code 1979, § 7-4) 
State law reference- Nonpayment of fees, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 22-27-5(e), 22-27-7. 
Sec. 17-15. - Private haulers. 
(a)	It shall be the duty and responsibility of the city and within its discretion to collect, remove and dispose of garbage as defined in this chapter in such manner and under such terms and conditions as may be determined expedient and as may now or hereafter be determined or fixed by ordinance. 
(b)	No person shall, for a fee, charge or commission, gather, haul or remove garbage from within the corporate limits of the city to any dump site, dumping area or garbage disposal area located outside of the corporate limits of the city. 
(Ord. No. 8-81, § 2, 7-27-81; Ord. No. 7-94, § 15, 4-11-94) 
Sec. 17-16. - Littering. 
    No person shall place or cause to be placed upon the public streets, sidewalks or alleys of the city any garbage, trash, refuse or like matter, except as provided in this chapter, and no person shall throw, place or dispose of any trash, litter, garbage, refuse or like matter upon the property of another. 
(Code 1979, § 7-7) 
Sec. 17-17. - Sweeping or throwing waste on street; allowing waste to be exposed to insects. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to sweep or throw trash, waste matter or other garbage or rubbish into the streets or alleys or on the sidewalks of the city or upon property not his own or under his control, and it shall be unlawful for any person to allow garbage, refuse or other waste matter to remain exposed to flies or other insects on his premises. 
(Code 1979, § 7-8) 
Sec. 17-18. - Penalty for violation of chapter. 
    Any person doing any act or thing declared by this chapter to be unlawful or any person failing to comply with the terms of this chapter shall be guilty of an offense against the city and, upon conviction, shall be punished by a fine of not less than two dollars ($2.00) nor more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) or by imprisonment or jail or by hard labor for no longer than six (6) months or by both fine and imprisonment, at the discretion of the court hearing the case. Each day any violation of this chapter continues shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 7-94, § 18, 4-11-94)

V, § 2; general improvements in subdivisions, App. B, art. VI, § 1. (Back)

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 18-1. - Adoption of standards for accommodating utilities. 
    The city council hereby formally adopts the state highway department standards for accommodating utilities on highway rights-of-way, and future amendments thereto, as standards for use by the city for accommodating utilities on roads and streets under the jurisdiction of the city on those roads and streets which involve the expenditure of state or federal highway funds. 
(Code 1979, § 13-1) 
Cross reference- Utilities, Ch. 20. 
Sec. 18-2. - Obstructing passage. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to stand, assemble, gather or loiter upon any street or sidewalk in the city so as to impede or obstruct the safe, convenient and free passage of persons or vehicles along the streets or sidewalks. It shall also be unlawful for any person to obstruct or encumber any street or sidewalk in the city so as to prevent or impede the safe, convenient and free passage of persons or vehicles along the streets or sidewalks. 
(Code 1979, § 13-2) 
Sec. 18-3. - Advertising from vehicle; use of loudspeakers or other noise-producing devices. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to advertise from any motor vehicle or other conveyance upon any street or avenue of the city, or to engage in any public speaking or preaching upon any avenue, street or sidewalk of the city by means of any loudspeaker, amplifier, radio, phonograph, phonograph record, bell, drum, horn or other instrument, or by any other loud noise. 
(Code 1979, § 13-3) 
Cross reference- Motor vehicles and traffic, Ch. 11. 
Sec. 18-4. - Exception to sections 18-2 and 18-3. 
(a)	The mayor may, by written permit, give to any person the right to advertise upon any street, avenue or sidewalk of the city or the right to engage in any public speaking or preaching on any of the avenues or streets or sidewalks of the city, and the right to stand, assemble, gather, encumber or impede any of the streets, avenues or sidewalks of the city. 
(b)	Subsection (a) of this section shall not apply to events described in Chapter 14 
(Code 1979, § 13-4) 
Secs. 18-5-18-12. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - DISPLAY OF STREET NUMBERS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 3-07, § 2, adopted February 12, 2007, did not specifically amend the Code, hence, inclusion as §§ 18-13-18-19 have been included at the discretion of the editor. 
Sec. 18-13. - Uniform system of numbering established. 
(a)	There is hereby established a uniform system of numbering buildings fronting on all streets, avenues and public ways in the city, and all houses and other buildings shall be numbered in accordance with the provisions of this article. Street names presently in use and street names now and hereafter designated on approved subdivision plats, all as shown by such uniform system, shall constitute official street names unless changed or re-designated by ordinance of the city. 
(Ord. No. 3-07, § 1, 2-12-07) 
Sec. 18-14. - Street address numbers and addressing standards. 
(a)	Addressing standards and guidelines as promulgated by the enhanced 911 system of the county and by the county addressing department, as the same may be amended or modified from time to time, subject to agreements with the City of Clanton, are hereby adopted by reference. 
(b)	All buildings, residences, mobile homes, or other fixed structures, within the corporate limits of the City of Clanton shall have address numerals/characters permanently and visibly displayed on the premises, on the mailbox post when said mailbox is located on the subject property, or on a free-standing post located at the driveway leading to the structure, so as to identify the location, subject to the following provisions: 
(1)	For the purposes of this section, an address for display is defined as the numerals and/or characters assigned in compliance with enhanced 911 and the county addressing department to a specific location. 
(2)	All numerals shall be Arabic numerals a minimum of three (3) inches high, made of durable and clearly visible material, of a contrasting color to the surface of the structure on which they are attached, or of durable reflective material. 
(3)	Address numerals shall be displayed where readily visible from the primary street or road on which the structure is addressed. Whenever any building is situated more than fifty (50) feet from the front property line, the number of such building shall be conspicuously displayed on the owner's property at the property line, near the walkway, driveway or entrance to such building, upon a gatepost, fence post or other appropriate place so as to be easily viewed from the street. 
(Ord. No. 3-07, § 2, 2-12-07) 
Sec. 18-15. - Compliance standards. 
(a)	New construction. Upon commencement of initial construction of a new structure, a clearly visible free-standing sign or post shall be erected and maintained in place until the permanent address numerals are attached or otherwise displayed upon the premises at completion. 
(b)	New structures. Permanent address numerals must be in place prior to receipt of a certificate of occupancy as issued by the appropriate authorities, subject to the following provisions: 
(1)	Single family residential structures and mobile homes must have the address displayed on the premises, on the mailbox post when said mailbox is located on the subject property, or on a free-standing post located at the driveway leading to the structure. 
(2)	Duplex structures must have the numeric address displayed as well as the suite or unit number. This may be displayed on the premises, on the mailbox post assigned to that unit when said mailbox is located on the subject property, or on a free-standing post located at the driveway leading to the unit so as to identify the location. 
(3)	Multi-family structures must have the numeric address of the site or of the individual building displayed on the premise and the apartment number shall be displayed on the door or near the entrance to each unit. 
(4)	Business structures must have the address displayed either on the building face or upon a post or free-standing sign situated at the driveway or entrance to the property when numbering on the structure is not readily visible from the street. A mailbox post may be used if the mailbox is situated near the street. In a business complex, each building shall have the numeric address displayed upon the building and suite or unit numbers displayed on the door or near the entrance to each unit. 
(c)	Existing structures. The resident or current occupant of any dwelling, the owner, manager, or occupant of any business structure, or the owner of any structure that is not occupied, is responsible for compliance with this section, and permanent addresses numerals shall be attached or otherwise displayed upon the structure or premises within ninety (90) days of the adoption of this article as described in the applicable section (b) (1), (2), (3), or (4) above. 
(Ord. No. 3-07, § 3, 2-12-07) 
Sec. 18-16. - Removal of numbers. 
    Numbers shall not be moved from one house to another and shall remain on the structure or location to which assigned unless changed by the authority of the county addressing department of the Enhanced 911 System of the county. 
(Ord. No. 3-07, § 4, 2-12-07) 
Sec. 18-17. - Compliance. 
    It shall be a violation of this article to fail to display the address as prescribed herein, or to display any address not officially assigned. 
(Ord. No. 3-07, § 5, 2-12-07) 
Sec. 18-18. - Notice of violation. 
    If the owner of any building required to be numbered by this article shall neglect for a period of twenty (20) days to duly attach and maintain the proper number of such building, the city shall serve upon him a notice requiring such owner to properly number the same and if he neglects to do so for ten (10) days after the service of such notice, he shall be deemed to have violated this article. 
(Ord. No. 3-07, § 6, 2-12-07) 
Sec. 18-19. - Enforcement. 
    Failure to comply with this article shall constitute a violation and may be prosecuted in the City of Clanton Municipal Court punishable by a fine not to exceed five hundred dollars ($500.00) and/or imprisonment not to exceed six (6) months. 
(Ord. No. 3-07, § 7, 2-12-07) 
Secs. 18-20-18-30. - Reserved.

Sec. 18-41. - Definitions.

(b)	It shall be lawful for retail or wholesale merchants operating with a business license within the city to display and offer for sale goods, wares or merchandise within the areas of the sidewalk adjacent to the retail or wholesale place of business of the merchant on four (4) Saturdays of each calendar year, with the Saturdays to be designated by the Downtown Merchants Association of the city.

(Code 1979, § 8-61)

Sec. 19-27. - Compensation for county tax assessor. 
    There is hereby fixed as compensation for the tax assessor of the county a sum equal to two (2) percent of the ad valorem taxes collected in each taxable year for compensation for levying ad valorem taxes for the city.
